1401 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Somers v. Stevens Point


No. 90-1823


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


165 Wis. 2d 511; 478 N.W.2d 595; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1501



November 27, 1991, Decided and Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Portage county: EDWARD F. ZAPPEN, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a town and certain town and city residents, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin) sustaining defendant city's direct annexation of acreage in the town and dismissing their complaint challenging the annexation.


OVERVIEW: The city directly annexed certain acreage in the town. The court affirmed the trial court's decision sustaining the annexation and dismissing the complaint. Direct annexation was authorized by Wis. Stat. § 66.021(2)(a). When announcing its findings of fact, the trial court applied the "rule of reason." Three parts of the rule of reason were: (1) exclusions and irregularities in boundary lines could not be the result of arbitrariness; (2) some reasonable present or demonstrable future need for the annexed property had to be shown; and (3) no other factors could exist which would constitute an abuse of discretion on the part of the municipality. The city had two purposes in annexing the land: first, to acquire undeveloped property which could be used for single family residences; second, since its municipal wells were adjacent to the annexed area, to protect its groundwater from future contamination. The city demonstrated a reasonable need for present and future development. A city could annex to expand its residential areas. Also, extension of municipal services to substantial numbers of residents in the annexed territory was a factor to be taken into account.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision sustaining the annexation and dismissing the complaint.

 

1402 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pernell


Nos. 91-0537-CR, 91-0538-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


165 Wis. 2d 651; 478 N.W.2d 297; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1461


October 1, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
November 26, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgments and an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Robert W. Landry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgments and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) to party to the crime of criminal trespass to dwelling, and party to the crime of criminal damage to property. He was subject to sentence enhancement for committing the misdemeanors while armed, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 939.63(1)(a), and to the habitual criminal statute, § 939.62. He appealed the order denying his motion to withdraw his guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his guilty plea was unconstitutional and that the trial court did not properly sentence him. The court affirmed and held that the sentencing court did exactly as Wis. Stat. § 971.08(1)(b) required. The trial court explained why it sentenced defendant as it did and defendant was affirmatively advised by the trial court that the total misdemeanor sentence depended on how the trial court ruled on the habitual criminality statute. Further, the court held that the record showed that, before the court accepted the guilty plea and sentenced defendant, he understood the happenings and the court's reasoning. The court also held that the penalty enhancer statutes were applied properly and the misdemeanor crimes remained misdemeanors even if the maximum penalty was increased because defendant was armed while committing the crime. The court notes that the added fact of being armed while committing a misdemeanor was not only a necessary condition for sentence enhancement but was also an element of the crime charged. Further, the court held that the plain language of the repeater statute did not divide its application into misdemeanors and felonies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

 

1403 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Page v. Grantsburg Volunteer Fire Dep't


Nos. 90-2902, 91-0621


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


165 Wis. 2d 512; 478 N.W.2d 595; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1488



November 19, 1991, Decided and Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the circuit court for St. Croix county: C.A. RICHARDS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff widow appealed two orders that were consolidated for appeal from the circuit court for St. Croix County (Wisconsin), which entered judgments in favor of defendants, a fire association (GFA) and a fire department (GVFD), in two wrongful death actions brought by the widow to recover for the death of her husband, caused by a collision between the husband's motorcycle and a municipally-owned vehicle driven by an association employee.


OVERVIEW: The widow brought the first lawsuit against the GFA and its insurer. That suit resulted in a payment of $ 250,000 to the widow by the GFA to satisfy the limit of liability imposed on the GFA pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 345.05(3). The widow challenged the constitutionality of the cap on liability. The trial court rejected the widow's arguments and found the limit to be constitutional. The trial court also denied the widow's motion to recover a second $ 250,000 limit from the GVFD, ruling that the GFA and the GVFD constituted only one agency, and, therefore, limited the widow to a single $ 250,000 limit under Wis. Stat. § 893.80(3). The widow initiated a second lawsuit against the GVFD, which was dismissed. The widow appealed the judgments, and they were consolidated. The court affirmed and held that the statutory limit on damages was not constitutionally infirm, that the mere continuation of an insurance policy in excess of the statutory limit of liability did not constitute a waiver of the right to rely on the statutory limit and that the GVFD was merely a subdivision of the GFA, and, therefore, the widow was entitled to only one recovery under § 893.80(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the capped judgment in favor of the widow and against the GFD and affirmed the dismissal of the widow's action against the GVFD.

 

1404 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Heritage Federal Credit Union v. Wis. Credit Union Sav. Ins. Corp.


No. 90-0388


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


165 Wis. 2d 511; 478 N.W.2d 595; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1457



November 14, 1991, Decided and Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: MICHAEL B. TORPHY, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff credit unions appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted defendant corporation's motion for summary judgment dismissing the credit unions' complaint seeking a declaration that Wis. Stat. § 186.35 was unconstitutional in precluding them from participating equally with other corporation members in the distribution of the corporation's assets on liquidation.


OVERVIEW: The credit unions were members of the corporation, which was a state created deposit insurer that went into liquidation, and sought to participate along with other member credit unions in the corporation's mandated distribution of assets to members operating under Wis. Stat. ch. 186. The credit unions filed a complaint seeking a declaratory judgment that they were entitled to participate in the distribution under Wis. Stat. § 186.35(11) or, in the alternative, for a declaratory judgment ruling that the statute was unconstitutional in precluding them from participating on an equal basis with other members of the corporation. The trial court granted the corporation's motion for summary judgment and the credit unions appealed. The court reversed the judgment, holding that the credit unions were members but not operating under ch. 186. The court concluded that the corporation offered no reasonable rationale for the distinction between members operating under the statute and members not so operating, and as a result, the credit unions were entitled to participate and to a declaratory judgment that § 186.35(11) denied them equal protection of the laws.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court granting the corporation's motion of summary judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

1405 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grayson


No. 91-0756-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


165 Wis. 2d 557; 478 N.W.2d 390; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1442


August 27, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
November 12, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Marathon County: Vincent K. Howard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin) on four felony counts of failing to pay child support for the calendar years 1986 through 1989 pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 940.27(2) (1987), and a post-conviction order upholding his conviction.


OVERVIEW: The court accepted defendant's pleas of no contest, found him guilty and sentenced him to four consecutive two-year terms of imprisonment and ordered restitution. Defendant's post-conviction motion challenged the conviction and restitution order on the grounds, inter alia, multiplicity. Defendant argued that Wis. Stat. § 940.27(2) (1987) contemplated only a single non-support charge for a violation of its terms, and the State could not prosecute multiple counts under § 940.27(2). The court affirmed, holding, inter alia, that multiple charging under the felony non-support statute met the requirement of the "additional fact" test, which examined whether each count required proof of an additional fact which the other count or counts did not. The State was required to prove that defendant formed a separate intent to violate the order that formed the basis for each individual charge, as well as a different 120-day time frame. Further, the court held that the legislature intended to allow for multiple prosecutions under the nonsupport statute.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed.

 

1406 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Egg Harbor v. Sarkis


No. 91-0254


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


166 Wis. 2d 5; 479 N.W.2d 536; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1591


October 10, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
November 12, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Door county: S. Dean Pies, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed. No costs to either party.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Door County (Wisconsin), which upheld an assessment by respondent village related to the owner's remodeling of an existing structure into a pub and restaurant. The village cross-appealed that portion of the judgment striking down the provision of the ordinance allowing interest to be calculated on the new assessment from the date of the enactment of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The property owner remodeled his commercial property into a pub and restaurant. The village assessed additional residential equivalent units (REU) and increased the owner's contributions to the cost of the sewage system. The trial court found that the reassessment was proper under a village ordinance and held that the ordinance was constitutional. However, the trial court set aside that portion of the ordinance that permitted the village to assess interest on the additional REU's calculated from the date of the enactment of the ordinance to the date of the assessment. On appeal, the owner argued that the ordinance under which the assessment was made was inapplicable to him and that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The court rejected these arguments and affirmed the assessment. The court held that the owner benefitted from the improved sewer system and the assessment was reasonable. The court also concluded that the trial court properly determined that the interest provision of the ordinance was unreasonable under Wis. Stat. § 66.60(1)(b). The court declined to reach the question of the constitutionality of the interest portion of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1407 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re S.A.


No. 91-0565


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


165 Wis. 2d 530; 478 N.W.2d 21; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1443


September 27, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
November 6, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County: Stephen A. Simanek, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Racine Family Court Commissioner appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) in which the trial court interpreted Wis. Stat. § 767.329 to mandate that the trial court approve a stipulated post-judgment custody transfer without inquiring into the best interests of the child. Respondents were the unmarried parents of the child in question.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a stipulation between the parents, the father moved the trial court to modify an earlier judgment and transfer custody and primary physical placement of the child to the father. The trial court granted this request and ordered the previous judgment to be amended to reflect the parents' stipulation. Subsequently, the commissioner appealed from an order in which the trial court interpreted Wis. Stat. § 767.329 to mandate that the trial court approve a stipulated post-judgment custody transfer without inquiring into the best interests of the child. The central issue on appeal involved the interpretation of § 767.329. The court concluded that § 767.329 did not mandate court approval of a stipulated post-judgment custody transfer without examining the best interests of the child. The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The court reasoned that the consequences would be absurd if § 767.329 were read to prohibit an examination of the best interests of the child.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the cause to the trial court to address the commissioner's motion to intervene and the commissioner's challenge as to whether the parents' stipulation served the best interests of the child.

 

1408 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Walworth County v. Tronshaw


No. 91-0525


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


165 Wis. 2d 521; 478 N.W.2d 294; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1517


October 22, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
November 6, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Walworth County: James L. Carlson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which found that the property owner violated an ordinance passed by plaintiff county placing a height limitation on fences on residentially zoned property.


OVERVIEW: The county sued the property owner for violating an ordinance restricting the height of fences to four feet. The property owner took the fence down and cut two feet off the six foot boards. He then built a berm on the original fence line and put the fence back. The total height from the street level to the top of the fence boards was over four feet. The county continued to object. The circuit court ordered the property owner to remove the fence or pay the county for its removal. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally overbroad or vague. The court held that the word fence was to be defined as a nontechnical word and given its ordinary and accepted meaning. The reasonable person was on notice that the standard for measuring structures, such as a fence, is found under "building height," determined by measuring from the mean elevation of the finished lot grade along the street yard face of the structure. Therefore, the ordinance was neither unconstitutionally vague or overbroad because it prohibited enclosures from exceeding the building height.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court, which held that the ordinance restricting the height of fences to four feet was valid.

 

1409 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Ahmad v. Milwaukee


No. 91-0533


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


165 Wis. 2d 512; 478 N.W.2d 596; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1427



November 5, 1991, Decided and Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5. STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MICHAEL D. GUOLEE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, previous store owners and new store owners (retailers), challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment to respondent City of Milwaukee (Wisconsin) in the action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and Wis. Stat. §§ 133.03, 134.01 in which appellants alleged that denying a liquor license application violated their due process rights and was a conspiracy to injure and to restrain trade.


OVERVIEW: The retailers alleged that the refusal to renew one liquor license and the denial of an application for another violated due process rights and constituted a conspiracy to restrain trade and to wilfully or maliciously injure trade. The grant of the motion for summary judgment was based on findings that there were no material issues of fact, neither retailer had liberty or property interests that were protectable under due process or equal protection arguments, and they could not sue the City for conspiracy damages. The court affirmed, concluding that the retailers were not entitled to relief. Res judicata barred the claims of one retailer, the other retailer's predecessor, because the issues could have been tried and litigated in the earlier action as to the denial of its request to renew its liquor license. The court held that a liquor license was a privilege and that terming it a right violated public policy. The court determined that the presumption that the denial of the successor retailer's application was not arbitrary and unreasonable, and the conspiracy claims failed because the City could not have been held liable for the intentional torts of its officers or agents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

NAWROCKI v. CITY OF MILWAUKEE FIRE & POLICE COMMN.


No. 91-0024


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


165 Wis. 2d 393; 478 N.W.2d 67; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1371



October 22, 1991, Decided and Released  
October 22, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: PATRICIA S. CURLEY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former police officer sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which sustained the decision from respondent City of Milwaukee Fire & Police Commission approving the former officer's discharge from the City of Milwaukee Police Department.


OVERVIEW: The former officer entered into an agreement of disposition whereby a criminal complaint against him was amended to one requiring civil forfeitures. The former officer entered a no contest plea and was convicted on charges of unfair residential practices and paid a fine. The chief of police dismissed the former officer for failure to obey the laws and ordinances of the City of Milwaukee under Milwaukee, Wis., Rules and Regulations of the Milwaukee Police Department R. 4. The Commission sustained the former officer's dismissal. The trial court affirmed the Commission's decision. In affirming on appeal, the court held that: (1) where R. 4 was an effective warning that allowed the former officer a reasonable opportunity to avoid conduct that would subject him to sanction and was consistently applied, it was not unconstitutionally vague or discriminatory; (2) the trial court lacked jurisdiction to consider the former officer's claim under the Wisconsin Fair Employment Act, Wis. Stat. §§ 111.31-.395, where he failed to pursue administrative remedies; and (3) it was appropriate to use the former officer's plea of "no contest" as the basis for administrative discipline.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the trial court, which sustained the Commission's approval of the former officer's discharge from the police department.

 

1411 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. SIEGER


No. 91-0807-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


165 Wis. 2d 394; 478 N.W.2d 68; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1344



October 16, 1991, Decided and Released  
October 16, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Oconto county: PHILIP M. KIRK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Oconto County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of first-degree intentional homicide, party to the crime, denied his motion for postconviction relief, sentenced him to life imprisonment, and set his parole eligibility date.


OVERVIEW: Defendant informed a friend about a plan to rip off his step-uncle. Defendant admitted that he suggested they kill his step-uncle, but claims he never seriously discussed it. As defendant and his friend were driving toward the cabin, when asked what they would do if the step-uncle were present, the friend replied that he would kill him. As defendant waited out of sight, the friend went up to the cabin. Defendant heard numerous gunshots. The friend killed the step-uncle. Defendant and the friend then rummaged through the cabin. There was no dispute that defendant intentionally aided and abetted and conspired to commit an armed burglary of the uncle's cabin. Defendant was convicted of first-degree intentional homicide, party to the crime, his motion for postconviction relief was denied, he was sentenced to life imprisonment, and his parole eligibility date was set by the trial court. On review, the court affirmed. The court held that a jury instruction on the lesser-included offense of reckless homicide and felony murder was not necessary where it was proven that the first-degree intentional homicide was a natural and probable consequence of the intended armed burglary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, the denial of his postconviction relief, and the setting of his parole eligibility date.

 

1412 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Freedom from Religion Foundation, Inc. v. Thompson


No. 90-2083


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


164 Wis. 2d 736; 476 N.W.2d 318; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1307


April 4, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
September 26, 1991, Decided  
September 26, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Robert R. Pekowsky, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state officials sought relief from a decision by the Circuit Court, Dane County (Wisconsin) granting respondent religious foundation judgment on the pleadings and finding that Wis. Stat. § 20.505(1)(fm) (1989) unconstitutionally violated the First Amendment and the Wis. Const. art. I, § 18 in providing a grant to one specific religiously affiliated educational institution for the planning of an international center.


OVERVIEW: The state officials sought relief from the trial court's decision. The court reversed and remanded. It found that the religious foundation brought an action seeking declaratory relief on its allegations and seeking a temporary restraining order enjoining the state officials from delivering the grant. Thus, the court noted its dismay about the trial court's reasons for issuing a final judgment when neither party filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings. However, the court found that the statutory governmental aid did not offend the state and federal constitutions if the statute had a secular legislative purpose, its principal effect neither advanced nor inhibited religion, and it did not foster an excessive government entanglement with religion. Based on this test, the court found that the complaint raised an inference that the grant had a sectarian purpose, raised questions of fact concerning the grant's primary effect, and was sufficient to state claims. Then, the state officials' responses raised genuine issues of disputed fact. Thus, the trial court erred in granting judgment on the pleadings and finding the statute unconstitutionally invalid on its face.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision granting judgment on the pleadings for the religious foundation and remanded with instructions.

 

1413 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bruette


No. 91-0278-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


164 Wis. 2d 752; 477 N.W.2d 364; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1288



September 24, 1991  
September 24, 1991, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Shawano county: Earl W. Schmidt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction as an habitual criminal from the Circuit Court for Shawano County (Wisconsin) following his conviction for disorderly conduct and his sentence on grounds that it inflicted cruel and unusual punishment in violation of U.S. Const. amend VIII. He argued that the trial court ignored the lesser misdemeanor status of the crime of disorderly conduct by imposing the maximum sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted to six prior convictions and did not contest his status as an habitual criminal. His prior offenses included armed burglary and endangering safety by conduct regardless of life, for which he received a four-year prison term, battery, obstructing an officer, a federal robbery conviction with a prison sentence, and another disorderly conduct conviction as a repeater with a prison sentence. The district attorney advised the trial court that the present offense had occurred within 48 hours of defendant's last release. Evidence and witness testimony showed that, after giving a usual and friendly greeting to defendant, the victim was assaulted. The jury apparently disbelieved defendant's testimony that he intervened in a dispute to aid his brother. The trial court held that defendant's aggressive nature mandated the sentence imposed. The court agreed, holding that the trial court's reasoning was correct, given the gravity of the offense, other sentences imposed on other offenders, and similar sentences in other jurisdictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and his sentence.

 

1414 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re City of Superior


No. 91-0375


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


164 Wis. 2d 718; 476 N.W.2d 611; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1263


August 12, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
September 24, 1991, Decided  
September 24, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Douglas County: Joseph A. McDonald, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners of condemned land challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Douglas County (Wisconsin) that upheld the payment of the interest that accrued on the compensation award while held in the trial court's depository into appellee county's general fund pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 59.42(2).


OVERVIEW: The owners claimed that paying the accrued interest to the county constituted a taking without compensation and that § 59.42(2) was unconstitutional. The court rejected both claims and affirmed the judgment. The court's review of the legislative history supported the conclusion that the reference to "any funds" in § 59.42(2) meant exactly that and included the interest that accumulated on the compensation award. Section 59.42(2) did not violate either Wis. Const. art. I, § 13 or U.S. Const. amend. V, which prohibited taking private property for public use without just compensation. The court reasoned that the owners' reliance upon a United States Supreme Court decision that held another state's statute unconstitutional because it required the depositing of funds with the state court and authorized both a fee for the clerk's services and payment of interest accrued on funds deposited with a state court, was misplaced because Wis. Stat. § 59.42(2) did not impose both a service fee and retention of interest. More importantly, the owners pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 32.06(11) had a right to withdraw the funds from the trial court and invest them as they saw fit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that upheld the payment of the interest that accrued on the owners' compensation award into the county's general fund.

 

1415 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


MASTER v. EISENBART


No. 90-2897


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


164 Wis. 2d 751; 477 N.W.2d 364; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1270



September 18, 1991 
September 18, 1991, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Racine county: Stephen A. Simanek, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed, but cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent-appellant father sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which issued a two-year domestic abuse injunction under Wis. Stat. § 813.12. The injunction prevented the father from having contact with petitioner-respondent mother. The father asserted that § 813.12 was unconstitutional and that the mother's petition lacked the necessary elements for an injunction under that statute.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 813.12, the trial court issued an injunction against a father accused of having abused a mother. The court affirmed the trial court's decision, found that the father's appeal was frivolous, and remanded for costs, fees, and reasonable attorney's fees under Wis. Stat. §§ 809.25(3)a, 809.25(3)(c)2. Although the father asserted that § 813.12 was unconstitutional, the court found that the statute was constitutional under principles of equal protection and due process pursuant to the Fourteenth Amendment. Further, the court noted that injury to reputation was not constitutionally protected because reputation was not liberty or property within the meaning of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court found that the trial court had acted within its discretion when it granted the father's motion for an adjournment and that the trial court had the authority to grant an injunction under Wis. Stat. § 813.12(4)(a). Similarly, the court found that the trial court acted within its discretion in the manner in which it conducted the judicial proceeding. The court found that the father's assertion that he was deprived of his right to a trial by jury lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision and concluded that the appeal was frivolous. The court remanded the matter for a determination of costs, fees, and reasonable attorney's fees.

 

1416 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baker


Nos. 90-2633-CR, 90-2634-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


165 Wis. 2d 42; 477 N.W.2d 292; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1384


July 30, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
September 17, 1991, Decided  
September 17, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted. Petition to cross-review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Brown County: Carl R. Fenwick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a portion of an order from the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which prevented the use of defendant's third operating after revocation (OAR) conviction as a prior conviction under Wis. Stat. § 343.44(2). Defendant cross-appealed that portion of the order permitting the use of his second OAR conviction as a prior conviction under § 343.44(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with his fifth OAR offense and one month later, he was charged again with a fifth offense OAR. Both fifth offense OAR charges were based on his four prior OAR convictions. The charges were consolidated for trial and disposition. The trial court allowed defendant to collaterally attack two of his four prior OAR convictions and issued an order declaring the third OAR void for sentencing purposes and declaring the second OAR conviction valid. On appeal by both parties, the court affirmed. Defendant was properly allowed to collaterally attack prior OAR convictions that were being used for enhancement purposes on constitutional grounds. Defendant's third OAR was not constitutionally obtained because the record was not only silent as to whether his plea was made voluntarily and intelligently, but it also indicated that he was not even present at the proceedings. Defendant failed to meet his burden of proving that his second OAR conviction was unconstitutionally obtained where his only supporting evidence that he did not waive his right to counsel was his conclusory affidavit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

M.I. v. State


No. 90-2749-NM


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


164 Wis. 2d 751; 477 N.W.2d 364; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1245

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Michael G. Malmstadt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) granting the State of Wisconsin's petition to terminate the mother's parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a petition to terminate the mother's parental rights to her four minor children. The State contended that the mother was unfit because her children were in continuing need of protective services and she suffered from continuing parental disability due to her mental disorders. The trial court granted the State's petition. In affirming the decision, the court found that the mother's interests were protected by counsel and her guardian ad litem. The admission of the testimony regarding the mother's medical records constituted harmless error because two doctors testified regarding their independent examinations of the mother and concluded that she suffered from a mental illness. There was overwhelming evidence to support the jury's findings based upon testimonies from a social worker, numerous doctors, and the minors' foster parents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

Hillman v. Columbia County


No. 90-0469


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


164 Wis. 2d 376; 474 N.W.2d 913; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1203; 12 A.L.R.5th 997


December 13, 1990, Oral argument  
August 29, 1991, Decided  
August 29, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review filed.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Columbia County: David C. Willis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment to defendant county and jail employees in his action violation of his right to confidentiality of an HIV test result, invasion of privacy, public disclosure of private facts, negligent and intentional infliction of emotional distress, and violation of his constitutional right to privacy under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's HIV test results were common knowledge at the jail. On review, the court found that: (1) the jail employees were not liable under Wis. Stat. § 146.025 as they did not conduct the HIV test and were not the authorized recipients of the results; (2) a medical records file was not a place within the geographical sense intended by the language of Wis. Stat. § 895.50(2)(a); (3) the oral communication among numerous employees and inmates at the jail was sufficient for "publicity" under Wis. Stat. § 895.50(2)(c); (4) the inmate failed to allege a physical injury for negligent infliction of emotional distress and failed to allege a disability as a result of his severe mental distress for intentional infliction of emotional distress; (5) the inmate stated a constitutional claim for violation of privacy as the jail employees were acting under the color of state law; (6) the dissemination of the inmate's HIV test results was outside the scope of their official duties so they were not entitled to immunity under 893.80(4) or qualified immunity; and (7) the inmate did not establish the county was deliberately indifferent to his rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for the county and the jail employees on the inmate's claims for violation of his right to confidentiality of an HIV test result, invasion of privacy, and negligent and intentional infliction of emotional distress. The court reversed and remanded summary judgment for the jail employees on the inmate's claims for public disclosure of private facts and violation of his constitutional right to privacy.

 

1419 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hermann


No. 90-2252-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


164 Wis. 2d 269; 474 N.W.2d 906; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1174


May 14, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
August 14, 1991, Decided  
August 14, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County: Thomas S. Williams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of delivery of a controlled substance and delivery of a controlled substance, party to a crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that he merited resentencing for several reasons. The court found that the penalty enhancer provisions of Wis. Stat. § 161.49 (1987-88), in effect when the offenses were committed, did not contain an express scienter requirement. Based on a review of the legislative history of § 161.49 and 21 U.S.C.S. § 845a, both of which provided for an enhanced penalty for distribution of controlled substances within 1,000 feet of a school, the court held that the legislature did not intend to require proof of scienter in order to invoke the more severe penalty. The court concluded that it was not cruel and unusual punishment to require a three-year mandatory minimum sentence for one found guilty of knowingly engaging in an illegal drug sale in a statutorily protected zone. The court also held that § 161.49 did not violate defendant's constitutional right to equal protection. The legislative classification in the statute was rationally related to the deterrence of illegal drug transactions near schools, and seeking to eliminate such an atmosphere near schools by more harshly penalizing those who contributed to it was not patently arbitrary or irrational.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against defendant.

1422 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Goeltzer v. First Wisconsin Nat'l Bank


No. 90-1374


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


163 Wis. 2d 1091; 474 N.W.2d 528; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1031



July 23, 1991  
July 23, 1991, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Marquette county; Donn H. Dahlke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action that involved respondent bank, appellant, a beneficiary under a later will, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Marquette County (Wisconsin), which held that a testatrix was bound to a joint will's terms, laches barred respondents, the testatrix's brother and a hospital, from receiving anything, the joint will disposed of after-acquired property, and gifts to respondent beneficiaries who had died did not lapse.


OVERVIEW: The testatrix and her husband executed the joint will as a single document. The joint will gave all of their property to the survivor. Upon the death of the survivor, the joint will gave the remaining property to designated beneficiaries. The husband died first. The testatrix executed a later will. The testatrix died. The bank was named the personal representative pursuant to the later will. The bank discovered the joint will and petitioned the court to determine the testatrix's true beneficiaries. Two of the named beneficiaries under the joint will, the testatrix's brother and the hospital, declined to participate in the proceedings. The court affirmed the finding that the joint will was contractual. The court reversed the trial court's ruling that the testatrix's brother and the hospital were barred by laches from recovering under the joint will because prejudice was not shown. The trial court had correctly found that after the husband's death, the gifts to the beneficiaries who had died after the husband had died had vested. After-acquired property was included in the joint will pursuant to the common law and Wis. Stat. § 238.03 (1969).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's rulings that the joint will was contractual, that it disposed of after-acquired property, and that no lapse occurred. The court reversed the ruling the denied a legacy to the testatrix's brother and to the hospital. The matter was remanded.

State ex rel. N/S Assoc. v. Board of Review


No. 90-2546


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


164 Wis. 2d 31; 473 N.W.2d 554; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1012


April 2, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
July 23, 1991, Decided  
July 23, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: William J. Haese, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner appealed, by writ of certiorari, a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a tax assessment of a shopping mall owned by the property owner. The original tax assessment was made by respondent board of review.


OVERVIEW: The valuation of the property owner's shopping mall increased substantially over a two year period. The increased assessment was triggered by the sale of the mall to the property owner during that time. The property owner contended that the board of review incorrectly assessed the value of the shopping mall. The court held that real property valuation had to be based on the fair market value of the property which was the amount the property would sell for upon arms-length negotiation in the open market between an owner willing, but not obliged to sell, and a buyer willing, but not obliged to buy. The court found that the sale of the shopping mall was an arm's length transaction and that the assessment was made in accordance with Wis. Stat. § 70.32(1) and the Wisconsin Property Assessment Manual. The court further held that the assessment had to be upheld because the board of review did not exceed its jurisdiction, it acted according to law, its decision was neither arbitrary, oppressive or unreasonable, and the evidence before the board of review was such that it could reasonably sustain the assessment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment upholding the valuation of the property owner's shopping mall by the board of review.

State v. Clemens


No. 90-2150


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


163 Wis. 2d 1092; 474 N.W.2d 528; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1083

July 18, 1991, Released

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for La Crosse county: John J. Perlich, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which revoked defendant's driver's license and denied his request for a free transcript.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's driver's license was revoked by the trial court. Defendant appealed that judgment and an order which denied his request for a free transcript, contending, among other things, that the officer who arrested him lacked probable cause to believe he was operating a motor vehicle under the influence of alcohol and that he was represented by ineffective trial counsel. The court held that because defendant did not file a copy of the trial transcript, it was compelled to accept the trial court's conclusion that the evidence was sufficient to find that the arresting officer had probable cause to arrest defendant. Further, a claim of inadequate trial counsel had to be raised by a hearing in the trial court, at which trial counsel could testify concerning the reasons behind the actions taken. Therefore, if defendant wished to pursue such a claim, he had to raise the issue by motion to the trial court pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06. Defendant's conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment revoking defendant's driver's license and the order denying his request for a free transcript were affirmed.

 

1425 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


No. 90-2654


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


163 Wis. 2d 1093; 474 N.W.2d 529; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1071



July 2, 1991  
July 2, 1991, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Michael J. Skwierawski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), denying his motion for post-conviction relief and modification of sentence under Wis. Stat. § 974.06. Defendant claimed that his attorney rendered ineffective assistance of counsel, that the trial court erroneously admitted evidence seized pursuant to his illegal arrest and that the trial court erroneously denied his motion for sentence modification.


OVERVIEW: The court found that it could not review defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel because defendant did not allege to the trial court that his attorney was ineffective. Thus, there was no trial court record on the issue. Additionally, the record demonstrated that defendant did not make any objection before or during the trial to his arrest or to the admission of the seized evidence. Where defendant failed to make an objection required to be raised before trial under Wis. Stat. § 971.31(2), that failure precluded defendant from obtaining appellate review as a matter of right. Thus, defendant waived any appellate challenge to the legality of his arrest or the admission of evidence seized pursuant to the unchallenged arrest. Finally, the trial court's denial of defendant's request for sentence modification was correct. Wis. Stat. § 974.06 did not authorize sentence modification unless the sentence was constitutionally or jurisdictionally defective. No such error was alleged or demonstrated by defendant's motion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Larkin v. Abrahamson


No. 90-1484


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


163 Wis. 2d 965; 473 N.W.2d 609; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 991



June 13, 1991  
June 13, 1991, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane county; Jack Aulik, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) denying the inmate's motion for summary judgment and granting summary judgment to respondent prison officials and employees in the inmate's complaint seeking monetary and injunctive relief under 42 U.S.C.S.§ 1983 and state law due to respondents' refusal to permit him to retain, or to store for him, personal items brought into the prison upon admission.


OVERVIEW: The inmate unsuccessfully claimed that respondents disposed of a mailed typewriter without due process and disposed of his personal effects in retaliation for his refusal to voluntarily do so himself and for his filing of inmate complaints challenging their actions. The court held that given the plain violation of the prison mailing rule, the respondents were not required to provide defendant with a hearing before returning the prohibited typewriter to its sender. The inmate complaint system used to challenge respondents' actions provided a meaningful post-deprivation remedy for the loss and satisfied procedural due process requirements. The property interest involved was insubstantial as the inmate was simply denied possession of his property while incarcerated. Balancing the government's substantial interest in limiting the risks to security and in minimizing administrative and fiscal burdens, defendant received all the process that was due him. The decision to send the prohibited property to defendant's parents was a discretionary under Wis. Adm. Code § DOC 303.10(3)(d) and respondents, as public officials, were immune from suit for actions undertaken to implement it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying the inmate's motion for summary judgment and granting respondents' motion for summary judgment.

Milwaukee Bd. of School Directors v. Wisconsin Employment Relations Com.


No. 90-2333


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


163 Wis. 2d 739; 472 N.W.2d 553; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 931


April 2, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
June 11, 1991, Decided  
June 11, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: William J. Shaughnessy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Wisconsin Employment Relations Commission (WERC) and a teachers union, challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which overturned WERC's ruling that a race-conscious layoff provision in a collective bargaining agreement between the teachers union and respondent school district was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The layoff provision stated that layoffs would be based on inverse order of seniority provided that the racial balance of schools was not disturbed. The teachers union alleged that this violated the constitutional rights of certain teachers and sought a declaratory ruling from WERC pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 111.70(4)(b). WERC agreed that the provision was a prohibited and illegal subject of collective bargaining. The circuit court overturned WERC's decision, holding that the dispute was not ripe and that WERC usurped the judicial function by declaring the provision to be unconstitutional. The court rejected the circuit court's ruling as based on erroneous facts and ordered the reinstatement of WERC's decision. The matter was ripe because layoffs had been conducted under the disputed provision and there was proof of actual injury. WERC did not usurp the judicial function by invalidating the provision. Instead, it was fulfilling its mandate under Wis. Stat. § 111.70(4)(b). WERC had the authority to determine if a provision was a prohibited subject of bargaining. If a provision was unconstitutional, then it necessarily was a prohibited subject of bargaining.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment and reinstated WERC's determination that the layoff provision was unconstitutional.

State v. Mitchell


No. 90-2474-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


163 Wis. 2d 652; 473 N.W.2d 1; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 906


April 29, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
June 5, 1991, Decided  
June 5, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgments and an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County: Jerold W. Breitenbach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgments and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgments and an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of aggravated battery, party to a crime, and subjected him to the hate crime penalty enhancement under Wis. Stat. § 939.645.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a group of young black people had been discussing the movie "Mississippi Burning" when defendant provoked the group to attack a white boy. During the incident, one of the attackers took the victim's shoes. The jury found that defendant acted against the victim because of the victim's race. On appeal, defendant attacked the constitutionality of § 939.645 by claiming that it punished activities protected by the First Amendment. Affirming, the court held that "intentionally selects" and "race" as used int § 939.645 were clearly understood by an ordinary person to mean purposely pick out a victim because of his race; therefore, the statute was not vague. The court found that the statute was directed at the action of selecting the victim and not at speech. The words used by defendant were merely circumstantial evidence that defendant specially selected the victim because of race. The court also found that the resultant beating and theft were probable consequences of defendant's incitement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for St. Croix County (Wisconsin), which waived juvenile jurisdiction under Wis. Stat. § 48.18 after defendant was charged with second-degree reckless homicide.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the circuit court erred in concluding that extended juvenile jurisdiction was not available in the action and that it had abused its discretion by waiving defendant into adult court. Defendant also charged that the classification of certain crimes given extended juvenile jurisdiction under Wis. Stat. § 48.366 violated the Equal Protection Clause. The court determined that the classifications were to be sustained because there were rational reasons to support such classifications. The court held that the decision whether to waive juvenile jurisdiction lied within the sound discretion of the juvenile court. The court found that inasmuch as the circuit court had kept the best interests of the child in mind when deciding to waive jurisdiction, it had not abused its discretion.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Mlynczak v. Board of Fire & Police Comm'rs


No. 90-1868-FT


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


163 Wis. 2d 965; 473 N.W.2d 609; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 942



June 4, 1991  
June 4, 1991, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Gary A. Gerlach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dispatcher sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) denying the dispatcher's request to amend his pleadings to include a petition for certiorari review and upholding a decision by defendant Board of Fire and Police Commissioners for the City of Milwaukee (Wisconsin) dismissing the dispatcher from his position.


OVERVIEW: While at his job the dispatcher appeared intoxicated. After making a dispatching error, he was relieved of his duties and ordered to submit to a urinalysis. The Department found the dispatcher guilty of violating Milwaukee, Wis., Fire Department R. 27.2, items 2, 13. The Board dismissed the intoxication charge for insufficient evidence and affirmed the other finding. The trial court did not misapply the law and did not abuse its discretion when it denied him permission to amend his pleadings to include certiorari review. It was undisputed that the dispatcher sought certiorari review more than six months after the Board's decision. The dispatcher argued, however, that prejudice must have been established for the doctrine of laches to be asserted. The court held that there was no need for prejudice to have been shown for the doctrine of laches to apply. The dispatcher's original pleading did not reference any facts or allegations that would have constituted sufficient grounds for certiorari review. His request for certiorari review came more than six months after the decision of which he sought to review. He was guilty of laches and was not entitled to amend his pleadings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court denying the dispatcher's request to amend his pleadings to include a petition for certiorari review and upholding the Board's decision dismissing the dispatcher.

May 20, 1991, Oral argument  
June 4, 1991, Decided  
June 4, 1991, Released

PRIOR HISTORY: Supervisory Writ to the Circuit Court for Racine County: Gerald P. Ptacek, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, defendant and the law firm retained by defendant, sought a supervisory writ to require the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) to pay for the law firm's representation of defendant in a homicide case and to provide funds so that defendant could retain expert witnesses on his behalf and finally, to prevent respondent judge from continuing to preside over the case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant retained the law firm to represent him in a homicide case. When he was unable to provide the additional compensation that he owed to the law firm, defendant and the law firm petitioned the trial court for payment of attorney fees and compensation for expert witnesses. The trial court denied the request. Defendant and the law firm sought a supervisory writ to order the trial court to provide the fees and for removal of the trial judge, contending that he had a personal interest in the outcome. The court denied the writ, ruling that it was within the trial court's discretion to provide funds and expert witnesses to defendant and he did not make the necessary showing of a particularized need. Rather, it appeared that the request for funding was made because the law firm did not want to accept the reduced fee rate that was available through the state public defender if the law firm was appointed through the state public defender. The court concluded that the trial judge's remarks did not require his removal because they were no more than comments that the taxpayers should not have to pay for defendant's trial when the law firm had already received a significant retainer.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant and the law firm's petition for a supervisory writ to order the trial court to pay for defendant's representation by the law firm and to provide fund for expert witnesses and to remove the trial judge from defendant's homicide case.

Elfelt v. Cooper


No. 90-1326


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


163 Wis. 2d 484; 471 N.W.2d 303; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 836


March 15, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
May 29, 1991, Decided  
May 29, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County: Clair Voss, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant joint tenant (tenant) challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment in favor of respondent grantees in an action by the grantees for rent and partition of property after the IRS levied upon and sold the tenant's husband's equal interest to satisfy his income tax arrears. The grantees cross-appealed denial of their request for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The grantees obtained title to one-half of an undivided interest in the joint tenant's home after the IRS levied upon and sold the interest to satisfy income tax arrears. The joint tenant (tenant) argued on appeal that because the IRS lacked the legal authority to sell the interest in the homestead that she shared with her husband, the grantees did not have good title and could not receive rent or partition. The grantees appealed denial of a request for attorney fees based on the alleged frivolous refusal of the tenant to admit certain facts. The court affirmed judgment for the grantees for rent and partition. The court held that the husband's interest in the home was a "right to property" under Wisconsin law and the federal tax consequences of I.R.C. § 6331 applied. The homestead could be seized despite the affect on the tenant's interest. The sale severed the joint tenancy and created a tenancy in common, entitling the grantees to rent and partition. The court held that the tenant's appeal was not frivolous. The court remanded for a determination of whether the tenant had reasonable grounds to deny requests for admission and whether the grantees were entitled to attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment for the grantees for rent and partition. The court remanded for a determination of whether the tenant had reasonable grounds to deny requests for admission and whether the grantees were entitled to attorney fees.

 

1434 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Zintek v. Perchik


Nos. 90-0838, 90-1795


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


163 Wis. 2d 439; 471 N.W.2d 522; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 807


March 5, 1991, Oral argument  
May 29, 1991, Decided  
May 29, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Ozaukee County: Joseph D. McCormack, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, physicians and insurance companies, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Ozaukee County (Wisconsin), which awarded judgment and damages in favor of respondents, patient and associated individuals, in medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, patient and associated individuals, initiated medical malpractice action against appellants, physicians and insurance companies. The trial court granted judgment in favor of respondents and awarded damages, taxable costs, disbursements, and postverdict interest. Appellants sought review. The court held that, in a medical malpractice action, the relevant question was not whether a physician had made a mistake, rather, the question was whether he was negligent. The court held that the evidence supported respondents' malpractice claims. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 814.01(1), respondents were permitted to recover costs and attorney's fees upon their recovery. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 814.04(4), judgment interest was permitted at the rate of 12 percent. The court held that the maximum rate of interest allowed was 12 percent. The court determined that the statutory interest rate was not usurious because it merely equaled the maximum rate. The court held that the trial court had not abused its discretion in awarding costs, attorney's fees, and judgment interest to respondents. The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which granted judgment to respondents, patient and associated individuals, in medical malpractice action against appellants, physicians and insurance companies. The court held that the trial court had not abused its discretion in awarding damages, taxable costs, disbursements, and postverdict interest to respondents because the evidence supported respondents' claims.

DeCecco v. Board of Regents


No. 90-1783


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


163 Wis. 2d 526; 472 N.W.2d 248; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 781



May 23, 1991  
May 23, 1991, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Robert A. DeChambeau, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner student sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of a university's nonresident appeals committee that determined that the student was not a resident for tuition purposes, finding that the student triggered the rebuttable presumption of non-residency embodied in Wis. Stat. § 36.27(2)(e).


OVERVIEW: The student enrolled in a state university's law school and after paying non-resident tuition for his first year of law school he appealed his non-resident status to the committee. The committee upheld the student's non-resident classification, among other reasons, that he entered and remained in Wisconsin principally to obtain an education. The student paid non-resident tuition for an additional year of law school and again appealed his non-resident status, claiming that since the time of the first appeal he had additional contacts with the State of Wisconsin. On review the court found no error. The court rejected the student's claim that the committee improperly required him to prove residency by conclusive evidence rather than clear and convincing evidence. The court held that the student took the term "conclusive evidence" out of context. The committee simply meant that the student's claims and proffered evidence were not in themselves conclusive on the subject of his residency. The committee neither required conclusive evidence of residency, nor did it subject the student to an impermissibly high standard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order.

State v. Thomas


No. 90-2843-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


163 Wis. 2d 528; 472 N.W.2d 249; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 831



May 15, 1991  
May 15, 1991, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)4, STATS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: Willis J. Zick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) that denied his motion for postconviction relief from a judgment of conviction for operating a motor vehicle with a blood alcohol concentration (BAC) in excess of the legal limit in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Police stopped defendant's vehicle after it was observed travelling at an excessive rate of speed. Police requested defendant to perform field sobriety tests because he exhibited signs of possible intoxication. Defendant was arrested and transported to a hospital for a blood test, which revealed his BAC to be in excess of the legal limit. Defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle with a BAC in excess of the legal limit. The trial court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief, and he appealed. The court affirmed. Defendant contended that the trial court erred when it refused to instruct the jury on an alternative method of computing BAC. Though defendant was entitled to an instruction on a valid theory of defense, he was not entitled to an instruction that merely highlighted evidentiary factors. Such an instruction was improper, and the trial court was correct to reject it. Defendant further contended that the State violated its duty to disclose exculpatory evidence when it failed to disclose that the blood testing kit contained ethyl alcohol. The constitutional duty of a prosecutor was to disclose exculpatory evidence within his exclusive control.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying postconviction relief.

WASHINGTON CTY. v. LABOR & INDUS. REVIEW COMMN.


No. 90-1945


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


163 Wis. 2d 527; 472 N.W.2d 248; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 804



May 8, 1991  
May 8, 1991, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Washington county: Walter J. Swietlik, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action regarding the award of disability benefits, appellant county sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin), which confirmed an order of respondent Wisconsin Labor and Industry Review Commission awarding benefits under Wis. Stat. § 66.191 (1981-82), to respondent deputy sheriff for injuries he suffered while employed by the county.


OVERVIEW: The deputy injured his knee while on duty. Cartilage was removed from his knee by arthroscopic surgery. The treating physician assessed 15 percent permanent partial disability at the right knee. The deputy later resigned and cited his knee injury as the reason. He also waived disability benefits under Wis. Stat. § 40.63, and elected to receive disability benefits under Wis. Stat. § 66.191. The county argued that it had never opted into § 66.191 via Wis. Stat. § 59.07(4), so the deputy was not eligible for benefits thereunder. The deputy argued that op-in was not required. The Commission awarded benefits to the deputy under Wis. Stat. § 66.191. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 59.07(4) revealed a legislative intent that a county board had the option of applying Wis. Stat. § 66.191 to those deputy sheriffs it so chose. Therefore, because the county did not elect to provide that § 66.191 apply to the deputy, he was not eligible for relief under that section.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and held that the deputy was ineligible for disability benefits.

Skow v. Goodrich


No. 90-0213


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


162 Wis. 2d 448; 469 N.W.2d 888; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 755


September 7, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
April 11, 1991, Decided  
April 11, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not disposed of at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Moria Krueger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge sought review of a judgment rendered by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his declaratory judgment action, holding that Wis. Admin. Code § DOC 302.32(2), which authorized the early release on probation of certain prison inmates, did not violates the separation of powers doctrine.


OVERVIEW: The judge filed suit seeking a declaratory judgment that Wis. Admin. Code § DOC 302.32(2), which authorized the early release on probation of certain prison inmates, was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers doctrine. The trial court dismissed the action and the judge appealed. The court held that the constitutionality of a provision of the administrative code was a question of law which the appellate court decided de novo. The court stated that statutes and regulations carried a heavy presumption of constitutionality and the challenger had the burden of proving unconstitutionality beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also noted that § DOC 302.32(2) did not violate the separation of powers doctrine because under the adversary process, the executive branch assumes the responsibility of directing the correctional and rehabilitative processes of the parole and probation system. The court observed that it was the function of the executive branch to grant paroles and pardons and therefore regulation of the timing and method of release from prison to parole was well within the department's powers. The court upheld the dismissal of the lawsuit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In Interest of K.K.

DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded with instructions to reinstate the order terminating C.D.K.'s parental rights.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which dismissed a petition to terminate respondent parent's parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The county appealed from an order dismissing a petition to terminate parental rights. The trial court initially determined the parental rights should be terminated. Upon reconsideration, however, the trial court concluded that, because only two of six dispositional orders contained the warnings required by Wis. Stat. § 48.356, the county could not establish that grounds existed under Wis. Stat. § 48.415 for termination of parental rights. The court held that termination cases for abandonment under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(1), only a single order need include the warnings. Because one of the grounds relied on by the trial court for termination was abandonment under § 48.415(1) and because the dispositional orders contained the required warnings, the trial court erred by dismissing the action upon reconsideration. Under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(1)(a)(2), the court found that the parent had abandoned the children before orders were entered. The court held that the phrase "incidental contact" was sufficiently unambiguous. Therefore, the attorney could not be deemed ineffective for failing to assert a vagueness challenge that would have been unsuccessful.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court dismissing the county's petition to terminate the parent's rights was reversed and remanded with instructions.

State v. Bertrand


No. 90-1327-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


162 Wis. 2d 411; 469 N.W.2d 873; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 752


December 11, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
April 3, 1991, Decided  
April 3, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County: Mark S. Gempeler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion for postconviction relief after he was convicted of violating the hostage-taking statute, Wis. Stat. § 940.305, by holding a police officer hostage after he was stopped for a traffic violation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the hostage-taking statute, Wis. Stat. § 904.305, was unconstitutional because it was silent about intent, vague about the timing of injury, and in violation of equal protection by providing an identical penalty for defendants who injured their hostages and for those who did not. The court found that the statute unambiguously punished more severely those who did not release their hostages unharmed before the hostage-taker's arrest. The court further found that defendant's misreading of the statute led him to the incorrect notion that the statute was vague and was a strict liability statute that violated his due process rights by not requiring the state to prove at trial that he had the intent to injure his hostage. Finally, the court found that the statute did not violate defendant's equal protection rights by means of an irrational classification. The classification in the statute had a rational basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief.

In Interest of B.S.


Nos. 90-0830, 90-0831, 90-0832


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


162 Wis. 2d 378; 469 N.W.2d 860; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 748


November 15, 1990, Oral argument  
April 2, 1991, Decided  
April 2, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: P. Charles Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which declared that Wis. Stat. § 48.355(6), which provided for sanctions when a juvenile delinquent violated a dispositional order, was unconstitutional because it deprived juveniles of liberty without due process of law, contrary to the fourteenth amendment to the United States Constitution. U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: In consolidated judicial proceedings, the state moved to impose sanctions on several juveniles under Wis. Stat. § 48.355(6) for violating a condition of a delinquency dispositional order entered against each child. The children each challenged the constitutionality of § 48.355(6) on the basis that it deprived juveniles of liberty without due process of law. The trial court found the statute was unconstitutional. Upon review, the court reversed. The court found that the sanctions under § 48.355 were merely incidental to the state's legitimate interests rather than unconstitutionally punitive where the purpose behind the statute was to save delinquent children from the consequences of criminal behavior. The court held that no basis existed for the conclusion that the statute granted juvenile courts contempt power. The court determined that the statute met due process requirements where notice of the intent to sanction needed to be given to the parties, all motions needed to state with particularity the grounds therefor, evidence against the juvenile needed to be disclosed at the sanctions hearing, and the child was entitled to present evidence at the hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment that declared a statute that provided for sanctions for a juvenile violating a dispositional order unconstitutional.

Wyss v. Albee
