DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff vendor challenged the judgment and order of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his complaint to foreclose a land contract and to obtain a deficiency judgment against defendant partners in the vendee.


OVERVIEW: The vendor brought an action against the partners to foreclose a land contract and to obtain a deficiency judgment. The partners asserted that they had no personal liability because they were limited partners in a defectively formed limited partnership. The trial court concluded that under Wisconsin law the partners had no personal liability to the vendor and dismissed his deficiency claim. The vendor filed a motion to dismiss his complaint in order to obtain appellate review. The trial court granted the vendor's motion. The court further concluded that the Iowa Revised Uniform Limited Partnership Act (1976), rather than the Iowa Revised Uniform Limited Partnership Act (1985) applied because the intent of the Iowa Legislature was that the 1985 version should only be prospective to the extent necessary to protect partners' expectancies. The partners were not entitled to summary judgment because they failed to show that the vendor did not believe them to be general partners.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the partners and the order dismissing the vendor's claim for a deficiency judgment and remanded the case to the trial court.

Northern States Power Co. v. Department of Revenue

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Michael N. Nowakowski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane county (Wisconsin), which dismissed the corporation's petition to review an order of the Tax Appeals Commission disallowing a the corporation's income tax deduction for its gift of real estate to the federal government.


OVERVIEW: The Tax Appeals Commission (Commission) denied the corporation's deduction because Wis. Stat. § 71.04(5)(a) and (d)(1) (1975) allowed deductions for gifts to the state, but did not allow a deduction for a gift to the federal government. On appeal, the corporation claimed that the statute was unconstitutional. The court upheld the dismissal of the corporation's appeal because the corporation failed to raise the issue before the Commission. The constitutional issue had to be raised and the record developed even though the Commission lacked power to decide the issue. Such was the mandate of the Wisconsin Supreme Court and the court concluded that it was compelled to follow that precedent. The corporation's passing reference to constitutional concerns of the statute before the Commission was not enough to raise the issue because the argument was not developed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Employers Health Ins. Co. v. Tesmer


No. 90-1682


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


161 Wis. 2d 733; 469 N.W.2d 203; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 291


January 8, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
March 14, 1991, Decided  
March 14, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court For Dane County: Michael B. Torphy, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff health insurer appealed a judgment and order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which, under Wis. Stat. § 102.30(7)(b), denied the insurer's request to intervene in a workers' compensation (WC) proceedings and dismissed the insurer's complaint against defendants, the insured and a WC carrier, for reimbursement of medical payments. The insurer alleged that Wis. Stat. § 102.30(7)(b) violated Wis. Const. art. I, § 9.


OVERVIEW: A health insurer paid an insured's medical bills; filed a complaint against the insured and the insured's employer's WC carrier for reimbursement of the bills, and filed a request to intervene in the proceedings on the insured's claim against the carrier for WC benefits. The trial court denied the request and dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed and held as follows: Wis. Stat. § 102.30(7)(b) expressly precluded the insurer from intervening in the insured's WC proceeding. However, if the insured prevailed on his claim for WC benefits, Wis. Stat. § 102.30(7)(a) allowed the insurer to petition the Wisconsin Department of Industry, Labor and Human Relations for reimbursement. Any settlement between the insured and the carrier was not binding on the insurer. Thus, the insurer had a remedy for its wrongs if any payments should not have been made, although it was not the remedy that the insurer would have preferred. Therefore, Wis. Stat. § 102.30(7)(b) did not violate Wis. Const. art. I, § 9.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Luedtke v. State


No. 90-2374


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


161 Wis. 2d 936; 469 N.W.2d 249; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 233



March 12, 1991  
March 12, 1991, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Pierce county: Robert W. Wing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Pierce County (Wisconsin), which reversed a determination of the Wisconsin Department of Transportation (DOT) that found plaintiff to be a habitual traffic offender.


OVERVIEW: Based on plaintiff's five convictions for out-of-state driving offenses, the DOT revoked his operating privilege for five years under Wis. Stat. § 351.025. Upon review, the lower court reversed the DOT's revocation order on the ground that only three of the offenses could be counted toward the four offenses needed to qualify as a habitual traffic offender under Wis. Stat. § 351.02(1)(a). Essentially, the lower court found that two offenses could only be counted as one because they arose out of the same occurrence and that a Michigan law under which plaintiff had been convicted was not in substantial conformity with Wisconsin law. The state appealed. Although the lower court did not exceed its authority under Wis. Stat. § 351.027(2) to review the DOT's license revocation decision, the court reversed because the lower court erred by requiring that laws of other jurisdictions must be in "substantial conformity" with Wisconsin law to be counted under Wis. Stat. § 351.02(1)(a)10. Rather, the 1989 amendment of the habitual traffic offender statute deleted the requirement that an out-of-state offense could only be counted when such an offense was in strict conformity with Wisconsin law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order that reversed the DOT's determination that plaintiff was a habitual traffic offender. Accordingly, the DOT's revocation of plaintiff's license was reinstated.

State v. J.E.B.


No. 90-0963-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


161 Wis. 2d 655; 469 N.W.2d 192; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 296


September 14, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
March 6, 1991, Decided  
March 6, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgments and an order of the Circuit Court For Kenosha County: Robert V. Baker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgments and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the sentencing provisions of two judgments of the Circuit Court For Kenosha County (Wisconsin), convicting him of first-degree sexual assault and from an order denying his motion for resentencing. Defendant argued that this sentence was invalid because the trial court improperly considered his use of reading materials protected under the First Amendment and because the trial court engaged in "mechanistic" sentencing.


OVERVIEW: The convictions resulted from defendant's illegal sexual contact with his juvenile daughter. The presentence investigation report noted that defendant had an interest in pornography, especially the novels containing graphic descriptions of adults having sexual contact with children. The text of the trial court's decision indicated that while defendant's choice of reading material was not the major factor influencing the sentence, it was nevertheless a relevant factor. The court found that the reading materials were constitutionally protected and that they did not constitute child pornography because they did not involve visual depiction of children engaged in sexual activity. However, there was a reliable showing of a sufficient relationship between the criminal activity and the constitutional activity so that the trial court's consideration of the reading materials did not violate defendant's First Amendment rights. The sentencing court's remarks, viewed in their totality, also did not merely pay "lip service" to the various sentencing criteria considered. Instead, the trial court touched on all the factors, positive and negative, which were relevant to defendant's sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction and the order denying resentencing.

DEPARTMENT OF EMPLOYE TRUST FUNDS v. LABOR & INDUS. REVIEW COMMN.

February 14, 1991, Released

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: George A.W. Northrup, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Wisconsin Department of Employee Trust Funds sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Dane County, which affirmed a trial court's affirmance of a decision by respondent Wisconsin Labor and Industry Review Commission awarding disability benefits to respondent ex-employee pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 40.65 (1985-86).


OVERVIEW: The ex-employee was injured in 1977. After she resigned, she applied for and was denied benefits under Wis. Stat. § 66.191 (1979). She reapplied under Wis. Stat. § 40.65 (1985-86). An examiner found that she was entitled to benefits. The Commission modified and affirmed the findings, and the trial court affirmed the Commission's decision. On appeal, the Department argued in part that the ex-employee was not entitled to benefits because she was not a protective occupation participant at the time she applied. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) Wis. Stat. § 40.65 (1985-86) plainly required one to be a "protective occupation participant" only at the time of injury; (2) evidence that the ex-employee underwent training for her job, which required her to deal with aggressive inmates, supported the Commission's finding that she was a "protective occupation participant" at the time of injury; and (3) the record did not show that the ex-employee received more benefits under § 40.65 than she would have under Wis. Stat. § 66.191 (1979), and thus did not support the argument that she got a retroactive increase from non-state funds in violation of Wis. Const. art. IV, § 26.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which had been in favor of the ex-employee.

 

1450 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zoellick


Nos. 90-1397-CR, 90-1399-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


160 Wis. 2d 483; 466 N.W.2d 911; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 61



January 31, 1991  
January 31, 1991, Filed  
January 31, 1991, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judges of the circuit court for Jefferson county: John B. Danforth, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Jefferson County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant for violating a temporary restraining order. Defendant argued the temporary restraining order was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: A victim obtained a temporary restraining order against defendant, who then had contact with her on two occasions. Defendant was convicted for violating the order and for violating the conditions of his bail on an unrelated charge. Four days after the temporary restraining order was issued, a permanent injunction was issued. Defendant again had contact with the victim, and was charged with violating the injunction. The charge was dismissed, but defendant was convicted for another count of bail jumping. On appeal, defendant argued that the temporary restraining order was unconstitutionally vague, and that the evidence did not support his conviction. The court affirmed the convictions, holding that the temporary restraining order did not violate due process because it only prohibited harassing behavior, where "harassing" was defined in terms of a statutory definition that had already withheld constitutional scrutiny. Further, evidence which showed in part that defendant watched the victim's daughter undress and followed the victim into a private office was sufficient to support the convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant for violating a temporary restraining order.

 

1451 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Vorwald v. School Dist. of River Falls


No. 90-1908-FT


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


160 Wis. 2d 536; 466 N.W.2d 683; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 89


December 10, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
January 29, 1991, Decided  
January 29, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not disposed of at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court For Pierce County: Robert W. Wing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant custodian sought appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court For Pierce County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the custodian's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim against respondent school district (district) for terminating his employment without adequate notice and a fair hearing in violation of his procedural due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The custodian was terminated after a job-related injury. The trial court dismissed the custodian's § 1983 claim because it held that worker's compensation law provided the exclusive remedy. On appeal, the court held that because the exclusivity of the worker's compensation law did not bar a § 1983 claim when the state terminated an employee without adequate notice and an opportunity to respond the judgment was reversed. The court found that the custodian was entitled to notice and a meaningful opportunity to respond before he was terminated. The court noted that because post-termination state remedies could not cure any violation of this right, the trial court erred by holding that the Worker's Compensation Act provided the exclusive remedy. The court disagreed with the district that a pre-deprivation hearing on the issue of termination was neither feasible nor practical where the termination was based on workplace injury. The court also rejected the claim that the custodian needed to exhaust administrative remedies before bringing a § 1983 action because the court noted there were no administrative remedies available to the custodian as the district did not provide a review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and held that the custodian's action was improperly dismissed.

 

1452 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Darlington


No. 90-1127


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


160 Wis. 2d 418; 466 N.W.2d 233; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 50


October 29, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
January 23, 1991, Decided  
January 23, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court For Lafayette County: William D. Johnston, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents individually and on behalf of their son's estate, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Lafayette County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment to respondents, a city and an insurer, for negligence in the drowning death of their son in the city's outdoor swimming pool because Wis. Stat. § 895.52 barred their complaint.


OVERVIEW: The drowning occurred in an outdoor swimming pool owned and operated by the city. At the time of the drowning, there were three lifeguards on duty, none of who were at their assigned stations. Appellants maintained that the city was not entitled to immunity under § 895.52 because of the duty of care created by the Wisconsin Department of Health and Social Services' regulations governing safety at public swimming pools. Upon review, the court found that there was no express intention in Wis. Stat. § 140.05 to create a standard of care whereby a violation served as an independent basis for a negligence action. Thus, a violation of the Department's regulations could not support their action. Under Wis. Stat. § 895.52(2)(a)(1) the city had no duty to supervise properly trained lifeguards. The exception for immunity when the municipal property was used for an event in which the owner charged an admission fee for spectators under § 895.52(4)(a) was unavailable because pool patrons could not be considered "spectators" at an "event." Summary judgment for respondents was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for respondents in appellants' action against them for negligent in the drowning death of their son in the city's outdoor swimming pool.

 

1453 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jeter


No. 90-1079-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


160 Wis. 2d 333; 466 N.W.2d 211; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 39


October 5, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
January 16, 1991, Decided  
January 16, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court For Racine County: Dennis J. Barry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment convicting him of possessing a controlled substance as a habitual offender, which was rendered by the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that a valid search warrant which specifically authorized the search of a house and the seizure of cocaine and related paraphernalia did not implicitly carry with it the right to search any individual who happened to be present in the house at the time of the search for weapons or contraband. The court disagreed. A no-knock warrant was executed on a residence. Defendant was present at the time, and was searched. The warrant and its supporting affidavit referenced cocaine and cocaine-related paraphernalia. The court found that the search of defendant was reasonable because it was minimally intrusive and was reasonably necessary to assure the officers' safety and to prevent the disposal or concealment of contraband. Furthermore, the address searched was not a public place, the site had been recently raided by police and the searches yielded weapons, drugs, and drug-related paraphernalia. It was reasonable to infer that the location was a drug house. It might have been difficult to accurately predict who might be on the premises at a given time. Therefore, although the warrant did not specifically name defendant, he had been lawfully searched.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

1454 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Martinez v. Department of Industry, Labor & Human Relations


No. 90-1266


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


160 Wis. 2d 272; 466 N.W.2d 189; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 38; 30 Wage & Hour Cas. (BNA) 362


November 19, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
January 15, 1991, Decided  
January 15, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court For Dane County: Susan R. Steingass, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Industry, Labor, and Human Relations (DILHR) sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which upheld the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 227.26 in an action brought by respondent individuals and joined by respondents, Joint Committee on Legislative Organization (JCLO) and Joint Committee for Review of Administrative Rules (JCRAR).


OVERVIEW: The DILHR adopted Wis. Admin. Code § Ind. 72.01(16), which set forth the requirements for probationary employment. Subsequently, the JCRAR exercised its power under Wis. Stat. § 227.26 and suspended parts of Wis. Admin. Code § Ind. 72.01(16), diminishing the time in which an employee was to be considered a probationary employee. The DILHR notified employers that the JCRAR lacked the authority to suspend the rule and implemented the rule as drafted. The individuals brought an action against the DILHR, seeking to require it to enforce § 72.01(16) as it read following the JCRAR's suspension and the JCRAR and the JCLO intervened in the action. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the individuals and the DILHR sought review. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 227.26 violated the separation of powers because it allowed the JCRAR to create new law without presentment to the governor and deprived the executive branch of the opportunity to exercise its power of veto. The court found that the JCRAR was not entitled to impermissibly interfere with executive powers and could not suspend Wis. Admin. Code § Ind. 72.01(16).


OUTCOME: The court, holding that the doctrine of separation of powers had been violated when the JCRAR suspended an administrative rule, reversed the trial court's decision and remanded the matter for a determination of issues not previously decided.

In Interest of S.R.


No. 90-1221


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


160 Wis. 2d 48; 468 N.W.2d 32; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1202



December 26, 1990  
December 26, 1990, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Christopher R. Foley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a dispositional order from the Circuit Court, Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, that transferred his custody to the Department of Health and Social Services, Division of Corrections, with physical placement at a boys' school for one year. The juvenile argued that because the stop and frisk was constitutionally infirm, evidence seized and his incriminating statement should have been suppressed.


OVERVIEW: The delinquency petition alleged that the juvenile, as party to a crime, knowingly possessed 10 grams or less of cocaine with intent to deliver. At the suppression hearing, an officer testified that he executed a "no-knock" search warrant at a flat. The warrant was based on an informant's tip that he had purchased cocaine from a person in the flat less than 72 hours earlier. The officers involved in the search were advised that a man with a gun and a lookout might be found near the flat. Police records showed that cocaine and money had previously been seized at the flat. The officer testified that he saw the juvenile standing on the porch leading up to the flat. The officer conducted a "stop and frisk" and found cocaine and money. Another officer took the juvenile's statement, which implicated him in the sale of cocaine at the flat. Under the totality of the circumstances, the court agreed that the stop and search was reasonable under Wis. Stat. § 968.16. The officer was justified in stopping and frisking the juvenile for his own protection. The trial court properly denied suppression of the cocaine and money seized and statements taken as a result of the stop and search.


OUTCOME: The dispositional order that transferred the juvenile to a boys' school for one year was affirmed.

State v. Pittman


No. 90-0840


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


159 Wis. 2d 764; 465 N.W.2d 245; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1229


October 26, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
December 19, 1990, Decided  
December 19, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Racine county: Jon B. Skow, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which entered a conviction against him for unlawfully possessing a firearm as a convicted felon pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 941.29(1)(a) and (2) and 939.62. Defendant argued that the evidence used against him was the product of an unlawful arrest.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court was whether the seizure of defendant, as a parolee, in his residence upon a parole violation apprehension request was valid under the U.S. Const. amend. IV. After verifying the apprehension warrant and obtaining defendant's address, the arresting officer went to defendant's residence and knocked on the door. Defendant partially opened the door, but then attempted to close the door. At that point, the officers pushed the door open and entered the apartment and seized defendant on the apprehension warrant. The court affirmed defendant's subsequent conviction for unlawful possession of a firearm as a convicted felon. Specifically, the court held that in light of a parolee's conditional liberty and diminished expectation of privacy under amend. IV, a judicially issued arrest warrant was not a prerequisite for the seizure of defendant, an alleged parole violator, in his residence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Edge


No. 90-1592-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


160 Wis. 2d 49; 468 N.W.2d 32; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1154



December 6, 1990  
December 6, 1990, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Grant county: John R. Wagner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin), which convicted him, upon his no contest plea, of possessing a switchblade knife, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.24(1).


OVERVIEW: Before pleading no contest to a charge of violating Wis. Stat. § 941.24(1) by possessing a switchblade knife, defendant unsuccessfully moved to dismiss on grounds that § 941.24(1) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. He appealed the judgment of conviction that was entered upon his plea, but the court affirmed the judgment because § 941.24(1) was constitutional. Even though defendant entered a no contest plea, his claim that the statute was unconstitutional survived his plea. The phrase "other device or movement" in § 941.24(1) was not vague because even if such language could be stretched to include a jackknife, such holding would only add jackknives to the range of prohibited knives. Section 941.24(1) remained sufficiently definite to alert an ordinary person to the type of conduct prohibited. The use of the terms "other device," "gravity," "thrust," and "movement" was not broadly sweeping language covering jackknives. Furthermore, defendant made no attempt to establish a constitutional right to carry a jackknife or any other kind of knife. He offered no other examples showing how § 941.24(1) could have deterred individuals from exercising purported constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Stippich

Defendant's arrest was part of a mass arrest of Indian spear-fishing protesters who refused to terminate their sit-in at a public boat landing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the complaint and the evidence at trial, the admission of evidence of the activities of protestors other than herself, and the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 166.04 and Wis. Stat. § 166.02, which permitted the use of law enforcement officers from other jurisdictions. Photographs showing defendant standing to the forefront of those on the boat landing, waving a large American flag, and defendant's own testimony that she knowingly stepped across the police line constituted sufficient evidence to support the verdict.

State v. Jackson


Nos. 90-1039-CR, 90-1040-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


159 Wis. 2d 432; 464 N.W.2d 680; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1107



November 15, 1990  
November 15, 1990, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane county: George A.W. Northrup, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged orders from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which sentenced him to three years in prison and 18 months probation for a violation of a no-contact provision from previous convictions. Defendant had previously pled no contest to misdemeanor battery and bail jumping. Defendant had received probation and was ordered not to have any contact with the victim.


OVERVIEW: The victim was defendant's girlfriend. After the issuance of the no-contact order, police were called to the victim's apartment. The victim had been physically abused. Defendant was arrested. The victim did not attend defendant's probation revocation hearing and signed an affidavit that stated she had lied about defendant beating her. Prior to sentencing, defendant married the victim. The sentencing court found that defendant's contact with the victim was adequate to sustain revocation of his probation. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's argument that the sentencing court had mistakenly relied on the evidence of the unproven battery. The sentencing court had properly evaluated defendant's character and was entitled to consider the underlying evidence of the victim's physical condition, despite the affidavit. The sentencing court had not failed to consider the victim's wish that defendant not be incarcerated. It had properly considered her wishes and disregarded them. Defendant had failed to prove that his sentence violated the Eighth Amendment. The sentencing court did not lose jurisdiction over defendant because he had been bound over pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 970.03(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that sentenced defendant for violation of the no-contact order from his previous convictions.

State v. McCollum


Nos. 90-0968-CR, 90-0969-CR, 90-0970-CR, 90-0971-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


159 Wis. 2d 184; 464 N.W.2d 44; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1121


October 3, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
November 14, 1990, Decided  
November 14, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from an order of the circuit court for Eau Claire county: Gregory A. Peterson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County dismissing charges of prostitution filed against four defendants who were each charged with one count of prostitution, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 944.30(5).


OVERVIEW: The State contended on appeal that the trial court erred by ruling that defendants were selectively prosecuted in violation of the fourteenth amendment's equal protection clause. The court found that no males who engaged in sexual contact with defendants were arrested and held that the trial court properly applied the "discriminatory effect/discriminatory purpose" standard which required defendants to show both that the state's enforcement system had a discriminatory effect and was motivated by a discriminatory purpose. The court further held that the trial court did not err in finding that defendants and their male patrons were similarly situated and that the state's program of enforcement had a discriminatory effect. Because the police intentionally focused their investigation on, and made their arrests of, only the female violators of Wis. Stat. § 944.30, and there was no important governmental objective substantially related to this enforcement scheme, the court concluded that the State selectively prosecuted defendants in violation of the equal protection clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the prostitution charges against defendants.

 

1461 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Grover


No. 90-1807


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


159 Wis. 2d 150; 464 N.W.2d 220; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1043


October 3, 1990, Oral argument  
November 13, 1990, Decided  
November 13, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: Susan R. Steingass, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, representing disadvantaged Milwaukee public school students, brought an action in the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) to compel defendant state school superintendent to comply with Wis. Stat. § 119.23, which required the state to pay private school tuition for the students. A taxpayer and others intervened as defendants, challenging the statute's constitutionality. The trial court upheld the statute and defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The statute, a multi-item state budget adjustment bill, provided a state subsidy for low-income children in cities of the "first class" to attend private school. Reversing the circuit court, the court found that the statute violated Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18, which provided that no private or local bill could embrace more than one subject. The purpose of art. IV, § 18 was to prevent bills benefiting private or local interests from being "smuggled" through the legislature. The court applied the classification test to determine that the bill was "private or local" within the meaning of the constitution. The statute failed to satisfy at least two parts of the test: first, there was nothing substantially distinct about cities of the first class (of which Milwaukee was the only one) that made it necessary for them, as opposed to all other cities, to have the Parental Choice Program. Second, the classification was not "germane" to the purpose of § 119.23, which was to conduct a test program in education. The statute was therefore "private or local" legislation that could not constitutionally be passed as part of a bill which embraced more than one subject.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court.

State v. Ellenbecker


No. 90-0898-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


159 Wis. 2d 91; 464 N.W.2d 427; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1080


October 8, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
November 7, 1990, Decided  
November 7, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Racine county: Dennis J. Barry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction in the circuit court for Racine County (Wisconsin) for possession of marijuana with intent to deliver.


OVERVIEW: A state patrol officer saw defendant's car, with the hood up, on the shoulder of a road. The officer pulled behind the car and offered help. He also asked for defendant's driver's license and ran a status check on it. After learning that the license was revoked, the officer arrested defendant. In the search incident to the arrest, the officer found drugs. Defendant was charged with possession of marijuana, possession with intent to deliver marijuana, and other offenses. The trial court denied defendant's pretrial motion to suppress the evidence. Defendant eventually pled guilty to possession of marijuana with intent to deliver. On appeal, the court held that: (1) a seizure was constitutional if it passed the Fourth Amendment's reasonableness requirement; (2) the officer's actions passed the Fourth Amendment reasonableness test because the public interest in asking for the license and conducting a status check outweighed the minimal intrusion involved; and (3) there was no basis to suppress the evidence discovered in the search because the officer's request for the license and the status check passed the Fourth Amendment reasonableness test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Sutton v. Kaarakka


No. 90-0966


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


159 Wis. 2d 83; 464 N.W.2d 29; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1106


October 8, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
November 7, 1990, Decided  
November 7, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Racine county: Stephen A. Simanek, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an employer and its insurer, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin). The trial court denied the employer's motion to intervene and to participate in respondent employee's medical malpractice settlement pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 102.29(3), which became effective after the employee's work accident but before the alleged medical malpractice.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied the employer and its insurer's motion to intervene in the employee's medical malpractice action. On appeal, the court reversed. The amendment to § 102.29(3), which became effective after the employee's work accident but before the medical malpractice, removed the prohibition against employers sharing in the employee's awards from medical malpractice claims and allowed the employer to intervene. Because the employee's cause of action against the doctor did not accrue until after the amendment became effective, neither did the employer's right to subrogation under § 102.29.


OUTCOME: The denial of the motion to intervene was reversed and the cause was remanded.

Oneida County v. New Northernaire, Inc.


No. 90-0414

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Oneida County (Wisconsin), which granted respondent developer's motion for summary judgment in the county's action to enforce its zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The developer purchased five former resort cottages on the shores of a lake. The cottages were nonconforming uses from the time of the enactment of the county's zoning ordinance. The developer applied for and received a zoning permit authorizing specified work for a specified amount for each cottage. The county's zoning ordinance governing work on nonconforming buildings prohibited work that exceeded 50 percent of the value the building became a nonconforming use. After the work commenced, the county filed an action against the developer alleging that the developer exceeded the authorized expenditures and thereby exceeded 50 percent of the estimated fair market value of the cottages. The developer argued that the county unconstitutionally applied the ordinance when it determined fair market value at the time the permit was issued. The trial court entered summary judgment for the developer. The county appealed. The court held that the developer could not enjoy the benefits of the zoning ordinance and attack its validity.

1465 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In Interest of M.G.


No. 89-1791


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


158 Wis. 2d 728; 463 N.W.2d 880; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 996



October 16, 1990  
October 16, 1990, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Christopher R. Foley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent county brought a termination of parental rights (TPR) petition against appellant mother. A jury in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) made findings against the mother, and the trial court granted the TPR petition. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county alleged that the mother had abandoned the child under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(1)(a) and that she had failed to assume parental responsibility under § 48.415(6). The mother claimed that she had seen the child periodically in the backyard of his foster home and had talked to him by telephone once. The trial court did not submit to the jury the question of whether the mother had failed to visit or to communicate with the child for six months or longer, but answered the question itself affirmatively, reasoning that any contact between the mother and the child was incidental and did not amount to normal visits or communication. The court held that the contacts were indeed incidental and thus did not preclude the trial court from finding that the mother failed to visit or communicate with the child. Even if the trial court erred in not submitting the question to the jury, the court added, the error was harmless because the contacts were incidental. The court also held that Wis. Stat. § 48.424(4), under which a parent would be presumed unfit after the judge or the jury determined that grounds existed for a TPR, did not violate the right to a jury trial and was not overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

1466 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Mequon v. Hess


No. 90-0711


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


158 Wis. 2d 500; 463 N.W.2d 687; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 941


August 24, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
October 3, 1990, Decided  
October 3, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Ozaukee county: Warren A. Grady, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Ozaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI) and operating a motor vehicle with a blood alcohol concentration (BAC) of 0.1 percent or more.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in admitting his breathalyzer test results into evidence because the arresting officer failed to provide him with warnings he claimed were required under Wis. Stat. § 343.305(4) (1987-88), and because his breathalyzer results varied widely. In affirming defendant's convictions the court rejected defendant's contention that an OWI-BAC suspect had to be advised not only of the statutory language in § 343.305(4)(c), but also of the specific penalties which might flow from an OWI-BAC, including a fine, forfeiture, suspension, or revocation of driving privileges, point reduction, and a possible jail sentence. The court noted that the use of the term "any" in § 343.305(4)(c), in requiring a person to be informed of the consequences of failing any BAC test, instead of the term "each," which was used in § 343.305(8)(b)2.d in describing which of the tests might be challenged in an administrative proceeding, might dissuade an accused from taking subsequent tests, but held that it was for the legislature to correct this contradiction in terms.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1467 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Barnhill v. Board of Regents of UW System


No. 89-0372


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


158 Wis. 2d 278; 462 N.W.2d 249; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 802


October 10, 1989, Oral argument  
September 27, 1990, Decided  
September 27, 1990, Filed  
September 27, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to cross-review granted. Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: Susan R. Steingass, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employers sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which found in favor of appellee employee in a suit in which he claimed he was discharged in retaliation for speech protected by the First Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked as an interviewer for a university research laboratory, conducting public opinion surveys. The employers granted the employee's request not to work on a survey of shoppers' attitudes toward group activities in shopping malls because of his political views. Before the survey was complete, the employee provided a copy of the questions to a newspaper, which published some of the questions and quoted the employee. The employers discharged the employee for violating a confidentiality agreement. On appeal, the court held that the employers' interest in promoting the efficiency of their services did not outweigh the employee's interest in commenting on a matter of public concern. Although factors of confidentiality and work rule violations weighed heavily in favor of the employers, the employee's speech touched matters of public concern with sufficient directness to outweigh those factors. The employers were not entitled to qualified immunity because reasonable officials would have known that discharging the employee for the exercise of free speech was unlawful. The jury was improperly instructed concerning the conditions under which punitive damages could be awarded.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part and the case was remanded for a new trial on the availability of punitive damages.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review from an order of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which denied their motion to reopen and vacate a judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was injured while working in a sawmill. He commenced an action more than six years after substantial completion of the sawmill's renovation. The trial court granted summary judgment on the ground that the suit was not commenced within the time required by Wis. Stat. § 893.89. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's dismissal, and the Wisconsin Supreme Court denied appellant's petition for review. However, that court did accept a petition for review in another case involving the same statute of limitations and ruled that § 893.89 was unconstitutional on its face. Appellant sought to reopen and vacate the earlier decision, but the trial court believed that it had no authority to vacate a judgment that had been affirmed by the court of appeals. Because a recent decision of the Wisconsin Supreme Court established that the trial court did have that authority, the court concluded that the order had to be reversed and the cause remanded for the trial court to exercise its discretion and determine whether exceptional circumstances justified granting relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded to the trial court.

Leverence v. United States Fidelity & Guaranty


No. 89-1646


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


158 Wis. 2d 64; 462 N.W.2d 218; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 799


May 5, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
September 5, 1990, Decided  
September 5, 1990, Filed  
September 5, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Price county: Douglas T. Fox, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded. No costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant home occupants challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Price County (Wisconsin), and appellees, insurance companies and a private inspector, cross-appealed the judgment, which dismissed appellants' claims for negligence and strict liability against appellees because the home builder had failed to provide timely notice of an occurrence, and the inspection agency had no extra-contractual duty to appellants.


OVERVIEW: Appellant home occupants brought an action against appellees, insurance companies and a private inspection agency, and others, alleging that that their houses retained excessive moisture as a result of defective design, inappropriate building materials, and faulty construction. The county circuit court granted summary judgment to appellees and concluded that plaintiffs' negligence and strict liability claims failed because the home builder had had not provided timely notice to appellee insurers, and the inspection agency had no duty to plaintiffs outside of its contract with the builder where plaintiffs had failed to demonstrate breach. On appeal, the court reversed the lack of notice ruling, concluding that there was an issue as to when the builder's duty to report arose. The court concluded that the business risk exclusion barred coverage for the cost of repairs, but that bodily injuries and other consequential damages were covered. In addition, the court held that the professional service and pollution exclusion clauses did not apply, rulings as to the effect of the statutes of limitations on the individual claims were not permissible, and that the joinder of claims was proper.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of appellees, insurance companies and a private inspection agency, reversed in part because material issues of fact existed with regard when the home builder's obligation to notify appellee insurers arose, as well as other issues. The court agreed with the trial court's rulings that were challenged on cross-appeal and, therefore, affirmed the judgment with respect to those issues.

 

1470 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stockheimer


No. 89-1615-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


157 Wis. 2d 813; 461 N.W.2d 448; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 773



August 30, 1990  
August 30, 1990, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Clark county; Frederic W. Fleishauer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Clark County (Wisconsin) convicting him of conspiring to practice law without a license.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that: (1) the prosecutor's failure to have a bond on file at the time of trial voided the proceedings; (2) his conviction violated the First Amendment; (3) the search warrant for his home was defective; (4) the State lost jurisdiction over him; and (5) the trial judge improperly denied defendant's motion for recusal. In affirming defendant's conviction, the court found the prosecutor was operating in a de facto capacity at the time of trial and his failure to renew the bond was not grounds for reversal. The impact of prosecuting defendant for practicing law without a license was incidental to his free speech rights. The constitutional protection afforded such rights did not extend to persons delivering legal advice without licenses. The warrant described the property to be seized as a typewriter and papers purporting to be legal documents. The items to be seized were described with sufficient particularity. By signing the waiver of his rights under the Interstate Agreement on Detainers Act, defendant waived his right to challenge any custody transfer. Defendant's civil action against the judge was a sham, so that the judge's impartiality was not questionable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1471 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Milwaukee v. Blondis


No. 89-1702


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


157 Wis. 2d 730; 460 N.W.2d 815; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 761


March 6, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
August 21, 1990, Decided  
August 21, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Richard G. Harvey, Jr., Reserve Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the City of Milwaukee, appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant motor vehicle owner. The trial court declared that Wis. Stat. § 346.55(2) and the City's related ordinance unconstitutionally infringed upon the owner's economic free speech rights by prohibiting him from leaving his vehicle for sale on a street within the City.


OVERVIEW: The owner was arrested for violating § 346.55(2) and the City's related ordinance by parking his automobile on a street with a "For Sale" sign. The trial court declared § 346.55(2) and the ordinance unconstitutional on the basis that it infringed upon the owner's economic free speech rights. On appeal by the City, the court affirmed. Although the "For Sale" sign was distracting, the commercial activity in selling the automobile was truthful and legal rather than misleading or illegal. Therefore, the owner's offer to sell was First Amendment commercial speech protected under the Fourteenth Amendment. Although the City had a substantial interest on traffic safety, the City failed to show that § 346.55(2) and the ordinance were not more extensive than necessary. In fact, the City failed to similarly prohibit other distracting commercial, as well as noncommercial, advertising. Therefore, § 346.55(2) and the ordinance did not directly advance the City's claimed substantial interest in traffic safety.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1472 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Josephson


No. 89-2219-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


157 Wis. 2d 814; 461 N.W.2d 448; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 772



August 14, 1990  
August 14, 1990, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Thomas P. Doherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of violating Wis. Stat. Ann. § 940.22(2) (1983-84), sexual exploitation by a therapist.


OVERVIEW: The victim began therapy with defendant in 1981 and continued her treatment with him until the fall of 1985. In the fall of 1982, defendant and the victim started having a sexual relationship in the context of their patient-therapist relationship. The sexual relationship continued after the therapy sessions terminated. Three weeks after the parties ended their relationship, the victim contacted the police department. On the basis of the stipulated facts presented to the court, defendant was found guilty of sexual exploitation by a therapist. Defendant appealed his conviction and argued that consent was a defense. Defendant also argued that the Wis. Stat. Ann. § 940.22(2) (1983-84) was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court determined that under Wis. Stat. Ann. § 940.22(2) (1983-84) consent was not a defense. The court concluded that § 940.22(2) was not unconstitutionally vague. The court found that the precise scope of § 940.22(2) was plain and clear, in that it was meant to prevent the sexual exploitation of patients by their therapist. The court found that defendant had fair notice of what the statute sought to proscribe.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for sexual exploitation by a therapist.

 

1473 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brownson


No. 90-0417-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


157 Wis. 2d 404; 459 N.W.2d 877; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 706


May 30, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
July 17, 1990, Decided  
July 17, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie county: Dennis C. Luebke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment entered in the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of violations that arose from a breached contract to build a garage. Specifically, defendant was convicted of failure to include the start and finish dates in a written home improvement contract, failure to furnish proper lien waivers, and failure to comply with the terms of a home improvement contract.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the entire regulatory scheme was vague and overbroad; that the evidence adduced at trial was, as a matter of law, insufficient to support the verdict. Further, defendant contended that criminalizing a breach of contract under Wis. Admin. Code § 110.05(9) violated the Thirteenth Amendment's prohibition of involuntary servitude. The court rejected defendant's first two arguments, but agreed that Wis. Admin. Code § 110.05(9) was unconstitutional. The court noted that the overbreadth doctrine did not apply here because defendant did not raise any claim that the statute infringed on his First Amendment rights. The court further noted that the lack of an element of intent within the administrative regulation did not violate defendant's due process rights. As to defendant's claim that Wis. Admin. Code. § 110.05 (9) was unconstitutional, the court noted that both the federal and state constitutions prohibited criminalizing the breach of a labor contract in the absence of any fraud or misrepresentation. The court found that the regulation at issue in this case violated the federal and state constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for failure to include the start and finish dates in a written home improvement contract and for failing to furnish proper lien waivers. However, the court remanded the case to the trial court with directions to vacate defendant's conviction and sentence for failure to comply with the terms of a written home improvement contract.

Gelhaar v. Milwaukee


No. 89-1492


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


157 Wis. 2d 503; 460 N.W.2d 446; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 702



July 10, 1990  
July 10, 1990, Released

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Leah M. Lampone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed an order of the Milwaukee County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) that upheld defendant board of zoning appeals' decision to deny the property owners' request for a permit to operate a pawn shop.


OVERVIEW: After obtaining a temporary certificate of occupancy, the property owners requested a special use exception, variance, and permanent certificate of occupancy to operate a pawn shop. The court upheld the trial court's decision affirming the board's denial of the property owners' application. Milwaukee, Wis., Zoning Ordinances § 295-27 did not unconstitutionally delegate legislative authority to the building inspector; the inspector did not have unlimited discretion to grant or deny special use permits. There was no proof that the property owners did not receive a fair hearing before the board or defendant municipal plan commission. Overwhelming evidence supported the board's denial of the property owners' application. The board made sufficient findings supporting its decision. There was no evidence that the denial of the property owners' application amounted to selective enforcement of the zoning ordinances. The property owners were not entitled to a trial de novo because the case was properly decided by the trial court on the existing record.


OUTCOME: The order upholding the board's decision to deny the property owners' request for a permit to operate a pawn shop was affirmed.

Stat. § 71.05(1)(a). The class action by appellee federal retirees alleged that the statute was unconstitutional and in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.

Stat. § 908.08.

Miller Brands-Milwaukee, Inc. v. Case


No. 89-0984


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


156 Wis. 2d 800; 457 N.W.2d 896; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 434


December 14, 1989, Orally argued  
May 31, 1990, Decided  
May 31, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: Susan R. Steingass, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Wisconsin Department of Revenue (DOR) appealed from a summary judgment by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) declaring that plaintiff wholesaler engaged in trade spending, which did not violate Wisconsin's tied-house law, Wis. Stat. § 125.33(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: The wholesaler sold its fermented malt beverage products to retailers holding Class "B" licenses under Wis. Stat. § 125.26. The DOR notified the wholesaler that it had received a complaint that the wholesaler had violated Wis. Stat. § 125.33(1)(a) by engaging in trade spending and that it was going to investigate the complaint. The wholesaler sought declaratory relief, requesting that the trial court determine whether trade spending violated §125.33(1)(a) and, if so, whether the statute was constitutional. The trial court granted the wholesaler's motion for summary judgment and the DOR appealed. The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment, holding that trade spending violated § 125.33(1)(a) and that the statute was constitutional. The court found that the phrase "thing of value," as used in § 125.33(1)(a), was unambiguous and when the wholesaler's sales agents or employees bought beverages for a retailer's customers, the wholesaler was giving the retailer a thing of value within the meaning of § 124.33(1)(a). The statute was constitutional because it was a reasonable and rational exercise of the state's police power and it was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

Wisconsin Hosp. Ass'n v. Natural Resources Bd.


No. 89-0420


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


156 Wis. 2d 688; 457 N.W.2d 879; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 435


August 24, 1989, Orally argued  
May 17, 1990, Decided  
May 17, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 2, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: Daniel R. Moeser, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed in part and affirmed in part and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, association, hospital, and businesses, sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that entered an order granting summary judgment in favor of appellee board on the constitutionality of the administrative rule in question and dismissing the appellants' claims that the rule was not statutorily authorized and that it denied the hospital equal protection of the laws.


OVERVIEW: The administrative rule in question required all air contaminant sources and their owners or operators to establish emission limitations for hazardous pollutants. Under the rule, hospitals as incinerators of infectious waste were treated differently. Appellants contended that the board had no statutory authority to promulgate the rule, and the hospital contended that the rule denied them equal protection of the law. The court held that the board was properly authorized but that there was insufficient evidence to deny the equal protection claim. The court held that: (1) appellants had standing to challenge the rule because their interests, including those of the association's members, were affected by the rule; (2) the board did not exceed its statutory authority because the elements of the enabling statute matched the rule against those elements; (3) where the constitutionality of an administrative rule was challenged, the existence of facts on which a reasonable justification depended, should appear in the record; and (5) because the record provided no factual basis for the classification, summary judgment should not have been granted supporting its constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the order dismissing appellants' claim that the board lacked statutory authority to adopt the rule, reversed that part dismissing the hospital's equal protection claim, and that part declaring the rule was valid.

American Legion Post 38 v. Appleton


No. 89-1613


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


156 Wis. 2d 825; 458 N.W.2d 391; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 382



May 10, 1990  
May 10, 1990, Filed  
May 10, 1990, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie county: Dennis C. Luebke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), which ruled in favor of respondents, a town and various landowners, and declared that an annexation ordinance enacted by the city was invalid.


OVERVIEW: The city annexed a parcel of land containing no residences on its western border, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 66.021(2)(a)2, after two landowners owning more than 50 percent of the land signed a petition for annexation. One of the petitioning landowners testified that he did not know why respondent landowners' property was included in the annexation and that it was no concern of his whether the city desired to include it. The trial court found that although § 66.021 was facially constitutional, the annexation was arbitrary and capricious. The court found that: (1) the trial court's finding that the city, not the petitioning landowners, determined the boundaries of the annexed territory was supported by ample evidence and was not clearly erroneous; (2) the boundaries of the annexation had to be scrutinized for an abuse of municipal discretion if the annexing municipality was shown to be the real controlling influence in direct annexation proceedings initiated by property owners; and (3) because the city failed to demonstrate a reasonable need for respondent landowners' property, the annexation violated the rule of reason and was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1483 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Wisconsin Public Service Corp. v. Public Service Com.


No. 89-0532


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


156 Wis. 2d 611; 457 N.W.2d 502; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 436; 115 P.U.R.4th 560


March 22, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
May 8, 1990, Decided  
May 8, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Brown county: N. Patrick Crooks, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In cross-appellant utility's rate increase proceeding, appellant citizens' group and the utility sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which affirmed respondent Public Service Commission of Wisconsin's (PSC) determination deducting one tenth of one percent from the utility's reasonable rate of return in setting a rate.


OVERVIEW: The legislature repealed a tax credit previously available to state utilities. The utility did not challenge the repeal, but other state utilities did so. During the pendency of the litigation, the utility paid its taxes without protest. The tax credit repeal was later held unconstitutional. The utility later sought a rate increase. The PSC found that the utility's failure to pay its taxes under protest was imprudent. The PSC determined a reasonable rate of return and deducted from that amount one tenth of one percent in setting the rate. The trial court affirmed the decision. On appeal, the court held that: (1) a finding of imprudence was warranted because the utility failed to take reasonable steps to protect its assets; (2) the PSC had wide discretion in determining factors upon which to set a rate schedule; (3) the PSC needed to consider imprudence only in setting the final rate, not in finding the zone of reasonableness; and (4) the court was bound to affirm the PSC's decision because imprudence was but one factor the PSC considered in setting rates, the "remedy" for imprudence was to be accorded great deference, and the PSC set a reasonable rate of return.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1484 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reed


No. 89-1569-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


156 Wis. 2d 546; 457 N.W.2d 494; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 448

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Racine county: Jon B. Skow, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), convicting defendant of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: The officers in executing a search warrant for defendant's vehicle also searched defendant's person. Defendant was placed in a paddywagon and was partially disrobed by the officers. Cocaine was found in defendant's crotch. Defendant filed a motion to suppress which was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. First, the court held that Wis. Stat. § 968.16 authorized the reasonable search of any person on the premises to prevent concealment or disposal of the particular items sought. The court noted that it was not unreasonable for the officers to believe that defendant would conceal or dispose of the drugs. Defendant's paralysis prevented the officers from conducting a standard search and thus, the officers' search was not unreasonable given the extensiveness of the intrusion. Second, the court held that the informant's affidavit was sufficient because the informant gave lengthy details as to defendant's vehicle and the fashion in which he sold the drugs. The information was reliable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1485 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re C.A.S.


No. 89-0265


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


156 Wis. 2d 446; 456 N.W.2d 899; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 344


October 12, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
April 26, 1990, Decided  
April 26, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Angela B. Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative father sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that dismissed the putative father's petition that sought that he be adjudicated the father of two children belonging to respondents, a mother and her husband.


OVERVIEW: The putative father sought to establish his paternity with respect to two children born to the mother while married to her husband. The trial court initially ordered blood tests but then dismissed the action on the basis of the newly enacted Wis. Stat. § 767.458(1m), which allowed dismissal in this particular situation if it was in the best interest of the child. The court affirmed the trial court's decision and found that the putative father had no constitutionally protected liberty interest in a relationship with the children and thus no right to a blood test because those children were born into an extant marital family. Furthermore, the fact that the initial decision to order blood tests was upheld on appeal was not recognition of the putative father's right to a blood test. The court also found that § 767.458(lm) was intended to be applied retroactively and that the putative father had waived his right to contest the constitutionality of its retroactive application because he did not raise the issue in the trial court. Finally, the court found that the trial court's determination that the best interests of the children warranted dismissal was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to dismiss the putative father's paternity action.

Luson Int'l Distributors, Inc. v. Basic Int'l Corp.


No. 89-0839


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


156 Wis. 2d 465; 458 N.W.2d 388; 458 N.W.2d 532; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 367



April 17, 1990  
April 17, 1990, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from judgments and orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Michael D. Guolee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a consignor corporation and its owner, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment to respondent bank in appellants' action against the bank and a consignee for the seizure and conversion of the consignor's machinery.


OVERVIEW: The consignor failed to perfect its security interest in machinery loaned to the consignee by filing the proper financing statements. The loaned machinery bore tags indicating that it belonged to the consignor. The bank had a perfected security interest in the inventory, machinery, and proceeds of the consignee. The bank seized the consigned machinery after the consignee defaulted on loans with the bank. The consignor sought to recover the machinery, and the trial court held that the bank's security interest in the consignee's collateral had priority over the consignor's unperfected interest. The court affirmed, finding that the consignor's relationship with the consignee was governed by the Uniform Commercial Code (UCC), Wis. Stat. ch. 402, 409, because the UCC predated the parties' agreement. The court held that the tags on the machinery did not give the consignor priority because there was no applicable sign posting law for consignors, and because the bank's perfected security interest had priority regardless of the bank's knowledge. The court held that the UCC did not impair the constitutional obligation of contracts provisions because the UCC preceded the claimed contract.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the bank.

Community Newspapers, Inc. v. West Allis


No. 89-0998


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


156 Wis. 2d 350; 456 N.W.2d 646; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 307; 18 Media L. Rep. 1614


February 7, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
April 17, 1990, Decided  
April 17, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Russell W. Stamper, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant company, whose newspaper was delivered free of charge to readers, disputed an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which entered summary judgment for plaintiffs, a rival corporation and its principal, in their action for declaratory and injunctive relief against the company and defendant City of West Allis, Wisconsin. The issue was which entity should have been awarded a contract for publishing legal notices.


OVERVIEW: The company's bid for the contract was significantly lower than plaintiffs' bid. On appeal, the court considered whether the company was qualified to publish the notices under Wis. Stat. § 985.03(1)(a), pursuant to which a newspaper in which such notices were published had to have a bona fide paid circulation that was 50 percent or more of its circulation. The court rejected the company's argument that paid circulation meant payment from any source, including advertisers. Section 985.03(1)(a) was unambiguous and the City's contract with the company contravened § 985.03(1)(a) and was void. The company's argument rendered parts of § 985.03(1)(a) superfluous. The structure of Wis. Stat. § 985.03 showed that the legislature intended to distinguish between a "paid circulation" and a "circulation;" there was no merit to the company's argument that the trial court's interpretation of Wis. Stat. § 985.03(1)(a) violated the equal protection provisions of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and Wis. Const. art. I, § 1. A strict scrutiny test was not required because no suspect class was involved and the legislative purpose in enacting Wis. Stat. § 985.03(1)(a) was neither arbitrary nor irrational.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment for plaintiffs.

 

1488 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. 89-1752-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


156 Wis. 2d 296; 456 N.W.2d 864; 458 N.W.2d 533; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 300


March 6, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
April 10, 1990, Decided  
April 10, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: William D. Gardner III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) convicting him for making a false statement in three applications for a certificate of title in connection with his sale of three used cars.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in not instructing the jury that a person could not be convicted of violating Wis. Stat. § 342.06(2) unless he or she personally submitted the application to the Department of Transportation. Second, he contended that Wis. Stat. § 342.06 did not authorize the Department to request the information sought by the Dealer's Statement of Sale portion of the application form, and that the trial court's contrary construction rendered the statute unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed. Wis. Stat. § 342.06 did not require that the person who made the false statement be the one who submitted the application to the Department. The statute was clear. Also, a criminal statute must be sufficiently definite to give a person of ordinary intelligence who sought to avoid its penalties fair notice of conduct required or prohibited. Wis. Stat. § 342.06(2) only punished a person who knowingly made a false statement in an application for a certificate of title. The jury found defendant knowingly made false statements. Neither the statute nor the application form could be fairly called a trap for the innocent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for making a false statement in three applications for a certificate of title, in connection with his sale of three used cars.
