1490 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Halverson v. Tydrich


No. 89-0621


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


156 Wis. 2d 202; 456 N.W.2d 852; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 304


October 12, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
March 29, 1990, Decided  
March 29, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Richland county: Kent C. Houck, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed insofar as it dismisses the complaint against Richland Hospital and otherwise reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured patient appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Richland County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his medical malpractice against defendants, two doctors and a hospital, on their motions for summary judgment based on the statute of limitations, Wis. Stat. § 893.55(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: The patient's complaint alleged his birth date and that he was admitted to the hospital and treated by the hospital, and the doctors. He first discovered his cause of action more than five years after the last treatment. Each defendant denied negligence and pleaded that the statute of limitations barred his action. The trial court dismissed the complaint on summary judgment motions based on the statute of limitations, pursuant to § 893.55. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment that dismissed the hospital. There was no evidence of concealment by the hospital, and § 893.55(1)(b) applied equally to adults and to minors in barring a suit after five years from the injury. Application of the statute did not violate the patient's constitutional rights as a minor. The court reversed the judgment with respect to the doctors because there were contested issues of fact that would determine whether the patient could rely on the tolling of the statute of limitations allowed in § 893.55(2), where the doctors intentionally concealed their negligent acts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment insofar as it dismissed the complaint against the hospital and otherwise reversed the judgment and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

McManus v. Department of Revenue


No. 89-1126


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


155 Wis. 2d 450; 455 N.W.2d 906; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 241


December 8, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
March 29, 1990, Decided  
March 29, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 11, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Robert A. De Chambeau, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which, in a Wis. Stat. ch. 227 review, affirmed a decision from the Tax Appeals Commission that sustained the decision by respondent Department of Revenue that the estate was not entitled to an income tax credit under the Farmland Preservation Credit statute, Wis. Stat. § 71.09(11) (1977), and declared it to be constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The estate consisted of the interests of the wife of the husband, who farmed land as a joint tenant with his wife. They had household income of $ 180,987, while she had income of $ 6000. She applied for an income tax credit under § 71.09(11), which the Department denied because her household income exceeded the $ 38, 429 statutory threshold. The Commission and then the trial court upheld that determination and the trial court also declared § 71.09(11) constitutional. On appeal, the estate contended that § 71.09(11) was a tax statute within the meaning of the uniformity clause of Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 1. The court affirmed without reaching the constitutional issue because it concluded that Wis. Stat. § 71.09(11) was a relief statute and not a tax statute and therefore was not subject to the uniformity requirement. The court noted that the legislative purpose of § 71.09(11) was to provide economic relief to needy farmland owners whose land was subjected to use restrictions in the nature of restrictive covenants. The estate also failed to show that the fiscal eligibility requirement was an impediment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1492 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Pritchard v. Mead


No. 89-1413


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


155 Wis. 2d 431; 455 N.W.2d 263; 458 N.W.2d 533; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 229


February 7, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
March 28, 1990, Decided  
March 28, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County: Emmanuel J. Vuvunas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff stockholder appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which granted to defendants, a corporation and its former president, motions for summary judgment in the stockholder's action that alleged that the corporation undervalued the stockholder's shares, demanded a declaration of the fair value of his shares, and sought damages in that amount.


OVERVIEW: The stockholder objected to a merger, and after the merger was approved, he made a written demand of the fair value of his stock. The stockholder did not present his stock certificates for notation on them of his demand for payment of fair value as required by Wis. Stat. § 180.72. The trial court held that absent fraud or wrongdoing, § 180.72 established the stockholder's exclusive remedy and because the stockholder did not fully comply with the statute, summary judgment in favor of defendants was proper. On appeal, the court agreed. The stockholder did not plead fraud or other illegality; the crux of his complaint was dissatisfaction with the price offered to him, which did not constitute fraud or illegality. The statute required strict compliance, and the doctrine of substantial compliance did not apply. The dissenting stockholder who failed to observe the requirements of § 180.72 forfeited the right to judicial valuation of his stock. Thus, the statute was accompanied by a penalty for failure to comply, which made strict compliance mandatory. The statute was constitutional because it sought to enforce property rights, not abrogate them, and its provisions were reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of defendants' motions for summary judgment.

 

1493 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hestnes


No. 89-1490


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


155 Wis. 2d 467; 455 N.W.2d 914; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 238



March 22, 1990  
March 22, 1990, Filed  
March 22, 1990, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Mark A. Frankel, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) denying him a sentence credit. Defendant claimed that he had a statutory right to a sentence credit and that the deprivation of that right condemned him to incarceration for a longer time than the period to which he was sentenced, in violation of his right to due process and to be free from double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: In earlier proceedings, defendant sought sentence credit for the time he was hospitalized after his accident and arrest. The court concluded that defendant was not in custody and affirmed denial of defendant's motion for sentence credit. Defendant next brought a postconviction motion challenging, upon constitutional grounds, the denial of sentence credit. The court affirmed denial of sentence credit. There were three elements required for arrest: The suspect's freedom of movement was restricted; the arresting officer intended to restrain the person; and the person under arrest understood that he was in custody. Although defendant was arrested, the court specifically had rejected in the previous proceeding, and again rejected here, defendant's claim that he was in custody. Because defendant did not know of a hold request, the existence of that request was irrelevant. Viewed objectively, a reasonable person in defendant's position would not have understood that he or she was in custody. The court concluded that it reached the correct result in the earlier proceeding and, therefore, rejected defendant's claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying defendant a sentence credit.

 

1494 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Madison v. Baumann


Nos. 89-0452, 89-0453


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


155 Wis. 2d 388; 455 N.W.2d 647; 458 N.W.2d 532; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 217


October 12, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
March 15, 1990, Decided  
March 15, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: James C. Boll, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, the city sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed citations issued by a city police officer to defendants for their violations of the city's anti-noise ordinance, City of Madison, Wis., Madison General Ordinances § 24.04(1), because it was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were professional musicians who were issued citations for violations of § 24.04(1) while playing music one night in a mall area adjacent to a street. Traffic was limited on the street and the city encouraged use of the mall area for the public's recreation and entertainment. On the complaint of a nearby resident, a police officer came to the area, listened to defendants' music, and issued the citations. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court on the basis that § 24.04(1) was unconstitutionally vague. The court found that § 24.04(1) was not overbroad because the "core" conduct it intended to proscribe was the making of any noise that tended to unreasonably disturb the peace and quiet of persons in the vicinity. An overbroad statute was one designed to proscribe activities that were not constitutionally protected but operated to include activities protected by the First Amendment. Section 24.04(1) was unconstitutionally vague because it had no discernible boundaries in its application and did not place noise within boundaries sufficiently distinct for citizens, police, juries, and the courts to determine what conduct it proscribed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

State v. Newman


No. 89-0367-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


155 Wis. 2d 465; 458 N.W.2d 532; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 223



March 13, 1990  
March 13, 1990, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Brown county: Philip M. Kirk, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of various criminal violations of the Wisconsin Uniform Securities law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the president and a stockholder of company. Defendant allegedly misrepresented his company as profitable when it was losing hundreds of thousands of dollars each year. The court rejected defendant's contention that Wis. Stat. §§ 551.21(1), 551.24(5) unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof from the state to defendant. The argument failed because the exemption provided for in the latter statute was not an element of the statutory offense in the former statute. The delegation of legislative authority in the provisions of § 551.63(1) was not unconstitutional. The technical distinction between the types of commercial paper handled by the federal reserve system and those commonly marketed to the general public was best drawn by an agency rather than the legislature. Defendant was not prejudiced by the state's amendment of the charges from party to a crime to principal status because an individual that directly committed the crime was liable under the party-to-the-crime statute. The state was not required to prove intent to defraud before defendant could be convicted of the offenses charged, only a knowing commission of the acts charged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State ex rel. Pirkle Freight Lines, Inc. v. Department of Industry, Labor & Human Relations


No. 89-0093


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


155 Wis. 2d 465; 455 N.W.2d 913; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 195



March 8, 1990  
March 8, 1990, Filed  
March 8, 1990, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1) (b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: ROBERT A. DE CHAMBEAU, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Wisconsin Department of Industry, Labor, and Human Relations appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied defendant department secretary's motion to dismiss plaintiff motor carriers' petition for a writ of prohibition and a complaint for declaratory judgment. The trial court also declared that liability under Wis. Stat. § 102 arose only when an employee sustained an injury.


OVERVIEW: The trial court also declared that under Wis. Stat. § 102.16(3), the Department did not have jurisdiction to conduct hearings on applications from five owner-operator truck drivers. The motor carriers sought to prohibit the Department from conducting hearings on the applications. The truck drivers, who were allegedly employed by the motor carriers, claimed that the motor carriers had unlawfully deducted from their wages premiums for worker's compensation insurance in violation of Wis. Stat. § 102.16(3). None of the applications alleged an injury. On appeal, the court reversed the order of the trial court. The court concluded that an injury was not necessary for a violation of § 102.16(3). Employers violated § 102.16(3) if they solicited, received, or collected any money from an employe or any other person or made any deduction from the employees wages, either directly or indirectly, for the purpose of discharging the employer's duty to maintain worker's compensation insurance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which declared that liability under the applicable statute for unlawfully deducting from employee's wages premiums for worker's compensation insurance arose only when an employee sustained an injury.

1498 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Eau Claire v. Larson


No. 89-1294


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


155 Wis. 2d 467; 455 N.W.2d 914; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 246



March 6, 1990  
March 6, 1990, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Eau Claire county: GREGORY A. PETERSON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction entered by the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County (Wisconsin) for operating a motor vehicle without a valid driver's license, operating an unregistered motor vehicle, and displaying forged license plates. Defendant contended that the trial court lacked jurisdiction and that the laws applied to him were unconstitutional and that he was denied due process and equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by a police officer while driving a car with hand-lettered license plates. Defendant refused to provide identification or vehicle registration. Defendant was convicted for operating a motor vehicle without a valid driver's license, operating an unregistered motor vehicle, and displaying forged license plates. Defendant appealed and contended that he was denied due process and equal protection because he was not promptly notified of the charges against him and was not given an opportunity to be heard. The court affirmed and held that the trial court had jurisdiction under Wis. Stat. § 345.30. Defendant was notified of the charges against him at his initial appearance, six weeks prior to the motions hearing and eight weeks before the trial itself. The court held that it was adequate notice and defendant had sufficient time to prepare. The court also rejected defendant's argument that the vehicle registration and the driver's license requirements were in violation of his right to travel. The court held that not only were the regulations reasonable, they would also survive a compelling state interest analysis and were a reasonable exercise of the police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1499 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schleusner


No. 89-1444-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


154 Wis. 2d 821; 454 N.W.2d 51; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 165


December 14, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
February 27, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Barron county: James C. Eaton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Barron County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of non-support in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.27(2) (1985-86). Defendant argued that the jury instructions unconstitutionally relieved the State of its burden to prove intent and ability to pay and that there was insufficient evidence to support the guilty verdict.


OVERVIEW: When defendant and his ex-wife divorced, the wife was awarded custody of the couple's three children, and defendant was ordered to pay monthly child support. When defendant made no child support payments, he was charged with non-support in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.27(2). He was convicted following a jury trial, and he appealed his conviction. In affirming, the court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction. Evidence that defendant voluntarily and without reasonable excuse quit two jobs shortly after learning that child support payments would be withheld, and that defendant made no payments for an 11-month period despite a court order mandating that make such payments, was indicative of defendant's intent not to pay. Further, the fact that defendant received public assistance did not require the jury to find that defendant lacked the ability to make the required child support payments, and the evidence was sufficient to permit the jury to conclude that defendant avoided employment for the purpose of intentionally avoiding his support obligations.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

1500 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Maxson


No. 89-1026-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


154 Wis. 2d 867; 455 N.W.2d 678; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 108



February 14, 1990, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Ozaukee county: WARREN A. GRADY, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Ozaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him upon his plea of no contest to the charge of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver following the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence. On appeal, defendant challenged the denial of his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that a pat-down search of his person violated Wis. Stat. §§ 968.24 and 968.25. The court concluded that the pat-down search was legal. Officers were executing a search warrant in the apartment of a third party when defendant and another man knocked on the door. A plain-clothes officer invited the men inside. Officers told both men to keep their hands at their sides. In response, defendant looked into his leather jacket and started to reach for the inside breast pocket. The officer warned defendant to move his hands away from his jacket. The officers conducted a pat-down search of defendant for weapons but found none. The officers then requested identification from both men. As defendant removed his wallet, he also appeared to push something into the inside breast pocket of his jacket. The officer then opened defendant's jacket and saw a baggie, which later proved to contain cocaine. The court ruled that the second pat-down search was proper. Defendant's furtive gestures toward the inside of his jacket pocket would reasonably suggest that defendant possessed a weapon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In Interest of S.S.K.


No. 89-1254


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


154 Wis. 2d 868; 455 N.W.2d 678; 458 N.W.2d 533; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 123



February 7, 1990, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Waukesha county: KATHRYN W. FOSTER, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which granted an extension order sought by respondent Waukesha County Human Services Department to continue the placement of the mother's minor child outside the home.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted an extension order for the removal of a minor child because it determined that the mother had not made adequate progress necessary to allow the return of the child. The mother asserted that: (1) the trial court did not have jurisdiction to enter the extension because its jurisdiction expired on the date in the original order; (2) Wis. Stat. § 48.365 was unconstitutionally vague; (3) the Department failed to make reasonable efforts to provide services to the mother; and (4) the trial court should have recused itself because for partiality. The court affirmed the extension and determined that: (1) the trial court had jurisdiction to hear the extension order because the expiration of the prior order was clearly specified by the date of the original order; (2) the extension order statute was not unconstitutionally vague because the criteria for extension of the order were well documented in the law; (3) the Department showed that it attempted to provide services but the mother refused to cooperate with requests; and (4) there was no demonstration that a complaint against the trial court on another issue rendered him impartial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the trial court that an extension order sought by the department to continue the placement of the mother's minor child outside the home.

 

1502 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Elkhorn


No. 89-1071


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


154 Wis. 2d 523; 454 N.W.2d 808; 1990 Wisc. App. LEXIS 14



January 24, 1990, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth county: JOHN R. RACE, Judge. Affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Proceeding pro se, plaintiff landlord appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his complaint against defendants, a city and its light and water commission, and which found that the landlord's suit was frivolous.


OVERVIEW: The city passed an ordinance assessing a delinquent utility bill belonging to the landlord's tenant as an amount due on the landlord's real estate taxes. The landlord filed an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 as a result. The suit was dismissed in the trial court, in federal court, and again in the trial court when it was refiled. The landlord contended that res judicata did not bar his suit and that certain of his claims were not addressed. The court agreed that it was error to fail to address certain claims but otherwise upheld the trial court's judgment. First, res judicata prevented the landlord from subjecting the city to repetitive litigation. In any event, the existence of a state remedy precluded his § 1983 claim as a legal cause of action. Second, no special benefit was required for assessment of the delinquent utility bill and the ordinance was not unlawful under Wis. Stat. § 66.60. Third, the landlord could not establish beyond a reasonable doubt that the ordinance denied him equal protection of the laws. Finally, the landlord's knowledge of the appellate decisions in his previous cases should have led him to conclude that further pursuit of his claim was frivolous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the trial court's judgment finding two of the landlord's claims to be frivolous which the trial court did not previously address. The court affirmed the judgment in all other respects. The cause was remanded for an allocation of costs and attorney fees for the frivolous portion of the action in the trial court and on appeal.

 

1503 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Schreiber v. Bennett


No. 89-0435


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


153 Wis. 2d 773; 452 N.W.2d 586; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1188



December 26, 1989, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rusk county: FREDERICK A. HENDERSON, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice action, appellants, the child and the parents, challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Rusk County (Wisconsin), dismissing the child and parents' medical malpractice claim.


OVERVIEW: The child suffered brain damage immediately after birth. It was determined that child suffered from neonatal hypoglycemia. The parents alleged that they contacted several attorneys and other physicians but no one was able to assist in determining the cause of the hypoglycemia. Some 24 years later, the parents received a medical report indicating that the neonatal hypoglycemia was the result of medical malpractice. The trial court dismissed the action as time barred. On appeal the court affirmed. First, the court held that the claim was filed well beyond the three-year statute of limitation period. The court further noted that the action was not filed within one year after the child reached the age of majority pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 330.205 (1959). Second, the court held that even if the discovery rule was applicable, the parents failed to exercise reasonable diligence in ascertaining the nature of the child's brain damage. The court concluded that where an otherwise healthy baby was brain-injured after birth by a known illness contracted while under the care of a physician in a hospital, reasonable diligence suggested further inquiry than what occurred in the present case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Shannon & Riordan v. Board of Zoning Appeals


No. 89-0466


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


153 Wis. 2d 713; 451 N.W.2d 479; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1179


August 1, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
December 20, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not disposed of at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Janine P. Geske, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied certiorari of an adverse decision from respondent, the Board of Zoning Appeals of Milwaukee, which denied the property owners a variance for their three properties pursuant to Milwaukee Code of Ordinances § 295-14-1 and Wis. Stat. § 62.23(7)(i).


OVERVIEW: The property owners filed a variance request with the Zoning Board, which the Zoning Board denied. The property owners filed a request for a writ of certiorari with the trial court, which the trial court denied. The property owners filed an appeal. In affirming the trial court's order, the court held that the Zoning Board operated within its discretionary authority when it denied the property owners' variances. The court found that the Zoning Board gave legitimate consideration to the concerns for the public health, safety, morals, and general welfare of the community and therefore concluded its denial of the variances was not arbitrary or unreasonable. The court stated that the ordinance had a reasonable and rational basis that called for the type of housing requested in the variance to be dispersed throughout the community without any over intensification in limited areas. The court concluded that the property owners failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the legislation violated the Equal Protection Clause. The court found that the property owners failed to cite any authority for their due process argument and thus deemed it abandoned.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order.

Saenz v. Murphy


No. 88-2084


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


153 Wis. 2d 660; 451 N.W.2d 780; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1220


June 8, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
December 14, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: George A.W. Northrup, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded for determination of damages.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted a summary judgment dismissing the inmate's complaint in favor of defendants, the superintendent, the hearing officer, and the committee member. The inmate sought compensatory and punitive damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, declaratory relief under 28 U.S.C.S. §§ 2201-2202, and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that defendants denied him procedural due process after an altercation with a correctional officer and placement in temporary lockup. The court concluded that defendants were not sufficiently involved in placing and continuing the inmate in temporary lockup for liability under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court opined that defendants reasonably should have known that the inmate was entitled to adequate notice and an opportunity to present a defense, calling witnesses of his choice. The court pointed out, however, that the inmate had no constitutional right to an advocate of his choosing. The court held that the inmate had more than 24 hours to prepare a defense, but he was denied due process in not being provided with a statement from his requested witness, and he was entitled to a trial on damages. The court determined that the inmate received adequate notice of his disciplinary hearing under Wis. Admin. Code §§ HSS 303.76(1), (3), 303.81, so he was not entitled to declaratory relief. The inmate did not claim any continuing, present adverse effects from his past exposure to defendants' alleged illegal conduct, so the court rejected his claim for injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in part, holding that the inmate was entitled as a matter of law to judgment that the hearing officer violated his due process rights to call a witness in his defense, and the cause was remanded to determine damages. In all other respects, the court concluded that defendants were entitled to summary judgment.

 

1506 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In Interest of C.H.


No. 89-0823


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


153 Wis. 2d 774; 452 N.W.2d 586; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1236



December 6, 1989, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Kenosha county: DAVID M. BASTIAN, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged orders of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which, after a jury trial, found her son to be a child in need of protection and services under Wis. Stat. § 48.13(3) and (10), transferred for one year the custody of her son to the Kenosha County Department of Social Services, and denied her motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: The son was found to be a child in need of protection and services under Wis. Stat. § 48.13(3) and (10) based on evidence that he was not getting sufficient nutrition, his home was not sufficiently heated, his sister threatened him with a knife and punched and pulled on his penis and genital area, and he was raped by a cousin. The court affirmed the orders of the trial court. Section 48.13(3) was not overbroad. The statute was jurisdictional and the relevant inquiry was not necessarily whether the parent was negligent. The statute also was not fatally vague. The terms used in § 48.13 were not so uncertain that a person of ordinary intelligence must guess at their meaning. Likewise, the statute did not fail for not precisely delineating a parent's duty of care. The focus of the children's code was the best interest of the child. Moreover, it was not necessary for a nexus between the son's abuse and any act or omission by his mother to have been shown. Because there was ample evidence of sexual abuse, the court determined that there was no need to decide whether sufficient evidence supported the jury's finding of physical abuse.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

State v. Richard

Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Iowa County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of three counts of burglary, three counts of theft, and two counts of criminal damage, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 943.10(1)(a), 943.20(1), and 943.01(1). Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in refusing to suppress the fruits of her arrest, which she claimed was illegal.


OVERVIEW: A bowling alley in Iowa County was burglarized. Two individuals followed the suspect's car, which travelled from Iowa County to the neighboring Grant County. The individuals stopped the car contacted the police. A deputy sheriff from Iowa County had received a dispatch concerning the burglary and proceeded to the car's location, which was about 50 feet into Grant County. Defendant was taken into custody. A subsequent inventory of the car produced bags containing money that were identified as having been stolen from businesses in Iowa County. Defendant claimed that because the arresting officer was outside his jurisdiction at the time he arrested defendant, the arrest was illegal, and the evidence should have been suppressed. The trial court denied the motion on the grounds that the officer was in fresh pursuit under Wis. Stat. § 175.40 and had probable cause to arrest defendant. The court agreed and held that even if there was no fresh pursuit, the evidence was not obtained in violation of defendant's constitutional rights, and no statute required suppression.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

John v. John


No. 88-1507


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


153 Wis. 2d 343; 450 N.W.2d 795; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1136


September 5, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
November 24, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Michael J. Barron, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former director challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) in favor of respondent officers permanently enjoining the executive from serving as director and trustee of the nonprofit corporation due to abuse of public trust, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 776.32. The former director also sought review of the award of equitable disgorgement and interest.


OVERVIEW: The former director was permanently enjoined from serving as director or trustee of the nonprofit corporation and ordered to pay disgorgement and interest because he committed gross misconduct and breached his fiduciary duties. On review, the court held that the trial court did not clearly err when it ruled that the corporation was not a religious corporation, as defined in Wis. Stat. §§ 776.46, 182.030, or Wis. Stat. ch. 187. Rather, it was a charitable corporation that made grants to religious organizations. Therefore the corporation was not excluded from the trial court's subject matter jurisdiction over the matter pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 776.32(4). The court then found that the injunction did not interfere with the former director's constitutionally-protected right to free exercise of religion. With regard to the former director's culpability under § 776.32(4), the court concluded that his abuse of power and fraud were contemplated under the term "gross misconduct," and were not mere exercises of business judgment. The court rejected the former director's claim for indemnification from the corporation, and affirmed the judgment in favor of respondent officers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the officers permanently enjoining the former director from serving as director and trustee of the nonprofit corporation and ordering the award of equitable disgorgement and interest.

State v. Albert


No. 89-0969-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


153 Wis. 2d 399; 451 N.W.2d 806; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1090



November 16, 1989, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Jefferson county: HAROLD H. EBERHARDT, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin), which entered a jury verdict convicting him of one count of operating a motor vehicle after revocation of his operating privilege and one count of operating a motor vehicle after suspension of his operating privilege in violation of Wis. Stat. § 343.44(1) and denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: At trial, defendant admitted that he knew that he did not have a valid driver's license at the time of his two arrests; he argued, however, that he had a valid chauffeur's license in his possession and that he did not know that it was suspended. The trial court instructed the jury that a valid chauffeur's license was acceptable only when the driver was operating a vehicle in the performance of his or her duties as a chauffeur. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions. Defendant was not entitled to a new trial in the interest of justice under Wis. Stat. § 752.35 based on the jury instruction. The trial court instructed the jury several times that the State had the burden of proof and a different result would not likely result on retrial were the jury specifically instructed that the State had the burden of proof on the chauffeur's license issue. The arresting officers testified that defendant did not have a valid chauffeur's license and there was no evidence that defendant was acting in the performance of his chauffeur duties when he was arrested.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order of the trial court.

State v. Clement


No. 89-1191


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


153 Wis. 2d 287; 450 N.W.2d 789; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1075


October 3, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
November 15, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: John F. Foley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) of first-degree sexual assault, Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(b), and kidnapping while armed, Wis. Stat. §§ 940.31, 939.63. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06, he moved the trial court to withdraw his guilty plea to the kidnapping charge. His motion was denied, and he sought review of the order.


OVERVIEW: The victim was walking to her place of employment when defendant approached her from behind and placed a knife to her throat. He then took the victim to an isolated area and sexually assaulted her. He initially pleaded guilty to first-degree sexual assault and kidnapping while armed and was convicted. He later sought to withdraw his guilty plea to the kidnapping charge. He appealed after the trial court denied his motion. On review, the court upheld the order. The court rejected defendant's argument that his conduct did not fulfill the element of kidnapping prescribing the intent to hold the victim to "service against his will, " and that because he misunderstood the scope of this element, his plea was not made knowingly and voluntarily. The court ruled that the word "service," as it was used in Wis. Stat. § 940.31, included acts done at the command of another and that it clearly embraced sexual acts performed at the command of another. The court found that it was clear that defendant not only intended to hold his victim to service against her will but actually did so. The court held that defendant knowingly and voluntarily made his plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

The mother asserted that the trial court erred by failing to make an independent determination regarding her unfitness as a parent in terminating her parental rights.

The court found that § 48.424(4) was not unconstitutional because the object sought by the State was the protection of the rights and well-being of children and the statutory means for terminating the parental rights had a real and substantial relation to protecting children. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

1512 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Burlington N. R. Co. v. Superior


No. 88-1794


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


153 Wis. 2d 206; 450 N.W.2d 486; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1107


October 12, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
November 7, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Douglas County: Douglas S. Moodie, Reserve Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In tax proceedings, appellants, a railroad company and a corporation, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Douglas County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment in their favor against respondent city but awarded them post-judgment interest at a rate of five percent under former Wis. Stat. § 74.73(1r) rather than at the requested 12-percent rate under Wis. Stat. § 815.05(8).


OVERVIEW: The city was determined to be liable for tax refunds for taxes that were collected but later determined to be unconstitutional. On appeal from the trial court's order awarding postjudgment interest under former Wis. Stat. § 74.73(1r), the court reversed. Section 74.73(1r) applied to unlawful taxes, not to taxes declared unconstitutional. The court determined that Wis. Stat. § 815.05(8), which provided for a postjudgment interest rate of 12 percent, applied. The court rejected the city's contention that Wis. Stat. § 66.09, which applied to governmental bodies, applied, and that the legal rate of interest prescribed under Wis. Stat. § 138.04 prescribed a rate of five percent. Wis. Stat. § 66.09 mentioned nothing about the rate of interest to be paid. Furthermore, conflicts between statutes were not favored and would not be held to exist if the statutes could otherwise be reasonably construed. Therefore, the court determined that Wis. Stat. § 815.05(8) controlled.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded for an order directing post-judgment interest payments at a rate of 12 percent.

State v. Scherreiks


Nos. 88-1733-CR, 88-1734-CR, 88-1735-CR

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgments and an order of the Circuit Court for Monroe County: James W. Rice, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgments and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Wisconsin) convicting and sentencing defendant as a result of his guilty pleas to the charges of attempted criminal damage to property, party to a crime, intimidation of a witness, party to the crime, and second-degree murder, party to the crime. Defendant was sentenced to the maximum sentences available and his postconviction motion was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to the charges of attempted criminal damage to property, intimidation of a witness, and second-degree murder, all of which were designated as party to a crime. He was sentenced to nearly maximum sentences allowed for each crime. Defendant sought modification of his sentences in a postconviction relief motion. The motion was denied. Although the trial court failed to timely decide defendant's postconviction motions, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 809.30(2)(i), such a failure was not grounds for remand. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not err when imposing the maximum two and one-half-year sentence for attempted criminal damage to property, as defendant affirmatively approved the sentence and could not attack it on appeal. The court rejected defendant's contention that his first offender status required consideration, as the gravity of the offense reduced that first-offender status to insignificance. The allegations of cruel and unusual punishment, contrary to U.S. Const. amend 8 and Wis. Const. art. I, sec. 6, were not supported, and therefore, not reviewed on appeal. The victim impact statements were properly used in sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Sturgis v. Neenah Bd. of Canvassers


No. 89-0912


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


153 Wis. 2d 193; 450 N.W.2d 481; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1098


October 4, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
November 1, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County: William E. Crane, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant write-in candidate sought review of a judgment of he Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which found in favor of respondents, the board of canvassers of a town, in the write-in candidate's action challenging the board's invalidation of disputed election ballots pursuant to its interpretation of Wis. Stat. § 7.50(2)(f).


OVERVIEW: The write-in candidate argued that votes that had been cast for him at the election for town chairman had been erroneously disallowed because the board of canvassers of the town had determined that because stickers bearing the write-in candidate's name had been pasted on the face of the ballots by voters, covering the name of the other candidate on the ballot, the disputed ballots had to be invalidated, which decision was affirmed by the circuit court. Reversing, the court held that § 7.50(2)(f)'s prohibition against placing sticker votes over other names on the ballot was applicable only to straight party ballots. Therefore, because the election in question was nonpartisan, the votes at issue had been erroneously disallowed and the town clerk was required to issue a certificate of election to the write-in candidate. In reaching this conclusion, the court attempted to ascertain the legislature's intent in light of the strong preference to give effect to the will of the electorate when construing election laws.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and remanded the cause with directions that the trial court reverse the board's determination and order the town clerk to issue a certificate of election to the write-in candidate.

 

1515 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Nelson Bros. Furniture Corp. v. Department of Revenue


No. 88-1647


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


152 Wis. 2d 746; 449 N.W.2d 328; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 959


May 5, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
October 26, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: James C. Boll, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporate taxpayer appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which upheld the state tax appeals commission's decision to uphold respondent Wisconsin Department of Revenue's tax determination against the corporate taxpayer, assessing a greater amount of franchise tax liability.


OVERVIEW: The Department determined that the corporate taxpayer had underpaid its state franchise taxes. The commission upheld the determination. On appeal, the trial court affirmed the decision. The corporate taxpayer appealed from that judgment, arguing that the Department had abused its discretion in directing a change in the corporate taxpayer's accounting methods which led to increased state franchise tax liability. The court affirmed, holding that its review was limited to whether the commission's determination was arbitrary or unreasonable. The court concluded that the Department reasonably and properly exercised its discretion to direct the change in accounting practices. The court was not convinced that the corporate taxpayer's recoupment claim was a grievance to the assessment. The court found that it was an equitable claim for an offset to the reassessment which was not barred from the commission's consideration by the taxpayer's failure to argue it to the Department. The court also noted that the apportionment formula resulted in an increase in the corporate taxpayer's state tax liability but that increases of 15 to 43 percent had been upheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to uphold the Department of revenue's tax determination against the corporate taxpayer, assessing a greater amount of franchise tax liability.

Beloit Corp. v. Labor & Industry Review Com.


No. 88-1885


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


152 Wis. 2d 579; 449 N.W.2d 299; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 968


April 3, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
October 5, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Rock county: J. Richard Long, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employer appealed from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of defendant Labor and Industry Review Commission (LIRC) awarding educational vocational rehabilitation benefits to defendant employee. The employer contended that the LIRC's decision was unreasonable because it enabled the employee to improve upon his preinjury earning potential.


OVERVIEW: The employee lost the use of his left arm in an industrial accident while working for the employer. He was only 19 years old at the time and attending a community college part time. The LIRC's determination extended educational vocational rehabilitation benefits to allow the employee to obtain a degree in mechanical engineering. The court held that the LIRC properly accepted another state's determination that the employee was eligible for the program because the employee was a resident of the other state and the program was part of the Federal Rehabilitation Act. Instructional benefits under the Act were administered by the agency in the state where the handicapped person resided. However, the court reviewed the LIRC's decision for reasonableness. The employer argued that it was unreasonable and violated the provision of Wis. Admin. Code § Ind. 80.49(4) that did not allow training beyond 40 weeks if it was primarily to improve the employee's preinjury earning capacity. The court held that LIRC's conclusion that additional training was warranted was reasonable because at 19 he had not yet established his full earning capacity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order of the lower court.

State v. Braun


Nos. 88-1065-CR, 88-2049-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


152 Wis. 2d 500; 449 N.W.2d 851; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 958


August 1, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
September 26, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Joseph P. Callan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment vacated and order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of bail jumping.


OVERVIEW: A special prosecutor was appointed under Wis. Stat. § 59.44(1) in anticipation of charging defendant and others with criminal trespass to a medical facility. Defendant was released on bail with the condition of staying away from the medical facility. Defendant was found protesting near the medical facility and was arrested. The special prosecutor then prosecuted defendant for bail jumping. Defendant was convicted and sentenced for bail jumping. On appeal, he argued that the special prosecutor was not authorized to prosecute him for such offense. The appellate court vacated and reversed his conviction. The special prosecutor's order of appointment invested him with all the powers of the district attorney for a limited purpose, namely, the prosecution of defendant and the others under Wis. Stat. § 943.145, as a result of their arrest at the medical clinic. Since the special prosecutor had no authority to venture beyond that mandate, defendant's conviction for bail jumping was vacated. The appellate court also found that the trial court's bail condition which impinged upon defendant's right to free speech was improper.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of bail jumping was vacated and the order was reversed.

 

1518 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Steadman


No. 89-0233-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


152 Wis. 2d 293; 448 N.W.2d 267; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 923


July 11, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
September 13, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Marvin C. Holz, Reserve Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), that convicted him for first-degree sexual assault, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(d) (1985-86), and two counts of sexual exploitation of a child, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.203(2) (1985-86).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his convictions for first-degree sexual assault, and sexual exploitation of a child. On appeal, he challenged the propriety of the investigation and search warrant that yielded the evidence supporting these convictions. He urged three arguments for dismissal of the action: (1) that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction because a necessary element of § 940.203(4) (1985-86), importation, was manufactured by a government sting operation that set up the search situation; (2) that the conduct of the government in securing his conviction was outrageous to the extent that it denied him due process; and, (3) that the search warrant did not allege probable cause and was insufficiently particular. The gist of defendant's due process argument was that the government, aware that mere possession of pornography was no offense, contrived his importation of pornography. The court disagreed with defendant's contentions, and affirmed. The court found no due process violation, noting that although the government provided the opportunity, it was defendant who committed the crime. The court also found that there was probable cause to issue the warrant against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction against defendant for first-degree sexual assault and sexual exploitation of a child.

 

1519 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Raymond


No. 89-0327-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


152 Wis. 2d 405; 449 N.W.2d 337; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 864



September 12, 1989, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Brown county: PETER J. NAZE, Judge. Reversed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant prisoner appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to dismiss a Minnesota detainer on a charge of aggravated robbery. Defendant contended that his rights under the Interstate Agreement on Detainers Act were violated because he was not brought before a judge in a timely manner as required under Wis. Stat. § 976.06, and he was not informed of his rights to a hearing within 30 days.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a prisoner at a Wisconsin correctional facility. An interstate detainer charging aggravated robbery was lodged against him by Minnesota authorities and was received by the prison on April 5, 1988. A hearing was held on July 1, 1988. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the detainer, which the trial court denied. Defendant appealed and contended that his procedural rights under the Interstate Agreement on Detainers Act were violated because he was not brought before a judge "forthwith" as required by Wis. Stat. § 976.06, and he was not adequately informed of his right to a hearing within 30 days of receipt of the detainer. The court reversed and held that the hearing was neither waived nor held within 30 days from the filing of the detainer. The court held that there was no indication that defendant knew of the 30 day requirement and therefore he could not have waived it. The court held that the statute unambiguously required the trial court to begin the 30 days from the time the detainer was filed. The court dismissed the detainer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and dismissed the detainer.

1521 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. McKenzie


No. 89-0013


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


151 Wis. 2d 775; 446 N.W.2d 77; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 733


June 7, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
July 26, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of conviction and from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: George A.W. Northrup, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin). The trial court convicted defendant of lewd and lascivious behavior and of obstructing an officer, and it sentenced defendant as a repeater under Wis. Stat. § 939.62(1). Defendant also appealed the denial of his post-conviction motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the repeat offender statute. Defendant argued § 939.62 violated the Equal Protection Clause. The trial court found § 939.62 was constitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed. In affirming, the court held that under an equal protection analysis, the court would uphold a statute if a rational basis existed to support the classification, unless the statute impinged on a fundamental right or created a classification based on a suspect criterion. The rational basis test was applied. That test provided that equal protection of the law was denied only where the legislature made irrational or arbitrary classification. The basic test was not whether some inequality resulted from the classification, but whether there existed any reasonable basis to justify the classification. The court held that the decision to treat repeat offenders differently served a legitimate governmental interest. Thus, § 939.62 was not irrational because it subjected all repeat misdemeanor offenders to the same maximum sentence. Further, the court held that § 939.62 was not unreasonable merely because different results could be reached in its application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1522 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


No. 88-1704


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


151 Wis. 2d 784; 447 N.W.2d 394; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 680



July 26, 1989, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: ROBERT DE CHAMBEAU, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which confirmed an arbitration award and dismissed his medical payments and exemplary damage claims against defendant insurer.


OVERVIEW: The insured and his friend were on the way to a tavern when the insured was struck by a hit-and-run unidentified driver. The two young men were taken to the emergency room. The nurse testified that she asked the friend what had happened and was told that the insured was running up behind a car, grabbing its bumper, and being towed behind it over icy streets. The arbitration panel found that the insured failed to meet his burden of proving that he was struck by an automobile whose driver was negligent or that any contact with an automobile was causally related to his injuries. The trial court granted the insurer's motion to confirm the award. The insured argued that award should be vacated because the arbitrators disregarded the law in failing to grant his motion to exclude the nurse's testimony. In affirming the award, the court found that the nurse's testimony was admissible since it was relating a prior inconsistent statement of a witness and that Wis. Stat. § 904.12(1) did not prevent admission of an injured witness's statement. The panel's finding that the insured failed to prove he had been struck by a vehicle was conclusive and defeated his claim for medical payments.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

State v. Miller


No. 88-2375-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


151 Wis. 2d 785; 447 N.W.2d 395; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 669

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal trespass to a medical facility in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.145 in connection with his entry into an abortion clinic in order to protest. Second, he argued that § 943.145 was unconstitutional because it gave disparate treatment to labor and non-labor related speech, sought to suppress a particular viewpoint, and created a heckler's veto. STATE v. VON LOH


Nos. 89-0770-CR-NM, 89-0771-CR-NM, 89-0772-CR-NM


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


151 Wis. 2d 787; 447 N.W.2d 396; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 679



July 13, 1989, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Dane county: MICHAEL B. TORPHY, JR., Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of three misdemeanor charges of unlawful use of a telephone, violations of Wis. Stat. § 947.012(2). Counsel for defendant filed a no merit report pursuant to Anders and Wis. Stat. § 809.32, and defendant did not respond to the report.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded no contest to unlawful use of a telephone. After his probation was revoked, he was sentenced to 33 months in prison as a repeat offender. In a consolidated appeal, after reviewing the record, the court concluded that any further proceedings would have been frivolous and without arguable merit. The trial court complied with the requirements set forth in Bangert to insure defendant had knowingly and voluntarily pleaded no contest. The trial court properly exercised its discretion in sentencing defendant after his probation was revoked. Committing these types of harassment offenses had become habitual for defendant, he had not responded to treatment or otherwise benefited from probation, and his continuing criminal acts posed a threat to society. These were proper factors to consider, and they justified sentencing defendant as a repeater. Defendant received effective assistance of counsel. His counsel had no choice but to accept the plea agreement in light of the evidence. Defendant's subsequent revocation and imprisonment was in no way attributable to errors of counsel. Any challenge to the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 947.012(2) would have failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful use of a telephone and relieved his appellate counsel of further representation of him on appeal.

CITY OF STEVENS POINT v. PLISKA


Nos. 88-1405, 88-1406, 88-1407


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


151 Wis. 2d 783; 447 N.W.2d 394; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 721



July 13, 1989, Decided and Filed; Review Denied October 10, 1989


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments and orders of the circuit court for Portage county: FREDERICK FLEISHAUER, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgments and orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner one sought review of a default judgment of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin), which assessed a forfeiture against him and review of an order refusing to vacate the default judgment entered in favor of respondent city. Appellant homeowner two appealed from two judgments convicting him of violating the same ordinance as well as orders denying him relief from both judgments.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners were cited for violating an ordinance that prohibited homeowners from keeping excessive amounts of garbage on their property. A default judgment was entered against homeowner one when he failed to appear in court and homeowner two lost at trial. Both homeowners appealed and the court affirmed. The court declined to hear the overbreadth challenge because the homeowners did not show any danger that the city's ordinance would infringe upon any first amendment protections of individuals not before the court. The trial court did not err when it determined that the phrase "for each day the violation exists," applied to both the forfeiture and the jail sentence provisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the city.

 

1526 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Thompkins


No. 88-0952


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


151 Wis. 2d 556; 445 N.W.2d 58; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 634



June 21, 1989, Decided; Review Granted September 13, 1989


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine county: DENNIS J. FLYNN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his motion to modify child support arrears. The trial court concluded that Wis. Stat. § 767.32(lm) prohibited it from modifying the father's arrears, and rejected the father's claim that § 767.32(lm) was unconstitutional. Respondents were the county child support agency and an individual.


OVERVIEW: The father claimed that Wis. Stat. § 767.32(lm) was unconstitutional, pointing out that prior to its enactment he had a cause of action under Wis. Stat. § 767.32(1) to request a modification of his accumulated child support arrears. The father claimed that if Wis. Stat. § 767.32(lm) deprived him of that cause of action, he was denied due process. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order. The court noted that divorce was a statutory proceeding, and the rights and remedies of the parties were limited to those provided by the statutes. The exclusive procedure for revision of child support provisions was also provided by statute.Because the father's cause of action to modify his support arrears was created by statute, the state was free to eliminate it, unless by doing so the father was deprived of a vested right. The court held that child support payments were not vested rights; statutory changes could alter them. The court noted that the father was not deprived of life, liberty, or property by application of the revision of judgment statute to the child support provision, hence § 767.32(lm) had not deprived the father of a constitutionally protected interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

In Interest of D.S.

1528 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Woodmansee v. Woodmansee


No. 89-0270


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


151 Wis. 2d 242; 444 N.W.2d 393; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 580


May 4, 1989, Orally argued  
June 6, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Rusk County: Frederick A. Henderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Rusk County (Wisconsin), which discharged respondent father's child support arrearages and reduced his future monthly obligations.


OVERVIEW: Wis. Stat. § 767.32(1) gave a trial judge the discretion to modify or eliminate child support arrearages. Wis. Stat. § 767. 32(1m), effective in 1987, limited the trial judge's power. A trial judge could not revise the amount of child support due prior to the date that notice was given of an action to revise the amount of support. The father was in arrears for the period between 1980 and 1988. The trial judge reduced the amount of the arrearage and reduced his monthly obligation. On appeal, the mother asserted that § 767.32(1m) removed the trial judge's power to reduce or cancel child support arrearages. The court agreed and concluded that arrearages were included in the statutory language of child support due. It held that the statute was unambiguous, but even if it was ambiguous, § 767.32(1m) was enacted to ensure that the State continued to receive federal funds. 42 U.S.C.S. § 654 required states to have laws necessary to improve child support enforcement effectiveness. 42 U.S.C.S. § 666(a)(9)(C) specified that such laws were required to provide that a child support judgment was not subject to retroactive modification. The application of the statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded with directions to the trial court to reinstate the father's child support arrearages.

Bedward v. Trempealeau County Mut. Ins. Co.


No. 88-2304


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


151 Wis. 2d 785; 447 N.W.2d 395; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 718



June 6, 1989, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Trempealeau county: RICHARD D. GALSTAD, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a judgment of the circuit court for Trempealeau County (Wisconsin), which was entered on a jury verdict in favor of defendant employers in the employee's personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: The employee, who worked on a farm, was assisting another employee in removing a tractor cab's window when the window exploded in his face and injured his eye. He brought a personal injury action against the employers. The evidence at trial centered on the tractor and its maintenance. The employee requested a jury instruction stating that an employer had a common law duty to provide a safe place of employment. The trial court declined to give the instruction. The trial court submitted standard negligence and causation instructions and an instruction stating that an employer had a duty to provide and maintain a safe motor vehicle as well as to repair it. The jury returned a verdict for the employers. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly declined to give the employee's requested instruction because the overall meaning communicated by the instructions submitted to the jury was a correct statement of law in light of the evidence adduced at trial. The court also held that the employee failed to preserve for review his argument that the farming exclusion from Wis. Stat. § 101.11 was unconstitutional because he did not raise the issue until his postverdict motion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Sheehan v. Otte


No. 88-1945


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


150 Wis. 2d 947; 444 N.W.2d 66; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 441



May 23, 1989, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Burnett county. HARRY F. GUNDERSEN, Judge. Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded for further proceedings. No costs to either party on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the co-personal representative of an estate, challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Burnett County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the personal representative's action against respondent adjoining property owner upon finding that the personal representative's claim was barred by res judicata, that the adjoining property owner was protected by Wis. Stat. § 30.122, and that the res judicata defense was not frivolous.


OVERVIEW: The adjoining property owner, who owned land on the lake near the estate's property, filled in an artificial ditch that had drained the lake. The filling caused the lake level to rise the flood the estate property. The Department of Natural Resources ordered the adjoining property owner to restore and maintain the ditch at his own expense. The trial court affirmed the agency decision. The estate brought an action for damages against the adjoining property owner. The trial court dismissed on grounds that the prior review of the agency decision was res judicata and barred the action and that Wis. Stat. § 30.122 protected the adjoining property owner. The estate contended that res judicata did not bar the action, that the adjoining property owner's defense of res judicata was frivolous, and that § 30.122 did not protect him from liability. On appeal, the court affirmed the ruling that the res judicata defense was not frivolous, but reversed the dismissal and finding that the adjoining property owner was protected. The court held that Wis. Stat. ch. 227 regulatory review had no substantive connection to the civil suit for property damage and was consequently not res judicata.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the ruling that the res judicata defense was not frivolous, but reversed the rulings that the proceeding was res judicata and that the adjoining property owner was protected from liability by statute.

 

1531 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Richards v. Cullen


No. 88-2419


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


150 Wis. 2d 935; 442 N.W.2d 574; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 514


April 3, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
May 18, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Susan Steingass, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Secretary of the Wisconsin Department of Health and Social Services, appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which declared Wis. Admin. Code § HHS 309.466(1) unconstitutional in plaintiff prisoner's action challenging the validity of § HHS 309.466(1) and ordered the immediate release of the funds in the prisoner's account.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was serving a life sentence. He filed a complaint challenging § HHS 309.466(1), which allowed prison officials to withhold 15 percent of all money earned or acquired by inmates, up to a maximum of $ 500, and to deposit all such funds into a "Mandatory Release Account" for the individual inmate's use upon release from prison. In his complaint he argued that because of he was serving a life sentence, § HHS 309.466(1) violated his right to due process and equal protection of the law. The trial court entered judgment for the prisoner. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. There was no basis for any claim of a substantive due process violation because the prisoner had no inherent or absolute interest in his personal property while incarcerated. There was no procedural due process violation with regard to his limited property interest in the funds. There was no equal protection violation even though he was a lifer with no mandatory release date. The dual goals of promoting the successful reintegration of released prisoners into society and of preserving the limited state funds available for operation of the prison system were valid and substantial governmental aims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

State v. Mayes


No. 88-1838-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


150 Wis. 2d 947; 444 N.W.2d 66; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 473
