PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha county: MICHAEL FISHER, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to suppress evidence and from a judgment convicting him of operating a motor vehicle after his driver's license was revoked, fourth offense, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 343.44(1).


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed defendant's vehicle traveling slower than the speed limit. The car caught his attention because he could not see a driver behind the steering wheel. The officer stopped the vehicle because he suspected that it was being driven by an unlicensed juvenile. When stopped, defendant could not produce a driver's license, and the officer determined that defendant's license had been revoked. Defendant pleaded not guilty to the charge against him. In addition, he filed a motion with the trial court to suppress evidence gleaned after the stop was made. Defendant argued that the stop was unconstitutional because the officer lacked reasonable suspicion to believe that a crime was being committed, making the stop unwarranted. The trial court denied defendant's motion. Defendant then pleaded guilty to the charge. The trial court adjudged him guilty and sentenced him to 90 days imprisonment with Huber privileges. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the officer had reasonable suspicion to believe that the vehicle he observed was being driven unlawfully and that the officer's stop of defendant's vehicle did not violate his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Hanson v. Madison Service Corp.


No. 88-0252


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


150 Wis. 2d 828; 443 N.W.2d 315; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 511


November 17, 1988, Argued  
May 11, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Robert A. DeChambeau, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ex-public employee sought review of orders of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted a judgment notwithstanding a jury's verdict finding that the employee did not receive an adequate hearing before his termination by defendant ex-public employer and which refused to reconsider a partial summary judgment holding that the post-termination procedures provided by the employer were constitutionally adequate.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a bus driver fired after his fifth "chargeable" accident within a four-month period. The employee filed a grievance, which the employer denied. The employee's union found that the grievance lacked sufficient merit to take to arbitration. After dismissal of the employee's action alleging that the union breached its duty of fair representation, the employee pursued an action claiming that the employer violated his due process rights. The trial court granted partial summary judgment in favor of the employer, holding that the employee received adequate post-termination process. After trial, the jury returned a verdict finding that the pre-termination procedures were inadequate. The trial court entered a judgment NOV in favor of the employer on that claim. The court affirmed the partial summary judgment because the grievance/arbitration provisions of the employee's bargaining agreement provided adequate post-termination process. The court reversed the judgment NOV, which was nullified by an intervening United States Supreme Court decision, but it held that the employee waived his right to more than nominal damages by failing to request actual damages in the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order refusing to reconsider its partial summary judgment that the employee was provided constitutionally adequate post-termination procedures. The court reversed the judgment notwithstanding the jury's verdict finding that the employee did not receive an adequate hearing before his termination by the employer. The court remanded the action to the trial court with directions to award one dollar to the employee.

In re Estate of Schneider


No. 88-2206


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


150 Wis. 2d 286; 441 N.W.2d 335; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 357


March 29, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
April 26, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County: Daniel P. Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an alleged nonmarital child, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin) dismissing his petition to be declared the nonmarital son of a decedent, so that he could inherit the decedent's estate.


OVERVIEW: The alleged nonmarital child conceded that his mother was lawfully married when he was conceived and born. Therefore, in order to show that he was a nonmarital child of the decedent, he had to overcome the presumptions of legitimacy and paternity codified in Wis. Stat. §§ 891.39(1)(a), 891.41. Pursuant to those statutes, he had to overcome the presumption that he was a marital child by producing a clear and satisfactory preponderance of evidence that the man to whom his mother was married was not his father. The court agreed with the trial court that the offer of proof was insufficient to rebut the presumption of legitimacy that arose upon proof that his mother was married when he was conceived and born. The alleged nonmarital child offered no evidence that it was physically or biologically impossible for his mother's husband to have been the father of the son born to her during the marriage. Most of his evidence dealt with the decedent's acknowledgments of paternity and the nature of his relationship with the alleged nonmarital child. That evidence, however, was premature. The requirement that such a child first illegitimatize himself did not render the statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the petition of the alleged nonmarital child seeking a declaration that he was a child of the deceased for purposes of inheritance.

 

1535 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. LeQue


No. 88-0921-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


150 Wis. 2d 256; 442 N.W.2d 494; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 351


January 19, 1989, Argued  
April 26, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from orders of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County: Steven W. Weinke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged shortly after his 18th birthday in the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin) as an adult with three counts of first-degree sexual assault committed when he was 15 years old. He moved to dismiss the charges for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and prosecutorial delay. Defendant sought appellate review of the denial of both motions.


OVERVIEW: The court held that defendant was subject to the adult court's jurisdiction because the determinative factor was his age on the date the action was filed, rather than his age when the alleged offenses were committed. The court held that the State successfully met its due process burden of showing that defendant was charged as an adult based solely on his age rather than as the result of intentional manipulation designed to avoid juvenile court jurisdiction. The court also held that the State acted with due dispatch in bringing the charges against defendant under the circumstances of the case at bar. The court held that defendant had a due process right not to be deprived of the potential benefits of juvenile jurisdiction through deliberate State manipulation designed to avoid juvenile jurisdiction. The court held that due process did not protect defendant from the loss of juvenile court jurisdiction due to the mere passage of time, absent manipulative intent by the State. The court held that the trial court's factual findings supported a finding that the State did not act with manipulative intent to avoid juvenile court jurisdiction and affirmed the orders entered below.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's finding that the period of time between the alleged incident's report and defendant's eighteenth birthday represented time spent on legitimate investigation and was not the product of intentional or negligent delay. The court held that the trial court's findings were not clearly erroneous and held that there was no intentional State manipulation. The court affirmed the trial court's orders.

 

1536 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Paternity of P.J.W.


No. 88-0052


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


150 Wis. 2d 123; 441 N.W.2d 289; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 364


November 7, 1988, Submitted on briefs  
April 6, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: William D. Byrne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult child sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his action against respondent putative father seeking a determination of parentage and child support.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after the child's birth, the putative father and the mother filed an illegitimacy agreement. In the agreement, the father denied that he fathered the child but agreed to pay a lump sum payment as future support and maintenance of the child. The agreement released the farther from liability and the mother and her husband agreed to treat the child as their natural son. When he reached majority the child brought an action against the father to determine paternity and for back child support. The trial court held that the action was barred by res judicata because of the illegitimacy agreement, and dismissed the action. The child appealed. The court held that because there was no judgment, res judicata did not bar the litigation of the child's paternity. The dismissal of the action for back child support was correct, however. The purpose of the illegitimacy agreement was accomplished; the child was supported to the age of majority. A child who had reached majority had no cause of action against a parent for an award of child support.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the child's claim for paternity. The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the child's claim for support.

Broome v. Steger


No. 88-0379


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


149 Wis. 2d 762; 441 N.W.2d 755; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 303



March 23, 1989, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: ROBERT DeCHAMBEAU, Judge. Reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenants sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which entered a judgment for respondent landlord in the landlord's eviction action.


OVERVIEW: The landlord filed a complaint that sought to evict the tenants. The tenants argued that the trial court lacked jurisdiction because the landlord had commenced the eviction action prior to the expiration of the landlord's 30 day notice of termination. The trial court granted a judgment for the landlord. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded the case for further proceedings. The court held that the trial court properly proceeded before the expiration of the third notice provided by the landlord. The tenants argued that the landlord filed the eviction action as retaliation for the tenants' threats of reporting building code violations. The court held that the trial committed reversible error in giving the jury an instruction that the landlord was prohibited from evicting the tenants solely for retaliation. The court concluded that retaliation was a defense to the eviction proceeding if the retaliation was a factor in the eviction, not the sole factor for the eviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which entered a judgment for the landlord in the eviction action against the tenants, and the court remanded the cause for further proceedings.

State v. Duprey


No. 88-2120-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


149 Wis. 2d 655; 439 N.W.2d 837; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 250


February 8, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
March 21, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Brown county: Peter Naze, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which amended its charge of felony nonsupport against defendant to a misdemeanor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was ordered to pay 25 percent of his income as child support. He failed to make any payments for two years. Defendant was charged with felony nonsupport under Wis. Stat. § 940.27(2) (1986). At the preliminary hearing, the mother testified that defendant told her that he was running a tavern, doing odd jobs, and painting during the two years. The trial court found probable cause and bound defendant over for trial. Defendant then filed a motion to reduce the charges to misdemeanor nonsupport because the State failed to prove that defendant earned income for 120 consecutive days. The trial court granted defendant's motion. The State appealed. The court held that the State met its burden of proving all of the elements required for a violation of § 940.27. Defendant was entitled to show as an affirmative defense that he had insufficient income to pay child support, but the State was not required to prove that defendant had income. Proof of defendant's ability to pay was not an element of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the action with directions to reinstate the felony charge.

State v. Bartlett


No. 88-1038-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


149 Wis. 2d 557; 439 N.W.2d 595; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 290


February 7, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
March 7, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Marvin C. Holz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of six counts of fleeing a traffic officer in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.04(3).


OVERVIEW: Three civilians and a police officer were injured and one police officer was killed as a result of the pursuit of defendant. The trial court convicted defendant of three violations of Wis. Stat. § 346.17(3)(b) and three violations of Wis. Stat. § 346.17(3)(d). Defendant contended that Wis. Stat. § 346.17(b)-(d) was unconstitutionally vague and that the evidence was insufficient to prove causality. The court determined that § 346.17(b) unambiguously required proof that a defendant's conduct was a substantial factor contributing to property damage, great bodily harm, or death, or to any combination of those losses. The court explained that the term "results in" was a causative term and it sought to prohibit attempts to elude a traffic officer or marked police vehicle. The court noted that § 346.17(b)-(d) was not void for vagueness because the statute prescribed the offense with reasonable certainty. The court concluded that the trial court's finding that defendant's conduct was a substantial factor in causing the collision was supported by ample evidence because had defendant stopped when he should have, the accident would not have occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of six counts of fleeing a traffic officer.

State v. Murphy


No. 88-1273-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


149 Wis. 2d 400; 439 N.W.2d 645; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 179



February 23, 1989, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waupaca county: JOHN P. HOFFMANN, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Waupaca County (Wisconsin) dismissing his motion to reopen and vacate a judgment revoking his drivers' license, pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 343.305(6m) and (9) (1985-86).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for unlawfully operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a), and while his blood alcohol content level was .20 percent or more, Wis. Stat. § 346.63(lm). The trial court revoked defendant's operating privileges for one year. Long after the time for appeal had expired, defendant moved to reopen and vacate the order and dismiss the case on grounds that the statute of revocation had been repealed and because the order of revocation was unconstitutional. The issue was whether the trial court abused its judgment. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion. To permit defendant to reopen the case after the time for appeal had expired on grounds he could have raised on a direct appeal would have been tantamount to allowing him to extend the time for appeal beyond the statutory limit. Wis. Stat. § 806.07 did not authorize the trial court to expand the time for appeal when the time for such appeal had passed.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion to reopen and vacate the judgment. Accordingly, the court affirmed the trial court judgment.

State v. Dums


No. 88-1154-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


149 Wis. 2d 314; 440 N.W.2d 814; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 205


January 11, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
February 21, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Taylor county: Douglas T. Fox, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought interlocutory review of an order by the Circuit Court for Taylor County (Wisconsin), which upheld the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 967.055(2). Defendant was charged with a second offense of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant (OWI), and he claimed that § 967.055(2) violated the separation-of-powers doctrine and failed to contain standards necessary for proper implementation.


OVERVIEW: When the citing officer discovered that the offense was defendant's second, he referred the matter for a criminal complaint, and without independently inquiring into the first charge, the prosecution prepared, signed, and filed a criminal complaint. The trial court refused a prosecution motion to amend the charge to a civil forfeiture, finding the 11 reasons supporting the motion to be contrary to public interest under § 967.055(2), and defendant unsuccessfully challenged the constitutionality of that section. On review, the court held that a well-established presumption of constitutionality attached to all legislative acts, and that once the prosecutor failed to exercise his broad discretion in issuing the criminal complaint and the prosecution commenced, the charge became subject to judicial control under § 967.055(2). The court found that the "in the public interest" standard was reasonable because it required an examination of all relevant factors concerning the public's interest in deterring drunk driving.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order upholding the constitutionality of the challenged provision.

Haack v. Haack


No. 87-2352


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


149 Wis. 2d 243; 440 N.W.2d 794; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 180


January 17, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
February 15, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review and cross review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from judgments of the circuit court for Waukesha county: Patrick L. Snyder, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband and respondent wife sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which granted the wife's petition for a divorce, divided the marital estate, and denied the wife's motion to amend the divorce petition to include a cause of action based on Wis. Stat. § 766.70.


OVERVIEW: The parties were divorced. The husband asserted that the trial court made numerous factual errors when dividing the marital estate. Valuation of assets, property division, and maintenance all rested within the sound discretion of the trial court. Because the trial court's decision was based upon a reasoned rationale, the court affirmed the division. The wife contested the trial court's denial of her motion to amend the divorce petition to include a cause of action under § 766.70 for property damages resulting from the breach of the duty of good faith. Wis. Stat. § 767.05 prohibited divorcing spouses from suing under Wis. Stat. § 766.70. The court determined that Wis. Stat. § 767.05 was constitutional. Wis. Stat. § 766.70 was not designed to create remedies for women, but for partners in a marriage. Therefore, the prohibition in § 767.05 was not gender biased simply because it could be used by a husband to undo an action under § 766.70. Although § 767.05(7) did create two classes of spouses, the classification was not unconstitutional. It was reasonable to merge all litigation between divorcing spouses into the divorce proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decisions.

Burlington Northern, Inc. v. Superior


Nos. 88-0701, 88-0702, 88-0703, 88-0704, 88-0705, 88-0706


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


149 Wis. 2d 190; 441 N.W.2d 234; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 160


November 14, 1988, Submitted on briefs  
February 7, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from judgments of the circuit court for Douglas county: Douglas S. Moodie, Reserve Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgments affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city government sought review of a judgment rendered by the Circuit Court for Douglas County (Wisconsin), which held that it was required to refund plaintiff railroad company occupational taxes paid pursuant to a tax statute that was later deemed unconstitutional. The railroad company filed a cross-appeal, arguing that the trial court erred in the calculation of judgment interest it was entitled to collect.


OVERVIEW: The city collected taxes pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 70.40(1) from the railroad company. The statute was later declared unconstitutional under the Commerce Clause by a court decision and the railroad company filed suit to collect its taxes paid. The trial court ordered the city to make a full refund plus prejudgment interest. The city appealed, claiming that it was not required to make a refund and the railroad company filed a cross-appeal, claiming that the trial court erred in the calculation of prejudgment interest. The court held that retroactive application of the decision, which held that the statute was unconstitutional, was proper because the decision did not establish a new principle of law, the retroactive application would not further or retard the operation of the new law, and retroactive application would not produce substantially inequitable results to the city because it was put on notice that the statute was unconstitutional. The court also concluded that the trial court erred in its calculation of interest because the railroad company was entitled to interest from the date it made payment, not when it filed a return, since the statute was void ab initio.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the judgment of the trial court, holding that the railroad company was entitled to a full refund of taxes it pay pursuant to an unconstitutional tax. The court also reversed in part, concluding that the trial court erred in its calculation of prejudgment interest the railroad company was entitled to collect. The court remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Kaster


No. 88-0447-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


148 Wis. 2d 789; 436 N.W.2d 891; 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 109


August 31, 1988, Submitted on briefs  
January 19, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Dane County: James C. Boll, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment on Count 3 reversed in part insofar as it mandates restitution on Counts 1 and 2 and judgment and order otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment and order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of three counts of theft and party to the crime, and denied postconviction relief in a case brought by the State of Wisconsin.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised the issues of whether the trial court erred by admitting evidence of other bad conduct, whether newly discovered evidence required a new trial, and whether the trial court improperly imposed restitution on two sentences. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it ruled that the conduct testimony evidence was relevant. After determining the relevancy of the other acts evidence, the trial court balanced the probative value of that evidence against the risk of unfair prejudice and ruled that the evidence was admissible. The court also held the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied the motion for a new trial because it found that were a reasonable jury to hear the new evidence, the result would not have been different. However, the State conceded that the trial court should not have entered a judgment of probation conditioned on restitution for the first two counts. Restitution could not be imposed for an offense for which defendant was sentenced to prison. Therefore, the court reversed that part of the judgment ordering restitution on the first two counts and otherwise affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the judgment that ordered restitution on the first two counts of defendant's conviction for three counts of theft and party to the crime and otherwise affirmed the judgment.

Oelke v. Spelius


No. 87-1822


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


148 Wis. 2d 945; 437 N.W.2d 234; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1136



December 21, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha county: WILLIS J. ZICK, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowner appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which awarded plaintiff easement user and her heirs and successors a prescriptive easement over a strip of land.


OVERVIEW: The landowner challenged a judgment awarding the easement user and her heirs and successors a prescriptive easement over a strip of land. The court affirmed, holding that the testimony was sufficient to support the jury's finding of a prescriptive easement based on a 20-year period. The use made of the alley by the easement user and her family, customers, and delivery vehicles was clearly open and visible. The family's acts of maintaining and improving the alley could have been deemed by the jury to be hostile, adverse, and based on an open claim of right because it was done in disregard or nonrecognition of the alley's true ownership during the 20-year period. The court rejected the landowner's contention that the action was barred by laches. Additionally, the court also held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in awarding costs to the easement user and refusing to order her to pay real estate taxes and to purchase liability insurance covering the easement.


OUTCOME: The court, in favor of the easement user, affirmed the judgment of the trial court awarding the easement user a prescriptive easement over a strip of land owned by the landowner.

 

1547 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


American Family Mut. Ins. Co. v. Milwaukee


Nos. 87-2268, 88-0260


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


148 Wis. 2d 280; 435 N.W.2d 280; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1146


September 6, 1988, Submitted on briefs  
December 21, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross Appeal from a judgment and Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Gary A. Gerlach, Judge and Russell W. Stamper, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed and judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two consolidated appeals, appellant city sought review of an order and a judgment by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which both held that the city had a mandatory duty to provide uninsured motorist coverage under Wis. Stat. § 66.189. In one of the appeals, respondent police officer cross-appealed the judgment that respondent insurer was an excess insurance carrier.


OVERVIEW: The first case involved a police officer who was hit by an uninsured motorist. The second case involved a passenger in a police squad car that was struck by an uninsured motorist. Both the police officer and the passenger had insurance with the insurer. In both cases, the circuit court found the city to be primarily liable. The central issue in both appeals was whether the city had a mandatory duty to provide uninsured motorist coverage under Wis. Stat. § 66.189. The court held that (1) § 66.189 was unambiguous and required the city to provide uninsured motorist coverage for officer-employees and passengers; (2) the insurer was not required to enforce § 66.189 through a writ of mandamus; (3) the court refused to exercise its discretion to determine the constitutionality of § 66.189 as allegedly violative of the public purpose doctrine; and (4) the insurer's insurance coverage was not excess and the insurer was liable for a prorated share of the police officer's damages up to its policy limits. The judgment in the first case was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The order in the second case was affirmed.


OUTCOME: In the first case, the court reversed that portion of the judgment declaring that the insurer was an excess carrier and affirmed the remainder of the judgment. In the second case, the court affirmed the order that the city was primarily responsible to the passenger.

County of Price v. Cash

Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


148 Wis. 2d 950; 437 N.W.2d 236; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1189

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Prince County (Wisconsin), which entered summary judgment of conviction for violating the setback requirements of plaintiff county's zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that the property owner was barred by the doctrine of res judicata from asserting various defenses to the charges that he was in violation of the county's setback requirements. However, because the property owner had failed to present evidentiary support in opposition to the motion for summary judgment, the trial court properly granted summary judgment and its decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which entered summary judgment of conviction for violating the county's setback requirements, was affirmed.

 

1549 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Competition Haircutters v. Cosmetology Examining Bd.


No. 88-0089


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


148 Wis. 2d 946; 437 N.W.2d 234; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1161



December 15, 1988, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: DANIEL R. MOESER, Judge. Affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant beauty salon sought review of a judgment of an order of the circuit court for Dane county (Wisconsin) that affirmed an order of appellee Cosmetology Examining Board suspending the beauty salon's license for 30 days. The board found that the beauty salon aided in the unauthorized practice of cosmetology, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 458.09(4), 458.13(1), and 458.14(2).


OVERVIEW: The beauty salon's license was suspended following a judgment that it had aided in the unauthorized practice of cosmetology. The salon had allegedly aided in the unauthorized practice of cosmetology by employing unlicensed persons to render cosmetology services to patrons on two occasions, and by permitting the beauty salon to operate on three occasions without the manager of record, a licensed manager or a qualified designee on the premises. The court affirmed the judgment except for the charge that a licensed barber had provided cosmetology to one of the salon's patrons and that the salon had aided in the unauthorized practice of cosmetology. The court found that §§ 458.09(4), 458.13(1), 458.14(2)(h), and the administrative regulations did not establish that the cutting of hair by a licensed barber in a beauty salon constituted the unauthorized practice of cosmetology. Because there was no substantial distinction between cosmetology and barbering, the court found that the allegation was not proved. The court found that the salon did not substantially comply with the licensing requirements and affirmed the remainder of the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment as to a licensed barber and remanded the cause to reconsider the penalty imposed. The court affirmed the judgment regarding other employees engaging in cosmetology without a license.

 

1550 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pulizzano


No. 88-0010-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


148 Wis. 2d 190; 434 N.W.2d 807; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1142


November 8, 1988, Argued  
December 7, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review filed. This petition was not disposed of at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha county: David M. Bastian, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of four counts of first-degree sexual assault contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(d).


OVERVIEW: The victims were defendant's children and her nephews. Defendant contended that the trial court's application of the rape shield statute, Wis. Stat. § 972.11(2)(a)-(c), to deny cross-examination of the testifying victim as to a prior sexual assault and exclude evidence of that witness's untruthfulness violated her Sixth Amendment right to confrontation. On review, the court held that, to resolve the conflict between the rape shield law and defendant's constitutional rights, the Davis balancing test was to be applied, which required that defendant be allowed limited inquiry into the prior sexual assault for the purposes of negating the inference that the testifying victim's sexual knowledge was gained from defendant's alleged assault. On remand, the trial court was to restrict the testimony where necessary to avoid embarrassment or humiliation of the testifying victim while at the same time protecting defendant's right to put her defense theory before the jury. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in prohibiting testimony of prior untruthful allegations of sexual assault made by the victim because its probative value was outweighed by the confusion that would ensue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the cause.

State v. Fischer

Court of Appeals of Wisconsin

Stat. §§ 161.16(2)(b)1, 161.41(1)(c)1, 161.41(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged an order denying his motion to suppress evidence. At issue on appeal was whether (1) the police exceeded the scope of a search warrant by seizing a locked safe in defendant's apartment; (2) the police unconstitutionally conducted a warrantless search of the safe after seizing it; and (3) the trial court should have ordered the state to disclose the identity of an informer whose statements to the police formed a partial basis for the warrant's issuance. Defendant failed to make the preliminary showing required by Franks and Mann that a person executing the warrant affidavit knowingly or with reckless disregard for the truth omitted from it the fact that the informant had a criminal record or was a drug addict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court.

1553 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Nelson v. Every


No. 87-1665


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


147 Wis. 2d 880; 434 N.W.2d 621; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1019



October 6, 1988, Decided and Filed; Review Denied December 6, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment in the circuit court for Dane county: SUSAN STEINGASS, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judgment lienholder challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that granted the summary judgment motion of defendant county and dismissed his action to collect a judgment lien on a parcel of real estate that the county had obtained through a tax deed. When the county sold the property, the lienholder sought imposition of a constructive trust on the proceeds and an order directing the county to pay his lien.


OVERVIEW: The lienholder argued that because the county did not notify him that it was selling the property for taxes and because it retained the surplus funds over and above the taxes due on the property, his constitutional rights to due process and equal protection were violated. The court affirmed the judgment. The court explained that a judgment lien was not a lien on any specific real estate of the judgment debtor but was a general lien on all of the debtor's real property. The court reasoned that, as a result, the lienholder did not have the type of property interest that entitled him to specific notice of the county's intention to take a tax deed to the property in question. The court found that a procedure allowing tax sales to proceed without requiring the county to search out and notify all general lienholders of its intent to take title to the property advanced a governmental interest. And, therefore, the court opined, that by establishing such a procedure, the legislature had not unconstitutionally classified public and private lienholders.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Black & Decker, Inc. v. Department of Industry, Labor & Human Relations


No. 88-0409


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


146 Wis. 2d 873; 433 N.W.2d 34; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 847



September 15, 1988, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: MICHAEL N. NOWAKOWSKI, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted judgment in favor of respondent Department of Industry, Labor, and Human Relations and held that there was probable cause under Wis. Admin. Code § 88.08 to believe that discrimination had occurred when the employer terminated defendant employee and held that the statute was valid.


OVERVIEW: The employer terminated the employee. The employee contended that such termination was discriminatory and filed a complaint with the Department. The Department held that there was probable cause to believe that discrimination had occurred under Wis. Admin. Code § 88.08. The employer initiated a declaratory action contending that the statute was invalid. The trial court held that the statute was valid, and the employer sought review. Under § 88.08, the Department was required to issue a determination as to whether there was probable cause to believe that discrimination existed and the employee had the right to appeal a finding of no probable cause. The court held that the Department had only those powers which were expressly conferred from the statute. The court found that the statute had not defined how the Department was to investigate complaints and further found that it was permitted to hold a hearing after an initial finding of no probable cause. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which granted judgment in favor of the Department and the employee and held that the statute, which gave the Department the authority to review the employer's termination decision for discriminatory actions, was valid.

Peck v. Department of Revenue


No. 87-2259


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


146 Wis. 2d 871; 433 N.W.2d 33; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 790



September 14, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha county: ROBERT T. McGRAW, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which affirmed an assessment by respondent Department of Revenue of capital gains tax following the sale of a one-half interest in real property.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer and his former wife owned a home together during their marriage. The divorce court ordered the home sold. The taxpayer and his fiancee decided that the fiancee would purchase the wife's half of the house. The wife could not deal with this emotionally, so the taxpayer bought the half-interest with his fiancee's money and transferred it to her. The Department assessed tax on the taxpayer's capital gains on the property. The taxpayer argued that he served as his fiancee's agent in the transaction and did not incur gains on the property. The trial court affirmed the Department's assessment. The taxpayer appealed. The court found no error in the trial court's decision. The taxpayer and his fiancee, both attorneys, failed to include any agency language in the purchasing documents. The taxpayer paid the transfer fee for transferring the property to his fiancee after successfully claiming an exemption for the first transfer. Substantial evidence supported the Department's assessment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1556 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Danzinger v. Modern Concrete Products Co.


No. 88-0244


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


146 Wis. 2d 872; 433 N.W.2d 33; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 781



September 6, 1988, Decided; Review Granted March 7, 1989


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Buffalo county: GARY G. SCHLOSSTEIN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the owners of a farming business, challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Buffalo County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their action against respondents, a contractor, a concrete company, and their insurers, for negligent construction of a cattle building. The trial court ruled that the action was barred by the six-year statute of limitations provided in Wis. Stat. § 893.89.


OVERVIEW: The contractor constructed a concrete foundation for a building on the owners' farms using concrete supplied by the concrete company. The owners contended that because of allegedly defective concrete and negligent construction, the foundation cracked and collapsed. The owners argued that § 893.89 was unconstitutional because it denied them due process and equal protection. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court reviewed its recent opinion concerning similar issues and held that § 893.89 did not violate Wis. Const. art. I, § 9 because six years after substantial completion, the owners no longer had a legally recognized right for which they were denied a remedy. The court concluded that the legislative declarations of policy, which were to cut off claims at some point and to distinguish owners from those associated with the construction of the building on the basis of possession and control, provided a rational basis for the classifications § 893.89 created. Further, the court found that in § 893.89 the legislature had expressly dictated that the limitations period began to run on substantial completion of construction, and thus the discovery rule did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1557 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anchico


No. 87-1414-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


146 Wis. 2d 866; 431 N.W.2d 327; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 705



August 25, 1988, Decided and Filed; Review Denied October 18, 1988


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: MICHAEL B. TORPHY, JR., Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him on a jury verdict of two counts of second-degree sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(a). The issues involved Wisconsin's rape shield law, Wis. Stat. § 972.11(2)(b)1, and the exclusions permitted by Wis. Stat. § 971.31(11).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that evidence of his past relationship with the victim was improperly excluded. The trial court held that the evidence was neither material nor relevant to the issue of consent. The court found that the trial court allowed defendant great leeway in questioning the victim about various aspects of their sexual relationship, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 972.11(2)(b)1. In the court's view, the jury was made aware of a wealth of details. The additional evidence that defendant wished to present included events from months before the assault and other written and pictorial materials that had no reasonable bearing on whether the victim consented. Thus, the evidence was excludable under Wis. Stat. § 971.31(11). Regarding defendant's claim that his prior bad acts were admitted in error, the court opined that the exceptions in Wis. Stat. 904.04(2) were illustrative rather than exhaustive. Thus, the jury was entitled to hear defendant's prior bad acts to complete the picture that defendant developed on cross-examination of the victim. The court declined to use its discretionary reversal power because the evidentiary issues were properly decided.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1558 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morke


No. 87-1924


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


146 Wis. 2d 866; 431 N.W.2d 327; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 731



August 25, 1988, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: DANIEL R. MOESER, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him on six counts of burglary and sentenced him to a total of 15 years' imprisonment, consecutive to an out-of-state sentence and ten years probation, consecutive to the prison term.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was denied parole in 1985, 1986, and in 1987 because he had not served sufficient time for punishment and his release posed an unreasonable risk to the public. Defendant argued that Wis. Stat. § 57.06(1) was amended effective in 1983 to change the parole eligibility threshold from one-half the minimum term prescribed by statute for the offense to 25 percent of the sentence imposed. The trial court concluded that defendant had not shown a new factor and denied defendant's motion to modify his sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court noted that defendant was correct that a retroactive application of an amendatory statute, which increased the period of time a prisoner was required to serve before he was eligible for parole consideration violated the ex post facto clauses under Wis. Const. art. I, § 12 and U. S. Const. art. I, § 9. However, defendant's remedy was to challenge that application by seeking review of the parole board's decision by certiorari or through a mandamus proceeding. The court held that a sentence modification was an inappropriate remedy for an unconstitutional application of parole eligibility rules and practices.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Ledger v. Waupaca Bd. of Appeals


No. 87-2091


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


146 Wis. 2d 256; 430 N.W.2d 370; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 767


June 24, 1988, Submitted on briefs  
August 18, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Waupaca county: Phillip M. Kirk, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of an order of the circuit court for Waupaca County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision by respondent city board of appeals to issue a permit for construction of an apartment building. The board upheld a city building inspector's grant of the permit even though the proposed development did not conform to limitations on the use of the property contained in a city zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: A former owner of the land on which the building was to be constructed had petitioned the city to rezone the property from single- to multiple-family residential use. The petition was granted, on the express condition that the building conform to the plans as submitted and that, in the event that the condition was not complied with, the property would automatically revert back to the single-family classification. When a new owner subsequently sought a building permit for a proposed apartment complex, which differed from the original submitted plans, the city building inspector determined that the imposed conditions were invalid. On appeal from the trial court's ruling that the conditions were arbitrary and unenforceable, the landowners argued that the board lacked the authority to declare the zoning ordinance arbitrary. The court, in reversing the trial court's decision, agreed and determined that the board had exceeded its powers. The court, noting that the board made no factual findings and gathered no evidence, found that the board's powers were limited, under Wis. Stat. § 62.23(7)(e)7, to matters relating to carrying out the strict letter of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had affirmed the board's decision to issue the building permit, even though the proposed use of the property did not conform to the zoning ordinance.

Marshfield v. Manlick

Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


146 Wis. 2d 868; 431 N.W.2d 328; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 770

NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Wood county: EDWARD F. ZAPPEN, JR., Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Wood County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of violating a city ordinance prohibiting minors from possessing or consuming alcoholic beverages.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged a judgment finding him guilty of violating a city ordinance that prohibited minors from possessing or consuming alcoholic beverages after a preliminary breath test showed a blood alcohol content of .02 percent. On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence of a preliminary breath test administered by the arresting officer was inadmissible to show violation of the ordinance, and that the evidence was insufficient to support the finding of guilt. The court concluded that the test results were inadmissible, but that any error was harmless because there was sufficient admissible evidence to support defendant's conviction. The court held that the evidence of the test results was barred by Wis. Stat. § 343.303, as the preliminary test was only admissible to show probable cause for an arrest or to prove that a chemical test was required. The court held that the testimony of the police officer, stating that he smelled alcoholic beverages, provided sufficient evidence to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

State v. Smith


No. 87-2307-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


145 Wis. 2d 906; 430 N.W.2d 380; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 585



July 27, 1988, Decided; Review Denied October 18, 1988


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit for Milwaukee county: JANINE P. GESKE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of incest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that he received inadequate notice of the offense's timeframe and that not sequestering an expert witness and allowing the victim to testify that defendant took nude photos of her deprived defendant of his right to a fair trial. The court affirmed the conviction, concluding that the valid decision to charge defendant with a continuing offense justified the six-year timeframe in the complaint and that any evidentiary error was harmless. The court reasoned that the victim testified that the incest occurred for several years, that the timeframe was selected to comply with the limitations period, and that defendant had adequate information to allow him to prepare a defense. The court also held that, although there was no basis for allowing the expert to be present throughout the trial, there was no evidence that either the verdict or his testimony would have been different if he had been sequestered. The court further determined that the other evidence of guilt was so overwhelming that defendant would have been convicted even if the victim had not been allowed to testify as to the photos.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for incest.

In re D.S.A.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a juvenile, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which denied her motion for a new trial after she was adjudicated delinquent on the ground that she was a party to the crime of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, along with two other juveniles, was adjudicated delinquent on the ground that she was a party to the crime of first-degree murder. Petitioner was 11 years old at the time of the murder. The victim was a nine-year-old boy. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not err when it rejected petitioner's motion to change venue. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in rejecting the request that the witness's testimony be stricken and a new trial ordered. Finally, the court found that the trial court's refusal to admit a polygraph test that petitioner proposed to take did not deny her right to present a defense.

Capital Preservation Fund, Inc. v. Department of Revenue


No. 87-1303


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


145 Wis. 2d 841; 429 N.W.2d 551; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 622


June 2, 1988, Submitted on briefs  
July 21, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: Mark A. Frankel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Wisconsin Department of Revenue sought review of a summary judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which declared that dividend distributions from respondents, the Capital Preservation Fund and the Trust for Short Term U.S. Government Securities, were not subject to the Wisconsin income tax.


OVERVIEW: The Fund and the Trust were mutual money market funds, which distributed substantially all of the income earned to their shareholders. The Fund invested solely in direct obligations of the federal government -- U.S. Treasury bills, notes, and zero coupon securities. The Trust invested exclusively in treasury obligations and those of other federal agencies, such as Federal Home Loan Banks. The Trust also entered into repurchase agreements, through which it purchased government obligations from third parties, normally banks, pursuant to a contract in which the bank agreed to repurchase the obligations from the Trust on a specified date and at a set price and rate of interest. The Fund, the Trust, and several investors brought a declaratory judgment action after the Department interpreted the Wisconsin income tax statutes as applying to the shareholder distributions. The trial court ruled that such an interpretation violated the provisions of 31 U.S.C.S. § 3124(a). The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, concluding that the state could not tax any of the investment distributions, but that distributions based on income from the Trust's repurchase agreements were taxable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed part of the trial court's judgment, concluding that the state could not tax any of the investment distributions, but reversed part of the judgment, concluding that distributions based on income from the Trust's repurchase agreements were taxable.
