Timm v. Portage County Drainage Dist.


No. 86-1379


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


145 Wis. 2d 743; 429 N.W.2d 512; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 649


March 10, 1988, Argued  
July 14, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied. Petition to cross review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Portage county: Frederic W. Fleischauer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought review after the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin) dismissed their claims against defendants, drainage district and drainage commission (commission), having permitted intervenor farmers to enter the action, which arose under Wis. Stat. § 893.80(4). On cross-appeal, the commission sought costs and attorney fees pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 814.04(9), 823.08(4).


OVERVIEW: The landowners were farmers. Their property lay adjacent to drainage ditches Nos. 3, 4, and 8, which the commission controlled and managed. The commission removed stop logs from dams 12 and 53. The landowners claim that that caused substantial widening and deepening of the ditches resulting in soil erosion, destruction of trees and vegetation, and that it decreased property and crop values. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the commission. On appeal, the court held that the trial court's finding that the commission had balanced the competing interests in making the stop log decision was supported by the record and was not clearly erroneous. Defendants' decisions were policy decisions inasmuch as they were the result of a conscious balancing of risks and advantages. The commission was entitled to Wis. Stat. § 893.80(4) immunity. Whether to award equitable relief was within the trial court's discretion. The facts cited by the trial court did not support its conclusion that the landowners' request for an order was barred by "unclean hands." With regard to the cross-appeal, the commission could not recover costs and attorney fees under Wis. Stat. § 814.04(9) or § 823.08(4).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling that defendants were immune from suit, reversed the trial court's denial of the landowners' request for equitable relief, and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1565 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Hartland-Richmond Town Ins. Co. v. Wudtke


No. 87-1780


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


145 Wis. 2d 682; 429 N.W.2d 496; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 581


March 29, 1988, Submitted on briefs  
July 12, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not disposed of at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Shawano county: Thomas G. Grover, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of a judgment and order from the Circuit Court for Shawano County (Wisconsin), which dismissed its complaint against respondents, a worker who installed electrical wiring in the building of involuntary appellants, the insureds, and the worker's insurer. The action was dismissed because it was not commenced within six years as required by Wis. Stat. § 893.89.


OVERVIEW: In 1978, the worker installed electrical wiring in a building being constructed for the insureds. In 1986, a fire destroyed the building and its contents. The insurer made a payment to the insureds and then sued the worker and his insurer for defective workmanship in 1978. The building was substantially completed more than six years before the fire. The trial court dismissed the action pursuant to § 893.89, which provided that a six-year statute of limitations began to run upon the substantial completion of construction for actions against those involved in construction. The court upheld the dismissal. First, the court held that the insurer lacked standing to challenge § 893.89 on the basis of a denial of equal protection because neither it nor its insureds were denied the protection provided by the statute of limitations under the facts of the case. Thus, they were not members of the class subject to the unequal protection of which they complained. Second, the court held that § 893.89 did not run afoul of Wis. Const. art. I, § 9 because six years after substantial completion, the insurer no longer had a legally-recognized right for which it was being denied a remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and order.

 

1566 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Schramek v. Bohren


No. 87-1831


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


145 Wis. 2d 695; 429 N.W.2d 501; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 597


April 26, 1988, Submitted on briefs  
July 12, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied. CALLOW, J., took no part.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Thomas P. Doherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part and reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint against defendants that alleged (1) violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983; (2) assault and battery; (3) intentional infliction of emotional distress; (4) invasion of privacy; (5) malicious prosecution and abuse of process; and that (6) Wis. Stat. § 813.12 was unconstitutional on its face and in its application.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff wife alleged that the trial court improperly sustained the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 813.12, and that the trial court erred as a matter of law in dismissing all of her causes of action. Plaintiff's constitutional challenge consisted of five parts: (1) inadequate notice of hearing and denial of a pre-TRO hearing; (2) denial of the right to a jury; (3) vagueness; (4) overbreadth; and (5) denial of equal protection. Plaintiff alleged inadequate notice of the injunction hearing and the nature of the charge, and no hearing prior to the issuance of the ex parte TRO on the domestic abuse charge. When the rights of a person were affected by judicial or quasi-judicial decree, adequate due process required that the notice must reasonably convey information about the proceedings so that respondent could prepare a defense or make objections. The court found that the facts asserted in the petition formed the basis for the claim of domestic abuse, placed plaintiff on notice of the claim, and provided her with circumstances to formulate a defense or raise objections. The seven-day notice was sufficient for due process purposes. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as to the statute's constitutionality. Because the trial court improperly dismissed the assault and battery action against defendant husband, the court reversed and remanded. Because the remaining claims constituted a collateral attack on the injunctive order of the family court commissioner; the court reversed and remanded with directions.

 

1567 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


American Druggists' Ins. Co. v. American Standard, Inc.


No. 87-1262


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


145 Wis. 2d 901; 428 N.W.2d 644; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 497



June 30, 1988, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson county: JOHN B. DANFORTH, Judge. Affirmed in part and reversed in part. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurer appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin) that granted summary judgment to defendants, a general contractor and architect, ruling that Wis. Stat. § 893.89 barred a subrogation action, and dismissed a claim against defendant, the manufacturer of the allegedly defective fireplace and chimney, on the basis of laches.


OVERVIEW: An apartment building burned four years after its substantial completion. The insurer paid the owner's claim and over two years later filed an action against the architect, general contractor, and the manufacturer of a fireplace and chimney that had allegedly caused the fire. The trial court ruled that the action against the contractor and architect was barred by Wis. Stat. § 893.89, which established a six-year limit for commencing actions based on improvements to real property. The trial court held that the insurer was guilty of laches where the manufacturer's right of contribution against the contractor and architect was precluded by § 836.89. In reversing the dismissal of the claim against the manufacturer, the court held that the trial court exceeded its discretion because laches did not apply in an action at law and the insurer had no duty to protect the manufacturer's right of contribution. Where 18 months had passed between the insurer's payment of the claim and the commencement of its subrogation action, the insurer lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 836.89 because the dismissal was the result of its own delay rather than the statutory bar.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded that part of the judgment that dismissed the insurer's claim against the manufacturer, and affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the architect and general contractor.

 

1568 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harris


No. 87-1918


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


145 Wis. 2d 902; 428 N.W.2d 645; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 489



June 28, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: JOHN E. MC CORMICK, Judge. Affirmed. 
Harris v. State, 89 Wis. 2d 764, 278 N.W.2d 283, 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3137 (Wis. Ct. App., Mar. 29, 1979)



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his Wis. Stat. § 974.06 motion for postconviction relief. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder as party to a crime and attempted robbery as party to a crime. The court of appeals had affirmed his conviction and the Wisconsin Supreme Court had denied his petition for review before defendant filed his § 974.06 motion.


OVERVIEW: In his motion for postconviction relief, defendant contended that: (1) the evidence was insufficient to convict him for first-degree murder as party to a crime; (2) his conviction for first-degree murder violated his right to due process; (3) he was deprived of due process when the trial court improperly instructed the jury; (4) he was denied a fair trial by the state's alleged failure to fully disclose the plea agreement offered to one of the witnesses against him; (5) Wis. Stat. § 939.05, the party to a crime statute, was unconstitutional; (6) allegedly prejudicial remarks in the prosecutor's opening and closing statements denied him a fair trial; and (7) he was denied effective assistance of counsel at trial and on appeal. The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion. Regarding the first two claims, the court held that defendant had challenged the sufficiency of the evidence in his direct appeal and could not relitigate the issue. The court further held that the trial court properly instructed the jury, that the statute was constitutional, that the prosecutor was allowed to give his opinion of the evidence, and that defendant received effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion.

 

1569 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brookens


No. 87-1566-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


145 Wis. 2d 901; 428 N.W.2d 645; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 511



June 23, 1988, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Dane county: MARK A. FRANKEL, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment rendered by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which found him guilty of felony intimidation of a witness. Defendant contended that he was denied a fair trial.


OVERVIEW: The prosecutor brought a charge against defendant for felony intimidation of a witness after he was acquitted of committing battery on a woman. Defendant was found guilty and appealed. The court held that the criminal statutes, Wis. Stat. § 940.42 and Wis. Stat. § 940.43, were not unconstitutionally vague because the statutes alerted a person of ordinary intelligence to the type of conduct that was prohibited and the phrase 'implied threat of force' was not overbroad because it was not so sweeping that its sanctions could be applied to conduct that the state was not permitted to regulate. The court also stated that defendant was not entitled to a prosecutorial vindictiveness presumption because defendant failed to prove a realistic likelihood of vindictiveness and the prosecutor only charged defendant with an offense after he was acquitted of the battery charge. Further, the court noted that the complaint had no material omission and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in not severing the intimidation charges since defendant failed to prove substantial prejudice. Finally, the court concluded that defendant received effective assistance of counsel and denied his appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1570 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Kalt v. Board of Fire & Police Comm'rs


No. 87-1929


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


145 Wis. 2d 504; 427 N.W.2d 408; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 475


April 26, 1988, Submitted on briefs  
June 14, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Ralph Adam Fine, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officers (officers) challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied their petition for a writ of certiorari and upheld the disciplinary action taken against the officers by respondent Board of Fire & Police Commissioners for the City of Milwaukee (board). Such disciplinary action arose out of the officers' failure to render aid, one officer's excessive force, and the death of a suspect.


OVERVIEW: The suspect was stopped by the officers. A struggle ensued, and the officers used force to subdue him that included putting a knee on the suspect's neck. The suspect became motionless, could not be roused with an ammonia capsule, and had a rapid pulse and trouble breathing. Although the officers were aware of the suspect's condition, they gave no aid to him and he died. The officers were suspended without pay, and one officer was discharged. The trial court's order, which the court affirmed, upheld the disciplinary action. The court held that the officers' conduct fell within the "hard core" of Milwaukee, Wis., Police Dept. R. & Regs. 4, § 67, which stated that an officer who failed to render first aid whenever necessary would be charged with a neglect of duty. Rule 4, § 67 was not unconstitutionally vague just because it required the exercise of some discretion. Ordinary men of common intelligence would have known that first aid was required. The suspension of the officers prior to the disciplinary hearing and the failure to adjourn the hearing pending the criminal matter against certain of the officers failed to show the board's alleged bias.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that denied the officers' petition for a writ of certiorari and upheld the disciplinary action against the officers.

 

1571 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Hasselblad v. Green Bay


No. 87-2261


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


145 Wis. 2d 439; 427 N.W.2d 140; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 487


May 9, 1988, Orally argued  
June 7, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Brown county: N. Patrick Crooks, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which limited their business replacement damages in eminent domain proceedings instituted by defendant City to $ 50,000 pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 32.19(4m)(a)1.


OVERVIEW: The property owners sought to have declared unconstitutional the Wisconsin statute setting a $ 50,000 limit on business replacement damages in eminent domain proceedings. They claimed that the limit was contrary to Wis. Const. art. I, § 13, which provided for just compensation for property taken for public use. The property owners were business partners whose commercial location was acquired by the city in order to complete a street expansion project. The city conceded that the type of damages contemplated under Wis. Stat. § 32.19(4m) exceeded $ 50,000, even after adjustments for a larger replacement facility. The trial court granted the City's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the property owners argued that their situation was similar to one in which a 12-month limit for rental losses caused by condemnation were held unconstitutional. The court held that the case under consideration differed because rental damages bore a direct relationship to fair market value and that business replacement expenses, and traditional incidental damages, such as moving expenses, did not. The court held that the statute limiting the property owners' damages was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1572 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Richards v. Young


No. 87-1874


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


145 Wis. 2d 322; 426 N.W.2d 117; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 422


April 22, 1988, Submitted on briefs  
May 26, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from orders of the circuit court for Dane county: P. Charles Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Orders reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. Id. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted respondent prison officials' motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and dismissed the inmate's declaratory judgment action against the prison officials.


OVERVIEW: The inmate sought a ruling on the validity of certain prison rules. The prison officials filed a motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction because the inmate did not serve the Joint Committee for Review of Administrative Rules (JCRAR) with a copy of his petition until more than 60 days after he filed his declaratory judgment action. The trial court held that Wis. Stat. § 893.02 voided the late service on the JCRAR and deprived it of jurisdiction over the action. The court rejected the prison officials' contention that Wis. Stat. § 227.40(5), which allowed the JCRAR to become a party to the proceedings upon approval of the legislative organization committee, elevated the JCRAR to de facto status as a party defendant to the action so as to invoke the 60 day service provision of Wis. Stat. § 893.02. The court held that while the JCRAR had a right to become a party to the action, it could only do so after approval by another legislative committee and as such, it was not automatically a party by operation of law. Thus, the JCRAR was not subject to the 60 day service requirement of § 893.02 and the inmate's late service on the committee was not fatal to his action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the inmate's action and it remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1573 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Galuska v. Racine County


No. 87-0151


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


145 Wis. 2d 895; 428 N.W.2d 561; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 454



May 25, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine county: STEPHEN A. SIMANEK, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court [*10] .--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents sought review of an order of the circuit court for Racine county (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint and amended complaint in their action against defendant town, county, and fair corporation for a declaratory judgment to invalidate a county zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The residents brought an action for a declaratory judgment to invalidate a county zoning ordinance that relocated the county fair. The trial court dismissed the residents' complaints. The residents sought review of the trial court's ruling. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision, finding that the trial court did not err in treating motions to dismiss as motions for summary judgment under Wis. Stat. § 802.06(2) because the parties did not object. The court also ruled that the trial court's dispositive order did not give leave to the residents to replead and that the resident's failure to notify the attorney general pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 806.04(11) of their constitutional claim did not void the trial court's order because the trial court did not reach that claim. The court held further that the county's approval of ordinance did not violate Wis. Stat. § 59.97(5)(e)4 and that the county did not engage in spot or contract zoning. The court also found that the resident's claim under Wis. Stat. § 130.065 were properly stricken as already pending in another suit and that the respondent's claim regarding class action status was moot given the decision on the merits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that had dismissed the residents' declaratory judgment action.

State v. Smith


No. 87-2011-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


145 Wis. 2d 898; 428 N.W.2d 562; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 395



May 17, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Ashland county: THOMAS GALLAGHER, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Ashland County (Wisconsin), which entered convictions against him for three counts of first-degree sexual assault, repeater, one count of abduction, repeater, and an order denying his motion for a new trial or for a sentence modification. Defendant asserted on appeal that his arrest was illegal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his convictions, defendant argued that his arrest was illegal because the officers lacked probable cause and used the probation officer and the probation hold order as a subterfuge to arrest him. Defendant further contended that Wis. Admin. Code § HSS 328.22(1), under which the probation officer authorized his apprehension, was unconstitutional. The court rejected defendant's contentions and affirmed. Specifically, the court held that where the victim's initial description of the assailant fit defendant, the assailant told the victim he was a rapist, defendant been convicted of two prior rapes, and the vehicle tracks at defendant's parents' residence were visually similar to the tracks left at the scene of the assault, there was probable cause for his arrest. Furthermore, the court found that because § HSS 328.22(1) was constitutional and the probation officer had a reasonable basis to believe that defendant had engaged in assaultive conduct, the trial court's finding of a bona fide probation hold request was not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and order.

 

1575 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Bartlett v. Winnebago County


No. 87-1543


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


145 Wis. 2d 897; 428 N.W.2d 562; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 451



May 10, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Winnebago county: ROBERT HAWLEY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which granted the motion for summary judgment that respondent Winnebago County (Wisconsin) filed in the action in which the owners challenged the validity of the county's condemnation of the owners' farm for the purpose of constructing a landfill on that site.


OVERVIEW: The owners alleged that disputed material facts existed as to if the county could have reasonably expected to achieve the stated public purpose, that the county did not negotiate in good faith toward an agreed price prior to the condemnation, and that it was not reasonably necessary to acquire a part of the farm as a source of covering soil and as an environmental buffer zone. The court affirmed the grant of summary grant, concluding that that county made a prima facie case for condemnation. The court reasoned that the funds that were needed to buy the farm would have been available, that the county would have been able to resolve the environmental and the town's issues, and that the farm was the only available site for the needed landfill. The court also held that the licensing process did not present a material dispute as to if the taking is for a public use and that obtaining a valid appraisal and ceasing the efforts to buy the farm on learning that the owners would not sell for any price that the county was willing to pay showed good faith. The court further determined that the need for the buffer and for the source of topsoil was shown to be reasonable necessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the county's summary judgment motion in the action in which the owners challenged the validity of the condemnation of the owners' farm.

 

1576 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


County of La Crosse v. Miller


No. 88-0173


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


145 Wis. 2d 899; 428 N.W.2d 563; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 391



May 5, 1988, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse county: MICHAEL J. MULROY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI) and that denied her request for a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court ruled that no excusable neglect was shown as to not timely requesting a jury trial. The judgment was affirmed. The court concluded that the circuit court correctly advised every defendant who was charged with a civil forfeiture and who timely arrived at the initial appearance hearing that, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 345.43(1), the right to a jury trial was waived if they did not demand one and pay the required fees within 10 days of pleading not guilty. The court also held that defendant did not hear that admonition because she was late for the hearing because she chose to stay at school and to pick her mother up prior to attending the hearing of which defendant had full knowledge. Noting that defendant had ample notice of the hearing date and had shown a lackadaisical attitude toward meeting the deadlines in the proceedings, the court further determined that the circuit court validly ruled that her tardiness waived her right to be informed of the requirements of § 345.43(1). The court also found that there was no duty to note the comings and the goings of the persons in the courtroom in order to assure that those who were late did not miss anything.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for OWI and the denial of her request for a jury trial.

 

1577 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wilson


No. 87-0761-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


145 Wis. 2d 143; 426 N.W.2d 56; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 429


February 18, 1988, Argued  
May 4, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha county: Jerold W. Breitenbach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order reversed and cause remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of second-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The victim who was the stepson of defendant remained home from school one day. Defendant, although working on the family car, periodically checked on the child. Defendant fed the child a lunch of chicken soup. The mother returned home to find the child very ill. It was determined that the child was suffering from a ruptured hollow viscus in the abdomen, with fluid peritonitis present. During surgery the doctors found a laceration in the child's stomach. Although the laceration was sutured, the child died the following morning. It was determined that the stomach laceration was due to a blunt force of trauma. It was determined that the injury was inflicted upon the child and that his death was not accidental. Defendant was convicted of second-degree murder. On review, defendant's major assertion was that the lesser-included offense of reckless homicide should have been given. The court reversed and remanded. The court held that because there was a void in the evidence concerning defendant's specific conduct it had to conclude that viewing the evidence in light most favorable to defendant that submission of the lesser included offense of reckless homicide was required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for second-degree murder and remanded for a new trial.

 

1578 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Herndon


No. 87-0357-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


145 Wis. 2d 91; 426 N.W.2d 347; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 461


October 6, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
May 3, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Gary A. Gerlach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied defendant's right to cross-examine juvenile complaining witness about prior arrests for prostitution, and which convicted defendant of third-degree sexual assault, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 940.225(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the juvenile propositioned him. The juvenile accused defendant of rape. At the trial, defendant was denied the right to cross-examine the juvenile on her prior arrests for prostitution, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 972.11(2), the rape shield law. The trial court convicted defendant of third-degree sexual assault pursuant to § 940.225(3) and sentenced defendant to four years incarceration to be served consecutively with the term he was serving as result of parole revocation. On defendant's appeal, the court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the case to the trial court with directions. The court determined that U.S. Const. amend. VI and Wis. Const. art. I, § 7 guarantee a defendant the right to confront adverse witnesses, that Wis. Stat. 972.11(2) provided only limited exceptions to the rape shield law, that the absolution nature of the rape shield law violated defendant's right to confrontation because it precluded the balancing test mandated in Davis v. Alaska, 415 U.S. 308 (1974), and that, therefore, § 972.11(2)(c), which precluded admission or reference to evidence unless expressly permitted under other sections, was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which had denied defendant's right to cross-examine juvenile complaining witness and had convicted defendant of sexual assault. The court ruled that the rape shield law unconstitutionally denied defendant his right to confrontation. The court remanded the action to the trial court with directions for a new trial.

 

1579 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Acquisition of Property of Sternberg


Nos. 87-1311, 87-1312


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


144 Wis. 2d 950; 425 N.W.2d 39; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 305



April 26, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from orders of the circuit court for Marathon county: ANN WALSH BRADLEY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review from the orders of the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin), which rejected the property owners' constitutional challenge to the appeal procedure in respondent county's condemnation proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The county condemned the property owners' land to construct a county jail. The trial court dismissed their appeals because they were not filed within 60 days of the taking award. The property owners argued that Wis. Stat. §§ 32.05, 32.06 denied them equal protection because the statutes provided a 60-day appeal deadline for the condemnation of their properties, while other kinds of condemnations had a two-year deadline. The court affirmed. As long as the statutes' classification had a reasonable basis, they did not deny equal protection of the laws. The two condemnation procedures covered two distinct classes of condemnation: transportation and all others. The procedural differences between the statutes were rational, and thus constitutional. The legislature could rationally conclude that transportation condemnation were best served by an early transfer of title, as the number of claimants and real estate parcels processed justified a more flexible procedure. The legislature could also rationally conclude that nontransportation condemnations were better served by a later transfer of title given the small number of claimants and parcels, which allowed a more restricted procedure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders.

 

1580 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


O'Donnell v. Reivitz


No. 87-0092


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


144 Wis. 2d 717; 424 N.W.2d 733; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 310


February 18, 1988, Submitted on briefs  
April 14, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: P. Charles Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the taxpayers' complaint against respondents, Department of Health and Social Services, the department's secretary, and the state treasurer, for a declaration that Wis. Stat. § 46.26(4)(a), part of the Youth Aids statute, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issues were: (1) Whether the taxpayers had standing to attack § 46.26(4)(a); (2) Whether the statute was a tax provision, and if so, whether it violated the requirement in Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 1, that the rule of taxation was required to be uniform. The court found that the taxpayers had a direct and personal pecuniary interest in the litigation and thus had standing the attack the constitutionality of § 46.26(4)(a). The court disagreed with the taxpayers' contention that the effect of § 46026(4)(a) was the imposition of a tax in their county and was therefore a taxing statute. The court reasoned that the fact that § 46.26 provided funds or grants-in-aid to assist counties and to pay all or part of the cost of services the state provided did not detract from the counties' responsibilities. The court held that § 46.26(4)(a) was not a tax statute. The court affirmed the trial court judgment and did not reach the uniformity issue because the statute was not shown to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which dismissed the taxpayers' complaint.

 

1581 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Koehler


No. 87-1125-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


144 Wis. 2d 950; 425 N.W.2d 39; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 343



April 13, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Sheboygan county: JOHN G. BUCHEN, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which upheld a jury verdict that found defendant guilty of one count of homicide by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.09(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: After defendant's conviction of homicide by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle, defendant sought review contending that the general drunk driving statute, Wis. Stat. § 940.09(1)(a), was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad because it did not give adequate notice of the proscribed conduct. The statute proscribed driving under the influence of an intoxicant to a degree which rendered a person incapable of safely driving. Defendant also alleged that his trial counsel was ineffective because he consented to a six-person jury, rather than a twelve-person jury, failed to point out defendant's weight when a hypothetical used a person 20 pounds lighter, and failed to present an independent expert toxicologist to refute the testimony of the State's medical expert. The court affirmed the conviction holding that the phrase, "under the influence of an intoxicant," was not vague or unconstitutionally overbroad and that people intuitively knew when they were overdrinking. Defendant was not prejudiced by the size of the jury or the failure to challenge the State's reliable intoxication testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for homicide by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle.

 

1582 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. KEEFE


No. 87-0831-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


143 Wis. 2d 901; 423 N.W.2d 882; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 253



March 23, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23 (3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MICHAEL J. BARRON, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, that convicted her of homicide by intoxicated use of a vehicle under Wis. Stat. § 940.09(1)(a), (b). Among other points of error, defendant argued that § 940.09 was unconstitutional, that the State inordinately delayed prosecution, that a blood alcohol test was inadmissible, and that the accident would have occurred even if she had not been intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was crossing an intersection when a motorcycle struck the car. The motorcyclist died. Defendant's blood alcohol content was .198 percent. Charges were not filed because the prosecutor mistakenly thought he had to prove that her intoxication caused the death. A supreme court decision clarified that a death and an accused's intoxication did not have to be causally linked. Defendant was charged under § 940.09(1)(a). The first blood test was suppressed, but a second blood sample taken at the hospital showed a blood alcohol content of .251 percent. The complaint was amended to include a charge under § 940.09(1)(b). Defendant's claim that she was prejudiced by the delay in prosecution was rejected. There was no proof that the delay was improperly motivated. She was not prejudiced by admission of the second blood test and the amended information. The test was done for valid, medical purposes. The State properly notified her of the blood test as soon as it was discovered, which was eight months before trial. The evidence supported the jury's conclusion that defendant was not entitled to the affirmative defense under Wis. Stat. § 940.09(2). Section 940.09 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment that convicted defendant of homicide by intoxicated use of a vehicle was affirmed.

 

1583 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


GARTHOFF v. VERNON CTY. ZONING BD. OF ADJUSTMENT


No. 87-1689


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


143 Wis. 2d 904; 423 N.W.2d 884; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 290



March 17, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23 (3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Vernon county: JAMES W. RICE, Judge. Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. No costs to either party.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Vernon County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their petition for a writ of certiorari to review a decision issued by respondent Vernon County Board of Adjustments and affirmed the Board's decision.


OVERVIEW: The landowners purchased the property in July 1984 and placed two mobile homes on it. The previous owners had a mobile home until August 1983 that was a nonconforming use. The landowners asserted that their homes were a continuation of an existing use or, alternatively, requested a variance. The Board denied the request and concluded that the new homes were not a nonconforming use. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. Although the trial court had a summary of the Board's hearing to review rather than a verbatim transcript, the landowners provided no authority for the proposition that the Board was required to prepare a hearing transcript. Because the Board did not respond to the landowners' contention that the trial court erred in ordering them to remove the homes, the court remanded with directions to delete that language. However, the court held that the landowners did not meet their burden of showing that the value of the new homes did not exceed 50 percent of the assessed value of the previous owners' home. Thus, the landowners could not complain that the Board failed to make proper findings regarding the continuation of a prior nonconforming use.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the part of the decision that ordered the landowners to remove their mobile homes. Otherwise, the court affirmed.

 

1584 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. DICKEL


No. 87-0871-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


143 Wis. 2d 901; 423 N.W.2d 882; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 190



March 8, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23 (3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Dunn county: ROBERT F. PFIFFNER, Reserve Judge, presiding. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dunn County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver in violation of Wis. Stat. § 161.14(4)(t) and sentenced him to three years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because the charging documents failed to allege an existing offense. The court affirmed the judgment, finding that because the documents charged a crime, defendant had to show actual prejudice in order to be entitled to any relief. Defendant made no such showing and, in view of an amended information that charged a violation of § 161.14(4)(t), the court found none. Defendant also argued that defects in the complaint deprived the trial court of personal jurisdiction. The court concluded that defendant waived his objections to the trial court's personal jurisdiction when he entered an Alford plea. Defendant further contended that a court commissioner was without authority to issue search warrants because he had not filed an oath of office. The court found that the acts of a "de facto" officer were valid as to the public and third parties. Finally, defendant argued that the trial court abused its discretion by sentencing him to prison for three years. The court found that the trial court properly concluded that the alternative of probation would have unduly deprecated the seriousness of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1585 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. PHILLIPPI


No. 87-1160-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


143 Wis. 2d 902; 423 N.W.2d 883; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 270



March 1, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23 (3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Shawano county: THOMAS GROVER, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Shawano County (Wisconsin) of uttering a forgery, Wis. Stat. § 943.38(2). Postconviction relief was denied. On appeal, the issues included whether he was illegally arrested and denied both effective assistance of counsel and a speedy trial and whether the forgery penalty provision violated equal protection of the laws because the maximum for similar crimes was substantially less.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that what defendant claimed was an illegal arrest was a reasonable Terry stop. Defendant argued that a seven-month failure to file a detainer caused a delay in bringing him to trial such that his constitutional right to a speedy trial was denied. On appeal, after reviewing the applicable test and Wis. Stat. § 976.05, which gave effect to the Interstate Agreement on Detainers Act, the court held that the delay was hardly inexcusable in light of the established record. As to his claim that he was illegally arrested, after reviewing the facts and Wis. Stat. § 968.24, which codified the Terry standard for temporary detention, the court held that a police officer had sufficient reasonable suspicion to make an investigative stop. Because the investigative stop was reasonable, the court did not have to address defendant's claim that trial counsel's failure to challenge it was ineffective assistance of counsel. Contrary to defendant's claim, a store manager's testimony was not hearsay because he testified to his present sense impression, Wis. Stat. § 908.03(1), as to defendant's presentation of a forged check for payment. Wis. Stat. § 943.38 was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the order denying postconviction relief.

State v. Mislivecek


No. 87-1661


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


143 Wis. 2d 896; 422 N.W.2d 463; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 150



February 25, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23 (3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: GEORGE A. W. NORTHRUP, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which revoked his driving privileges based on his failure to submit to a chemical test for intoxication under Wis. Stat. § 343.305(3)(b).


OVERVIEW: The trial court revoked the driver's driving privileges based on his failure to submit to a chemical test for intoxication under Wis. Stat. § 343.305(3)(b). The trial court's judgment was affirmed on appeal. The court found that the arresting officer had not unlawfully stopped the driver's pickup truck. The court found that the officer had probable cause to stop the driver's vehicle because the vehicle, which was travelling at erratic fluctuating speeds, crossed a centerline and turned without signaling. The court found that the stop was constitutional because the officer had specific and articulable facts on which to reasonably believe that the driver had violated the traffic laws. Moreover, judicial precedent had determined § 343.305(3)(b)5 to be constitutional. Finally, the court found that the driver's demand for a jury trial had been properly denied because there was no right to a jury trial in a refusal hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1587 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Peck


Nos. 87-0816-CR, 87-0283-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


143 Wis. 2d 624; 422 N.W.2d 160; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 80


December 7, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
February 25, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not disposed of at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Vernon county: James W. Rice, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Vernon County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to suppress marijuana seized from fields near his house, and which convicted him of manufacturing controlled substances in violation of Wis. Stat. § 161.41(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: After law enforcement officials used binoculars to observe defendant growing marijuana on his property, ostensibly for use in his capacity as priest of a cult, defendant was arrested and charged with manufacturing controlled substances in violation of § 161.41(1)(b). The trial court denied his motion to suppress evidence seized from his property, and defendant was convicted. He appealed, and the court affirmed, holding that defendant's right to free exercise of religion under U.S. Const. I was not violated because the State had an overriding interest in regulating controlled substances. Although some of the marijuana was grown in the curtilage near defendant's home, the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress because he could not have had a reasonable expectation of privacy concerning property that was in plain view. Defendant was unable to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that § 161.41(1)(b) violated equal protection principles because although certain churches were able to use controlled substances in connection with their services, defendant's church lacked the unique cultural and historic attributes of those churches.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1588 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Tomah-Mauston Broadcasting Co. v. Eklund


No. 87-1359


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


143 Wis. 2d 648; 422 N.W.2d 169; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 99


January 20, 1988, Submitted on briefs  
February 25, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Robert R. Pekowsky, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed its petition for judicial review of an order of respondent Labor and Industry Review Commission on grounds that the company did not timely serve the employee with a copy of its petition for judicial review as required by Wis. Stat. § 227.53(1)(c).


OVERVIEW: The employee filed an age discrimination complaint against the employer. When the employer sought judicial review of the Commission's initial decision, the summons and petition were served on the employee's attorney without objection. The employer served the attorney with another review proceeding after the Commission rendered an adverse decision on remand. The trial court dismissed the petition and the employer sought review. The court affirmed, finding that (1) service upon the parties as required by Wis. Stat. § 227.53(1)(c) was necessary to confer subject matter jurisdiction upon a circuit court; (2) all of the employee's and attorney's affirmative acts in acquiescing to service of process on the attorney took place in the prior proceedings that were concluded by the Commission's order; (3) a petition for review of that order under Wis. Stat. § 227.53 was the start of a special new proceeding; (4) there was no affirmative action that established special circumstances allowing the court to find that the attorney was authorized to accept service for the employee; and (5) the employee was not estopped to assert the trial court's lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court and declined to assess fees against the employer.

In Interest of S.S.K.


No. 87-1644


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


143 Wis. 2d 603; 422 N.W.2d 450; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 102


November 25, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
February 24, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from orders of the circuit court for Waukesha county: David Dancey, Reserve Judge, presiding, and Marianne Becker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which entered an order that found the mother's child to be in need of protection and services under Wis. Stat. § 48.13(2) and placed the child outside the home. Respondent county human services department had filed a petition that claimed the child was abandoned under Wis. Stat. § 48.13(2).


OVERVIEW: The county human services department filed a petition against the mother wherein the county human services department claimed that the mother had abandoned her child under Wis. Stat. § 48.13(2) and that the mother was neglecting, was refusing, or was unable to provide the necessary care for the child under Wis. Stat. § 48.13(10). The trial court entered an order that found the child to be in need of protection and services under Wis. Stat. § 48.13(2) and placed the child outside the home. On appeal, the mother requested relief from the order because of ineffective assistance of counsel. The court held that: (1) nothing in the performance of any of the mother's lawyers prevented the real controversy from being tried or resulted in a miscarriage of justice; (2) denying a lawyer's motion to withdraw and ordering the lawyer to try a case as best as possible was a viable option when a client failed to appear; (3) the term "abandonment" as it was used in Wis. Stat. § 48.13(2) was not unconstitutionally vague; and (4) when the best interests of the child came into conflict with the rights of a parent, resolution of the conflict was in favor of the child's interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Madison v. Polenska


No. 86-1858


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


143 Wis. 2d 525; 421 N.W.2d 862; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 111


November 12, 1987, Argued  
February 18, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: William Byrne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of violating Madison, Wis., General Ordinances § 12.42(1)(c)1, which adopted Wis. Stat. § 346.37(1)(c)1, after he was involved in a motor vehicle collision while driving an ambulance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was operating an ambulance on an emergency call. He was approaching an intersection with a red traffic signal and there was another car approaching the other way. He did not see the other car stop, although he expected it to do so. The ambulance struck the other car. Defendant was convicted of violating the statute requiring the vehicles facing a red signal should stop. On appeal, the court confirmed. The court found that under Wis. Stat. § 346.03, the operator of an emergency vehicle was exempted from certain traffic laws. The court concluded that this privilege was qualified by § 346.03(5), which required the operator to drive with due regard for the safety of all persons. The court reviewed the trial court's findings under a clearly erroneous standard. The court accepted the findings and found defendant had violated the ordinance. The court determined that it was for the legislature to determine the public policy implications of allowing emergency vehicle operators to have privileges other drivers did not.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Woodward Communications, Inc. v. Department of Revenue


No. 87-0195


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


143 Wis. 2d 512; 442 N.W.2d 137; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 90


December 17, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
February 18, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not disposed of at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: James C. Boll, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of the Tax Appeals Commission that affirmed the decision of respondent Department of Revenue in denying the taxpayer's petition for a redetermination of the assessment of the sales and use taxes.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Revenue had issued a decision that denied the taxpayer's petition for a redetermination of the assessment of a sales and use tax. Both the Tax Appeals Commission and the circuit court had affirmed the Department's decision. The taxpayer had filed an appeal, claiming that its printing of shoppers guides for others was not a sale of a service under Wis. Stat. § 77.52(2)(a)11 (1975, 1977). The court disagreed, and found that the printing service sale was taxable as a retail sale of providing a service of a tangible personal property under § 77.52(2)(a)11. The court came to this conclusion by virtue of the general language in the introductory paragraph to Wis. Stat. § 77.51(4), and the specific provision in Wis. Stat. § 77.51(4)(k) had included in a retail sale a transfer without a valuable consideration. Finally, the court rejected the taxpayer's constitutional challenge to § 77.54(15) because the taxpayer had not satisfied its burden in showing any constitutional deficiency. The court affirmed the circuit court's order that affirmed the denial of the request for a redetermination of the tax assessment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order that had affirmed the decisions of the Tax Appeals Commission and the Department of Revenue in denying the taxpayer's petition for a redetermination of the assessment of the sales and use taxes.

ELLICKSON v. WISCONSIN DEPT. OF HEALTH & SOC. SERVS.


No. 87-1626


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


143 Wis. 2d 896; 422 N.W.2d 463; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 149



February 11, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23 (3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse county: PETER G. PAPPAS, Judge. Reversed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Wisconsin Department of Health and Social Services sought review from the order of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which revised the Department's decision to deny petitioner claimant certain medical assistance benefits.


OVERVIEW: Claimant requested coverage for a proposed alveoloplasty, which the department denied based upon the express language of Wis. Admin. Code § HSS 107.07(4)(p). Claimant contended that there was an exception to § 107.07(4)(p) based upon medical necessity or other individual circumstances. The trial court reversed the department's determination. The court reversed the trial court's order. The court determined that neither Wis. Admin. Code §§ HSS 107.07(2)(c)2, 107.07(5) created an exception to the blanket exclusion on alveoloplasties contained in Wis. Admin. Code § 107.07(4). The reference to "other covered services" in Wis. Admin. Code § HSS 107.07(2)(c) unambiguously established proof that the provisions of Wis. Admin. Code § HSS 107.07(2)(c)2 extended only to covered services and did not set up an authorization procedure for noncovered services. With respect to Wis. Admin. Code § HSS 107.07(5), reimbursement was required only if the department requested noncovered service in order to substantiate a prior authorization request; however, the department did not request the alveoloplasty and claimant did not need to surgery to substantiate a prior authorization request.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

City of Milwaukee v. Brunner


No. 87-1766


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


143 Wis. 2d 896; 422 N.W.2d 463; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 106



February 10, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit for Milwaukee county: CHARLES B. SHUDSON, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.-- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated contrary to Milwaukee, Wis., Code of Ordinances § 101-3 (1972) (adopting Wis. Stat. §346.63(1)(a)).


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed defendant driving erratically. Approaching defendant as he exited a store, the officer noticed that he had difficulty in speaking and in finding his driver's license, his eyes were red and watery, and he was leaning against the car. After defendant failed a field sobriety test, the officer arrested him. Because defendant was unable to perform a breath test for health reasons, officers collected a urine sample. Defendant argued that his warrantless arrest pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 345.22, for violation of a municipal traffic ordinance, infringed his rights under the Fourth Amendment and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11, and that the urinalysis results should have been suppressed because he was not given the opportunity for an alternative test and because they were unreliable as a matter of law. The court affirmed the judgment. It held that the arrest was proper where there was probable cause and the offense was committed in the officer's presence; that defendant waived the evidentiary issue by failing to object to admission or to move to suppress; and that because the chemical test was specified by statute, it could not be deemed unreliable as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Overlook Farms Home Asso. v. Alternative Living Services


No. 87-1065


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


143 Wis. 2d 485; 422 N.W.2d 131; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 121


December 1, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
February 10, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Clarence R. Parrish, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a home association and related parties, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which ruled that Wis. Stat. § 46.03(22) permitted respondent, an alternative living service, to operate a group home despite a restrictive covenant in the association's subdivision.


OVERVIEW: The service purchased a home in a subdivision for the purpose of operating a group home. The home was to serve as a residence for up to eight elderly persons who needed assistance. The association filed an action seeking a permanent injunction preventing the service from operating the group home on the ground that the property was subject to a restrictive covenant. The service maintained that § 46.03(22) permitted the group home to operate despite the restrictive covenant. The trial court held that the legislature did not intend for the statute to apply retroactively but that the statute was constitutional and that the service could rightfully operate the group home. Upon review, the court affirmed but disagreed with the trial court that the statute was not intended to apply retroactively to covenants created prior to its enactment. In addressing the constitutional challenge as to the retroactive application of § 46.03(22), the court held that, although the statute substantially impaired the contractual obligations of the association, the statute was supported by strong legislative purpose and was properly tailored to fulfill that purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1595 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wolske


No. 87-0533-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


143 Wis. 2d 175; 420 N.W.2d 60; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2


October 20, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
January 20, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: Harry G. Snyder, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the following charges against defendant: causing death by operating a boat while under the influence of an intoxicant, causing death by operating a boat while having a blood alcohol concentration of .10% or more, and causing death by a high degree of negligence in operating a boat.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that a person might be charged, convicted, and punished for both homicide by intoxicated operation of a motorboat and homicide by highly negligent operation arising out of the same incident. The trial court held that even though the intoxication and negligence charges were neither multiplicious nor lesser-included offenses, multiple punishment was inappropriate. The court compared the elements of the statutes involved and found that the negligence statutes required the State to prove operation of a vehicle with a high degree of negligence, while the intoxication statutes required the State to prove operation of a vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant. The different conduct proscribed and different grounds for the negligence and intoxication statutes along with their distinct factual elements convinced the court that multiple prosecutions, convictions, and punishments were intended by the legislature. Therefore, the court reversed the dismissal of the complaint on multiplicity grounds. The court affirmed the judgment in so far as it found probable cause to support the complaint against defendant.


OUTCOME: The order that dismissed the charges against defendant was reversed and that portion of the order that found probable cause supported the State's complaint was affirmed.

Kuhnen v. Musolf


No. 86-0372


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


143 Wis. 2d 134; 420 N.W.2d 401; 1988 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4


May 6, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
January 14, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied. Petition for cross-review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: Angela Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded with directions to enter judgment consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which ruled in favor defendant Secretary of the State of Wisconsin Department of Revenue in the taxpayers' action seeking to have Wis. Stat. §§ 71.05(1)(a)5, 7 (1979-80), Wis. Stat. § 71.09(6p)(d)1 (1979-80), and Wis. Stat. § 71.53(6) (1979-80) declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers were two couples who, in each case, sold their principal residence in Wisconsin and, in employment-related moves, moved to another state where they acquired a new principal residence. They brought their action on behalf of themselves and all former residents of the state, similarly situated. In each case the Department sought to impose on them additional income taxes under the challenged statutes. Had either couple relocated in the state in an employment-related move, no additional tax would have been due. The trial court declared the statutes constitutional and the taxpayers sought review. On appeal, the court overturned the judgment as to Wis. Stat. § 71.05(1)(a)5, but upheld the judgment as to the remainder of the challenged statutes. The court ruled that because there was no substantial reason for the different treatment of nonresidents in the taxation of gain realized on the sale of their principal residences and the treatment had no substantial relation to a legitimate state objective, it declared that § 71.05(1)(a)5 violated the privileges and immunities clause. The court held that the rest of the statutes affected interstate commerce only incidentally.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment as to one of the challenged statutes and affirmed the judgment as to the rest of the statutes. The court remanded the cause with directions to enter judgment declaring that former statute was unconstitutional.

STATE v. HECHT


No. 86-2127


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


142 Wis. 2d 944; 419 N.W.2d 573; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4375



December 30, 1987, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23 (3)


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition by Denial of Review March 15, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: DANIEL R. MOESER, Judge. Reversed and cause remanded with directions.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion for unlimited access to the prison law library in a correctional institution. Defendant was imprisoned for life and was awaiting trial on six felony charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with various charges that ranged from escape through evincing a depraved mind based upon allegations regarding defendant's alleged commandeering of a pickup truck. Defendant was representing himself. Defendant alleged that he was in a program segregation unit, he was not allowed physical access to the library, that no "satellite" library was available, and the he needed direct access to certain legal books. Defendant stated the he was allowed two books per day and that this was not sufficient access. In reversing the trial court's decision and remanding the cause, the court held that defendant had a special legal need for access to legal materials. Defendant had a constitutional right to represent himself. Defendant also had a fundamental constitutional right of access to the courts. Under Wis. Admin. Code § HSS 309.27(1), special provisions had to be made to provide defendant with access to legal materials. The trial court was directed to hold an evidentiary hearing to determine whether the restrictions placed on defendant's access to legal materials and to the library satisfied Wis. Admin. Code § HSS 309.27(1).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the cause with directions.

GREAT LAKES PRODS. v. WI DEPT OF AGRIC.


No. 86-2046


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


142 Wis. 2d 944; 419 N.W.2d 573; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4435



December 30, 1987, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23 (3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: MICHAEL N. NOWAKOWSKI, Judge. Reversed and cause remanded with directions.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Wisconsin Department of Agriculture, Trade, and Consumer Protection, appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment to plaintiff manufacturer and declared Wis. Admin. Code § Ag 72.04(10) void insofar as it prohibited the sale of butyl nitrite.


OVERVIEW: The manufacture alleged that it produced room odorizers that contained butyl nitrite. It brought an action to declare Wis. Admin. Code § Ag 72.04(10) unconstitutional. The manufacturer moved for summary judgment on the ground that the Wisconsin Department of Agriculture, Trade, and Consumer Protection lacked jurisdiction to ban nitrite-based products because butyl nitrite was a drug, and Wis. Stat. § 100.37(1)(c)5 excluded drugs from the definition of "hazardous substances" that Wis. Stat. § 100.37(2)(d) permitted the Department to ban. In support of the motion, the manufacturer submitted certified copies of the rulemaking record, including the Department's findings of fact and statement of need for the rule. The court held that the manufacturer's evidentiary materials failed to show that the Department had found that butyl nitrite was a drug, and that nothing in the materials indicated whether that was a contested issue in the rulemaking proceeding. The court rejected the manufacturer's argument that a drug was anything intended to be inhaled.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case with directions to dismiss the motion for summary judgment.

 

1599 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Montgomery Ward & Co. v. Department of Revenue


No. 87-0544


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


142 Wis. 2d 772; 419 N.W.2d 348; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4391


December 7, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
December 30, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: Susan Steingass, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department store challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that affirmed a decision and an order of respondent, the Wisconsin Tax Appeals Commission, that affirmed the Department of Revenue's deficiency assessment against the department store for sales and use tax and the imposition of 12 percent interest on the deficiencies.


OVERVIEW: Prior to July 31, 1981, the interest penalty on sales and use tax deficiencies was nine percent; effective August 1, the rate was 12 percent. In 1982, the Department of Revenue issued a deficiency assessment against the department store and charged interest on the deficiencies at the rate of 12 percent. The department store challenged the assessment, and after the tax appeals commission affirmed, the department store sought judicial review. The circuit court affirmed, and the department store appealed. In affirming, the court concluded that the plain language of Wis. Stat. § 2203(45)(g) (1981) indicated that the new interest rate applied to all determinations made on or after August 1, 1981, regardless of the taxable periods to which those determinations might pertain. Because the deficiency assessments were made after July 31, 1981, the 12 percent interest rate was applicable. Further, the court rejected the department store's equal protection argument. The fact that some taxpayers might be assessed interest at different rates dependent upon when the deficiency was determined and when the assessment was made did not establish the unconstitutionality of the law.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

 

1600 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Galuska v. Kornwolf


No. 87-0242


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


142 Wis. 2d 733; 419 N.W.2d 307; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4349


October 20, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
December 23, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Racine county: Stephen A. Simanek, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which held that Wis. Stat. § 130.065 was unconstitutional and that mandamus did not lie to compel defendants, a county clerk and a sheriff, to enforce the statute against transient merchants.


OVERVIEW: The residents of a subdivision near a fair filed a mandamus action to compel the county clerk to establish procedures for the issuance of licenses for transient merchants under Wis. Stat. § 130.065 and to compel the county sheriff to enforce the statute. The trial court held that the statute violated the Commerce, Equal Protection, and Due Process Clauses of the United States Constitution. On appeal, the court concurred that a writ of mandamus did not lie, but upon different grounds than those relied upon by the trial court. The court determined that mandamus did not lie against the county clerk because the clerk had no affirmative duty under § 103.065(2)-(6) to take any action until a merchant requested a license. Likewise, the court held that mandamus was not available to compel the sheriff to act because the sheriff's duty asserted by the residents was discretionary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying a writ of mandamus to the residents to compel enforcement of the statute regulating sales by transient merchants.
